Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
The Four Ways to Deflect Naqd Objections in Qiyas
Explains four methods to counter objections against a qiyas-based 'illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply each of the four Hanafi methods for deflecting a naqd objection against a qiyas-based 'illah.

Core Idea
A valid 'illah can be defended against counterexamples by showing absence of its description, meaning, ruling, or purpose.

One of the most powerful critiques of qiyas is the objection (naqd) that a proposed 'illah is present in a case where the ruling is absent. The Hanafi school, through its sophisticated theory of ta'lil, developed four systematic ways to deflect such objections. This lesson unpacks those four methods using the classical example of whether impure bodily excretions other than urine/stool constitute hadath. The discussion reveals the depth of Hanafi usul reasoning and the use of istihsan to preserve the 'illah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 'illah under attack
Recognize the Hanafi claim: any impure substance exiting the body is hadath like urine, based on Quran 5:6 and qiyas. Understand the Shafi'i objections: (1) non-flowing excretion and (2) flowing wound blood.
The 'illah is 'impure exit from the body'.
2
Apply the first two methods: wasf and ma'na thabit bi al-wasf
For the non-flowing objection, show that the description (wasf) of 'exiting' is absent—what appears under skin is not actually exiting. Then argue that the meaning (ma'na) established by that description—the obligation to wash the entire body—is also absent, so the cause is not present.
First method: negate the wasf. Second: negate the ma'na.
3
Apply the third method: al-hukm
For the flowing wound objection, do not concede that the ruling is absent. Instead, argue that the hadath ruling is present but delayed due to necessity (istihsan) until after the time of wudu exits. The ruling is not absent; it is simply postponed.
Third method: show the ruling exists in another context.
4
Apply the fourth method: al-gharad
Explain that the purpose (gharad) of the 'illah—to equate blood with urine—is fulfilled because both become excused (ma'fu) when continuous. Thus the objection does not undermine the analogy.
Fourth method: show the purpose is achieved even in the counterexample.

باب القياس
العلل والممانعة والمناقضة كما نقول في الخارج من غير السبيلين: إنه نجس خارج من بدن الإنسان، فكان حدثاً كالبول، فيورد عليه ما إذا لم يسل، فندفعه أولاً بالوصف وهو أنه ليس بخارج؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة رطوبة وفي كل عرق دماً، فإذا زال الجلد كان ظاهراً أي فارق مكانه صار الدم ونحوه لا خارجاً ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف دلالةً، وهو وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع للتطهير فيه صار الوصف حجةً من حيث أن وجوب التطهير في البدن باعتبار هو الخارج النجس عليه ما يكون منه لا يحتمل الوصف بالتجزي، وهناك لم يجب غسل ذلك الموضع، فانعدم في غير المسائل الحكم لعدم العلة. وهو عن بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف ثم بالحكم ثم بالغرض والتفصيل يأتي انتظره. فبعض النقوض يدفع بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف، وبعضه بغيره من الأقسام الأربعة الخارج من غير السبيلين إلخ فالخارج النجس علة للحدث، وقد ثبت تأثيره مرةً في السبيلين بقوله تعالى: أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ . عليه: أي على تعليلنا هذا بالنقض من قبل الشافعي له. إذا لم يسل : أي لم يتجاوز المخرج فإنه نجس خارج وليس بحدث، فقد تخلف الحكم الحدث هذه العلة وهي الخارج؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة رطوبة وفي كل عرق دماً. ظاهراً لا خارجاً فالحاصل أن الوصف الذي هو علة للحدث ليس بموجود في مادة التخلّف، فإن العلة هي الخارج النجس، وما لم يسل ليس بخارج بل هو باد. ثم بالمعنى الثابت إلخ أي ثم ندفعه ثانياً بعدم المعنى الثابت بالوصف الذي كان ثبوته بالوصف بالدلالة، وبسبب هذا المعنى كان ذلك الوصف علة للحكم، فإذا لم يوجد فيه ذلك المعنى لم يكن علة، فإذا لم يوجد العلة لم يتخلّف الحكم كما تقول في ذلك المثال لو سلّم أن وصف الخروج موجود لكنه لم يوجد فيه المعنى الذي كان بسبه علة. وهو وجوب إلخ: لأنه يزيل بخروج النجس الطهارة الحاصلة للبدن ،كله، فيجب أولاً غسل ذلك الموضع من النجاسة ثم غسل البدن كله، ولكن لما كان فيه حرج عظيم اقتصر على الأعضاء الأربعة دفعاً للحرج فيه: أي بسبب وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع. ما يكون منه أي ما يخرج منه، لا ما يكون من خارج، فإن النجاسة الخارجية يوجب غسل ذلك الموضع فقط. لا يحتمل إلخ: فلما وجب غسل ذلك الموضع وجب غسل كل البدن لا محالة لعدم العلة: فكأنه لم يوجد الخروج لعدم المعنى المذكور، فلم يوجد الحكم وهو الحدث، لا أن العلة موجود والحكم متخلف كما قال الخصم.
ويورد عليه صاحب الجرح السائل فندفعه بالحكم ببيان أنه حدث موجب للطهارة بعد خروج الوقت، وبالغرض؛ فإن غرضنا التسوية بين الدم والبول، وذلك حدث، من هذا التعليل فإذا لزم صار عفوا لقيام الوقت فكذلك ههنا. في صورة سلس البول ويورد عليه إلخ عطف على قوله : فيورد عليه ما إذا لم يسل، والحاصل يورد علينا من جانب الشافعي ليه في المثال المذكور نقصان، الأول ما دفعناه بطريقين، والثاني هو صاحب الجرح السائل، فإن ما يخرج من جرحه نجس خارج وليس بحدث ناقض للوضوء ما دام الوقت موجوداً. فندفعه إلخ: أي ندفع بطريقين، الأول بوجود الحكم وعدم تخلّفه بأن نقول: الحكم المطلوب ليس بمتخلف عن العلة، وهذا الطريق قسم ثالث والقسمان الأولان مرّ ذكرهما، والرابع سيجيء ببيان أنه إلخ: يعني لانسلّم أن ما يخرج مثل جرح السائل ليس بحدث بل هو حدث، ولكن تأخر حكمه للضرورة إلى ما بعد خروج الوقت، ولهذا يلزم الوضوء بذلك الحدث بعد خروج الوقت. وبالغرض: عطف على قوله بالحكم، أي ندفعه ثانياً بوجود الغرض من العلة بأن نقول: فإن غرضنا إلخ. التسوية إلخ : وإلحاق الفرع بالأصل وذلك حاصل، وإليه أشار بقوله : وذلك البول الذي جعلناه أصلا. ههنا يعني الدم كان حدثاً، فإذا لزم صار عفواً، فحصل التساوي بين البول المقيس عليه والدم وما يخرج من بدن الإنسان، حيث يصير بسبب الدوام عفواً كالبول، وهذا قسم رابع، فتم أقسام دفع النقض. ولما فرغ من دفع النقض شرع في المعارضة الواردة على العلة المؤثّرة.
Chapter of Analogy. The effective causes, opposition, and invalidation: Just as we say concerning what exits from other than the two passages: it is impure exiting from the human body, so it is an invalidator (hadath) like urine. Then an objection is raised against it: what if it does not flow? We deflect it first by the description: it is not exiting; because under every skin there is moisture, and in every vein there is blood. When the skin is removed, it becomes apparent — meaning it left its place, the blood and the like become apparent, not exiting. Then by the meaning established by the description as an indication, which is the obligation to wash that spot for purification; thereby the description becomes a proof in that the obligation of purification in the body is due to the impure exiting from it; that which comes from it does not admit of the description of partiality, and there the washing of that spot was not obligatory. So in other cases the ruling is absent due to the absence of the cause. And it is about the meaning established by the description, then by the ruling, then by the purpose; the detail will come later. So some objections are deflected by the meaning established by the description, and some by others of the four categories. Exiting from other than the two passages etc. So the impure exiting is the cause for hadath, and its effect has been established once in the two passages by His statement: 'Or one of you comes from the toilet.' Against it: i.e., against our reasoning with an objection from al-Shafi'i. When it does not flow: i.e., does not go beyond the exit; for it is impure exiting but not hadath; so the ruling of hadath has been absent from this cause, namely the exiting; because under every skin there is moisture, and in every vein there is blood. Apparent, not exiting. So the conclusion: the description which is the cause for hadath is not present in the instance of absence. For the cause is the impure exiting, and what does not flow is not exiting but is apparent. Then by the meaning etc.: i.e., we deflect it secondly by the absence of the meaning established by the description, whose establishment was by the description as an indication, and because of this meaning that description was a cause for the ruling. When that meaning is not present in it, it is not a cause. When the cause is not present, the ruling is not absent — as you say in that example: even if we concede that the description of exiting exists, but the meaning due to which it was a cause is not present in it. And it is the obligation etc.: because by the exiting of impurity, the purity obtained for the entire body is removed; so it is first obligatory to wash that spot from impurity, then to wash the entire body. However, because there was great hardship, it was limited to the four limbs to remove hardship. In it: i.e., due to the obligation of washing that spot. 'What comes from it': i.e., what exits from it, not what comes from outside. For external impurity obligates washing only that spot. 'Does not admit' etc.: So when washing that spot was obligatory, washing the entire body became inevitable. Due to the absence of the cause: it is as if the exiting did not occur due to the absence of the mentioned meaning; so the ruling, i.e., hadath, did not occur; not that the cause exists and the ruling is absent as the opponent claimed. And there is raised against it the case of a flowing wound; we deflect it by the ruling by stating that it is a hadath that necessitates purification after the time exits, and by the purpose; for our purpose is equality between blood and urine; that is hadath from this reasoning. So if it becomes continuous, it becomes excused due to the time, and similarly here. In the case of urinary incontinence. And there is raised against it as a conjunction to his statement: 'there is raised against it what if it does not flow.' The summary: there are raised against us from al-Shafi'i in that example two objections: the first we deflected by two ways; the second is the case of a flowing wound, for what exits from his wound is impure exiting but is not a hadath that breaks wudu as long as time exists. We deflect it: i.e., we deflect by two ways. First, by the existence of the ruling and its not being absent: we say that the required ruling is not absent from the cause. This way is the third division, and the first two divisions were mentioned earlier, and the fourth will come by stating that it is hadath: i.e., we do not concede that what exits like the wound of a flowing person is not hadath; rather it is hadath, but its ruling is delayed due to necessity until after the exit of time, and for this reason wudu becomes obligatory by that hadath after the exit of time. And by the purpose: conjunction to his statement 'by the ruling', i.e., we deflect it secondly by the existence of the purpose of the cause by saying our purpose etc. The equality etc.: i.e., equating the branch with the root, and that is achieved; and towards it he pointed with his statement: 'and that urine which we made as the root.' Here: i.e., blood was hadath; if it becomes continuous, it becomes excused. So equality is achieved between urine as the analogand and blood and what exits from the human body, when due to continuity it becomes excused like urine. This is the fourth division. Thus the categories of deflecting objections are completed. And when he finished deflecting objections, he began to discuss the counterargument against the effective cause.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul discussion on how to defend a qiyas-based 'illah (effective cause) against two objections raised by the Shafi'i school. The topic is whether excretion from other than the two passages (urethra and anus) is a hadath (ritual impurity) like urine. The Hanafis argue it is, using qiyas with urine. The first objection: what if the excretion does not flow? The Hanafi responds that the description 'exiting' is absent; what appears under the skin is not technically 'exiting', so the cause is missing. The second objection: a flowing wound (jarh sa'il) — the wound's blood is impure but not a hadath. The Hanafi counters using two methods: (a) by the ruling: the hadath ruling is actually present but delayed until after the time exit due to excused continuity (like istihsan); (b) by the purpose: the goal of equating blood with urine is achieved because both become excused when continuous. The text systematically presents four ways to deflect objections: by the description (wasf), by the meaning established by description (ma'na thabit bi al-wasf), by the ruling (hukm), and by the purpose (gharad). The author follows the order from the matn, explaining how each method works in the example. This is a classic Hanafi position that uses istihsan (juristic preference) to maintain the 'illah while accommodating cases of hardship, such as urinary incontinence or constant wound flow.

Key Terms
النقض (al-naqd): An objection to a qiyas-based 'illah by presenting a case where the 'illah is present but the ruling is absent (counterexample)
المعنى الثابت بالوصف (al-ma'na al-thabit bi al-wasf): A meaning or underlying rationale that is established by the description (wasf) and makes that description a valid cause for the ruling
الغرض (al-gharad): The purpose or objective behind the 'illah, used in deflection to show that the intent of the analogy is fulfilled even in the counterexample

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four ways to deflect a naqd objection against an 'illah in qiyas?
A) By the description (wasf)
B) By the meaning established by the description (ma'na thabit bi al-wasf)
C) By the ruling (hukm)
D) By the textual proof (nass)

Key Takeaway
The four methods of deflecting naqd—by description, meaning, ruling, and purpose—allow Hanafi usulis to defend systematic 'illal against counterexamples without abandoning their principles.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Defending an Illah from Naqd: The Wound Case
Explaining how to refute a contradiction in qiyas with an example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of defending against the objection of naqḍ in qiyas using the oozing wound example, and apply the two refutation strategies: by affirming the ruling and by affirming the purpose of the cause.

Core Idea
The effect of an illah can be temporarily suspended due to necessity without invalidating the causal link.

In Hanafi usul, a common objection against an 'illah in qiyas is naqḍ (contradiction): the 'illah is claimed to produce no ruling in a relevant case. This passage addresses such an objection concerning a person with a continuously oozing wound, and shows two ways to refute it. Understanding these methods deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists defend analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection (Naqḍ)
Recognize the Shafi'i objection: the oozing from a wound is impure (najis) but not a hadath (ritual impurity), so it does not nullify wudu. This would contradict the Hanafi claim that blood is a hadath analogous to urine.
The objection targets the 'illah of 'being a hadath'.
2
First Refutation: By Affirming the Ruling
The Hanafi response does not deny the ruling (nullification) but delays its effect. The oozing is a hadath, but its nullifying effect is postponed until after the prayer time due to necessity (continuity). This shows the ruling exists, just temporarily suspended.
Analogous to urinary incontinence (sals al-bawl): a continuous hadath is excused.
3
Second Refutation: By Affirming the Purpose
The purpose of the 'illah is to equate blood with urine as hadath that becomes excused when continuous. Even if the immediate effect is delayed, the equality (taswiyah) between the original case (urine) and the branch (blood) is achieved.
This highlights the maqsad (objective) of the 'illah beyond its literal effect.
4
Synthesize the Divisions of Refutation
The text mentions four ways to repel naqḍ. The first two were discussed earlier; the third is the 'by ruling' method, and the fourth is the 'by purpose' method. Together, they form a complete defense of the 'illah.
Understanding these divisions helps you systematically respond to naqḍ objections.
5
Apply to a Parallel Scenario
Use the same reasoning for any continuous impurity (e.g., blood from a wound or urine drip). The key is that continuity (damān) justifies temporary suspension of the effect, not denial of the cause.
This method preserves the integrity of qiyas while accommodating practical necessities.

Source Text

باب القياس
العلل والمماتعة والمناقضة
ويورد عليه صاحب الجرح السائل فندفعه بالحكم ببيان أنه حدث موجب للطهارة بعد خروج الوقت، وبالغرض؛ فإن غرضنا التسوية بين الدم والبول، وذلك حدث، من هذا التعليل
فإذا لزم صار عفوا لقيام الوقت فكذلك ههنا.
في صورة سلس البول
ويورد عليه إلخ عطف على قوله : فيورد" عليه ما إذا لم يسل، والحاصل يورد علينا من جانب الشافعي ليه في المثال المذكور نقصان، الأول ما دفعناه بطريقين، والثاني هو صاحب الجرح السائل، فإن ما يخرج من جرحه نجس خارج وليس بحدث ناقض للوضوء ما دام الوقت موجوداً.
فندفعه إلخ: أي ندفع بطريقين، الأول بوجود الحكم وعدم تخلّفه بأن نقول: الحكم المطلوب ليس بمتخلف عن العلة، وهذا الطريق قسم ثالث والقسمان الأولان مرّ ذكرهما، والرابع سيجيء ببيان أنه إلخ: يعني لانسلّم أن ما يخرج مثل جرح السائل ليس بحدث بل هو حدث، ولكن تأخر حكمه للضرورة إلى ما بعد خروج الوقت، ولهذا يلزم الوضوء بذلك الحدث بعد خروج الوقت.
وبالغرض: عطف على قوله بالحكم، أي ندفعه ثانياً بوجود الغرض من العلة بأن نقول: فإن غرضنا إلخ.
التسوية إلخ : وإلحاق الفرع بالأصل وذلك حاصل، وإليه أشار بقوله : وذلك البول الذي جعلناه أصلا. ههنا يعني الدم كان حدثاً، فإذا لزم صار عفواً، فحصل التساوي بين البول المقيس عليه والدم وما يخرج من بدن الإنسان، حيث يصير بسبب الدوام عفواً كالبول، وهذا قسم رابع، فتم أقسام دفع النقض. ولما فرغ من دفع النقض شرع في المعارضة الواردة على العلة المؤثّرة.
Chapter of Qiyas. The causes, prevention, and contradiction. And it is objected to him by the owner of the wound that oozes, so we refute it by the ruling by stating that it is an event requiring purification after the time exits, and by the purpose; for our purpose is equality between blood and urine, and that is an event, from this reasoning. So when it occurs it becomes excused due to the presence of time, similarly here. In the case of urinary incontinence. 'And it is objected to him' etc. is attached to his statement 'he objects' regarding when it does not flow, and the outcome: there is objected to us from the side of al-Shafi'i regarding the mentioned example two deficiencies; the first we refuted in two ways, and the second is the owner of the wound that oozes, for what exits from his wound is impure external matter and is not a hadath that nullifies wudu as long as time exists. 'So we refute it' etc.: i.e., we refute in two ways: first by the existence of the ruling and its non-delay by saying: the required ruling is not delayed from the cause, and this way is a third division, and the first two divisions have been mentioned, and the fourth will come. By stating that it is etc.: meaning that we do not concede that what exits like the wound of the oozer is not a hadath; rather it is a hadath, but its ruling is postponed due to necessity until after the time exits, and for this wudu is required due to that hadath after the time exits. 'And by the purpose': attached to his statement 'by the ruling', i.e., we refute it secondly by the existence of the purpose of the cause by saying: our purpose is etc. 'Equality' etc.: and attaching the branch to the origin, that is achieved, and to that he alluded by his statement: 'and that urine which we made the origin.' Here he means blood was a hadath, so when it occurs it becomes excused, so equality occurs between the urine analogized upon and the blood and what exits from the human body, where it becomes due to continuity excused like urine, and this is a fourth division, so the divisions of repelling contradiction are complete. When he finished from repelling contradiction, he began on the counter-argument (mu‘āraḍah) directed at the effective cause.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage explains how to defend an 'illah (cause) from the objection of naqḍ (contradiction) in qiyas. The author first presents the objection: a person with a continuously oozing wound—his wound is not a hadath (ritual impurity) but merely najis, so it does not nullify wudu during prayer time. The Hanafi position is that such oozing is indeed a hadath, but its ruling (nullification) is postponed due to necessity until after the prayer time, similar to urinary incontinence (sals al-bawl). The refutation uses two approaches: first, by affirming the ruling and showing it is not delayed from the cause (the hadath exists but its effect is temporarily suspended); second, by stating the purpose of the cause—to equate blood with urine as both being hadath that become excused when continuous. The author then summarizes that four ways to defend against naqḍ have been completed. This is a typical Hanafi usul method: they accept the kawn (existence) of the 'illah even if its athar (effect) is blocked by a necessity (darūrah).

Key Terms
النقض (al-naqḍ): An objection that the 'illah (cause) produces a contradictory ruling in a case where it should apply, thereby invalidating the analogy.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): A state of ritual impurity that nullifies wudu; in this passage, it is argued to apply to wound oozing despite being continuous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a person suffers from a continuously oozing wound, what is the Hanafi position on wudu during prayer time?
A) Wudu is invalidated immediately.
B) Wudu remains valid during prayer time, but must be renewed after.
C) Wudu is never required because it is not a hadath.
D) The person must pray without wudu.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul defends an 'illah from naqḍ by showing that its effect can be temporarily suspended due to necessity without undermining the causal link.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Mu‘āraḍah and Qalb: The Inversion Method in Hanafi Usul
Defining mu‘āraḍah and explaining the first type with qalb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two types of mu‘āraḍah and apply the qalb method to refute an opponent's analogy in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Qalb inverts the cause and ruling to expose the flaw in an opponent's analogy.

In usul al-fiqh, when two scholars disagree, mu‘āraḍah is the primary tool to counter the opponent's evidence. This lesson explains the two types of mu‘āraḍah and focuses on the first type, qalb (inversion), where the cause and ruling are swapped. Using the classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on punishments for fornication, you will see how qalb refutes a weak analogy.

Guided Path
1
Define mu‘āraḍah and its two types
Mu‘āraḍah is presenting evidence contrary to the opponent's evidence. It is divided into two types: one that contains a contradiction (munāqaḍah) and one that does not. The type containing contradiction is called qalb.
The opposite of mu‘āraḍah that contains contradiction is not mere naqḍ but a specific inversion.
2
Understand qalb and its conditions
Qalb means making the cause a ruling and the ruling a cause, like turning a vessel upside down. It is valid only when the reasoning (ta‘līl) is by a ruling (ḥukm), not by a pure description (waṣf).
If the 'illah is a pure description, qalb is not accepted because it would be a mere contradiction.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
The Shafi'is argue: For Muslims, unmarried fornicators are flogged and married ones are stoned. So flogging is a cause for stoning. By analogy, disbelievers should be treated similarly: unmarried flogged, married stoned.
They treat the ruling (jald) as a cause for another ruling (rajm).
4
Apply the Hanafi qalb to refute
The Hanafis invert: stoning is actually the cause for flogging in Muslims. Moreover, Islam is a condition for ihsān (being muhṣan), and disbelievers can never be muhṣan. Thus, all disbelievers—married or not—are flogged.
By inverting the cause-effect, the Shafi'i analogy loses its foundation.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis flog all fornicating disbelievers; Shafi'is stone married disbelievers. This shows the real-world impact of the qalb argument.
The dispute arises from a different conception of ihsān.

أما المعارضة التي فيها مناقضة فالقلب، وهو نوعان، أحدهما قلب العلة حكماً والحكم علة، وهو مأخوذ من قلب الإناء، وإنما يصح هذا فيما يكون التعليل فيه بالحكم، مثل قولهم الكفار جنس يجلد بكرهم مائة، فيرجم تيبهم كالمسلمين. قلنا: أي الشافعية المسلمون إنما يجلد بكرهم مائة؛ لأنه يرجم ثيبهم، المعارضة: وهي إقامة الدليل على خلاف ما أقام الدليل عليه الخصم، فإن كان هو ذلك الدليل الأول بعينه فهو النوع الأول وإلا فهو النوع الثاني. معارضة فيها إلخ فمن حيث تدلّ على نقيض مدعى المعلل تسمّى معارضة، ومن حيث أن دليله لم يصح دليلاً له، بل صار دليلا للخصم تسمّى مناقضة لخلل في الدليل، ولما كان المعارضة أصلا فيه والنقض ضمنياً؛ لأن النقض القصدي لا يرد على الدليل المؤثر، سميت معارضة فيها المناقضة، لا مناقضة فيها المعارضة. فالقلب : أي هي القلب في اصطلاح الأصول والمناظرة، والقلب تغيير التعليل إلى هيئة تخالف الهيئة التي كان عليها، بأن يجعل المعلول علة والعلة معلولاً مثلا على مثال قلب الإناء. قلب الإناء: أي جعل أعلاها أسفلها وأسفلها أعلاها، فإن العلة لكونها أصلاً كانت أعلى من الحكم والحكم لكونه تبعا كان أسفل منها، وبهذا القلب يصير أعلى التعليل أسفله وأسفله أعلاه، فكان كقلب الإناء. بالحكم بأن يجعل المستدلّ حكم الأصل علة لحكم آخر فيه ثم عداه إلى الفرع، وأما إذا كانت العلة وصفاً محضاً فلا يقبل هذا النوع كالمسلمين والحاصل أن عندهم الإسلام ليس بشرط للإحصان، فكما أن المحصنين من المسلمين يرجمون وغير المحصنين يجلدون فكذا الكفار يجب أن يرجم المحصنون منهم ويجلد غيرهم، فجعلوا جلد المائة علة لرجم الثيب بالقياس على المسلمين، وهو في الواقع حكم شرعي، وعندنا لما كان الإسلام شرطاً للإحصان فالكفّار كلهم غير محصنين فليس عليهم إلا الجلد بكرهم وثيبهم فيه سواء، عارضناهم بالقلب. قلنا : المسلمون إلخ : أعني لانسلّم أن الجلد علة للرجم في المسلمين، حتى يقال: إن الجلد يوجد في ثيبي الكفار، فيجب الرجم أيضاً بل الأمر بالعكس، وهو أن الرجم علة لجلد المائة في المسلمين، فلما احتمل الانقلاب =
Chapter on Counter-argument (Mu‘āraḍah). Types of Mu‘āraḍah: As for Mu‘āraḍah, it is of two types: a counter-argument containing contradiction (munāqaḍah), and a pure counter-argument. [Qalb] The first type: As for the counter-argument that contains contradiction, it is Qalb (inversion), and it is of two kinds: one is making the cause a ruling and the ruling a cause, and it is derived from turning over a vessel. This is valid only when the reasoning is by the ruling, such as their statement: 'The disbelievers are a category: their unmarried ones are flogged a hundred, and their married ones are stoned, like Muslims.' We said: i.e., the Shafi'is: Muslims, their unmarried ones are flogged a hundred because their married ones are stoned. Mu‘āraḍah: it is presenting evidence contrary to what the opponent has presented evidence for. If it is the same first evidence, it is the first type; otherwise it is the second type. 'Mu‘āraḍah containing' etc.: insofar as it indicates the opposite of the claimant's claim, it is called Mu‘āraḍah; insofar as his evidence did not become evidence for him, but rather became evidence for the opponent, it is called Munāqaḍah (contradiction) due to a defect in the evidence. Since Mu‘āraḍah is primary and Naqḍ is secondary (because deliberate contradiction does not affect the effective evidence), it is called 'Mu‘āraḍah containing Munāqaḍah', not 'Munāqaḍah containing Mu‘āraḍah'. So Qalb: it is, in the terminology of Uṣūl and debate, Qalb is changing the reasoning to a form opposite to the form it was upon, by making the effect a cause and the cause an effect, like turning a vessel. Turning a vessel: i.e., making its top its bottom and its bottom its top. For the cause, being an origin, is higher than the ruling, and the ruling, being a follower, is lower than it. By this inversion, the top of the reasoning becomes its bottom and its bottom its top, so it is like turning a vessel. 'By the ruling': by having the proponent make the ruling of the origin a cause for another ruling in it, then transfer it to the branch. But if the cause is a pure description, this type is not accepted. Like the Muslims: the outcome is that according to them Islam is not a condition for ihsān, so just as the Muslims who are muhṣan are stoned and those who are not muhṣan are flogged, so too the disbelievers: their muhṣan should be stoned and others flogged. So they made flogging a hundred a cause for stoning the married one by qiyās on Muslims, but it is actually a legal ruling. According to us, since Islam is a condition for ihsān, all disbelievers are non-muhṣan; so they only get flogging, their unmarried and married are equal. We countered them by Qalb. We said: 'Muslims' etc.: i.e., we do not concede that flogging is a cause for stoning in Muslims, such that it is said that flogging exists in married disbelievers, so stoning would also be necessary. Rather, the opposite: stoning is a cause for flogging a hundred in Muslims. Since inversion is possible =
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage defines Mu‘āraḍah (counter-argument) in uṣūl al-fiqh and focuses on the first type, which is Qalb (inversion). Mu‘āraḍah is presenting evidence against an opponent's evidence. It is divided into two types: one that contains a contradiction (munāqaḍah) and a pure one. The type containing contradiction is Qalb, which itself has two subtypes: (1) making the cause a ruling and the ruling a cause (valid only when the 'illah is a ḥukm); (2) other forms. Qalb is likened to turning a vessel upside down, swapping the position of cause and effect. The author illustrates with a dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding punishment for fornication. The Shafi'is argue that because Muslim unmarried fornicators are flogged 100 lashes and married ones are stoned, the same should apply to disbelievers. They treat flogging (a ruling) as a cause for stoning in Muslims. The Hanafis counter with Qalb: they invert the relationship—stoning is actually the cause for flogging in Muslims (since flogging is prescribed because the married one avoids stoning). Since Islam is a condition for ihsān (being muhṣan), disbelievers are never muhṣan, so they only receive flogging. Thus the analogy fails. This demonstrates how Qalb can be used to refute an opponent's reasoning by showing the cause-effect relationship is reversed.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍah): Presenting a proof contrary to the opponent's proof, either by using the same proof (first type) or a different one (second type).
القلب (al-qalb): Inverting the positions of cause and ruling in a ta‘līl, such that the ruling becomes the cause and the cause becomes the ruling, used to refute an opponent's analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute about punishment for disbelieving fornicators, what is the Hanafi counter-argument using qalb?
A) Flogging is a cause for stoning in Muslims.
B) Stoning is a cause for flogging in Muslims.
C) Flogging and stoning are both punishments but independent.
D) Disbelievers are not subject to Islamic punishments.

Key Takeaway
The qalb method in Hanafi usul inverts the presumed cause and ruling to reveal the weakness in an opponent's qiyas, preserving the integrity of legal reasoning.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Definition and Types of Mu'aradah: Qalb of 'Illa and Hukm
Defines mu'aradah and explains the first type of qalb (inversion of 'illa and hukm).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'aradah, distinguish between opposition containing contradiction and pure opposition, and explain the mechanism and condition of the first type of qalb (inversion of 'illa and hukm) using the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute as an example.

Core Idea
Mu'aradah with qalb turns the opponent's evidence against them by inverting cause and ruling.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, mu'aradah (opposition) is a key method for challenging an opponent's qiyas. Not all opposition is equal: some undermine the opponent's evidence by exposing an internal contradiction. This lesson unpacks that type—qalb—and its first variety, the inversion of 'illa and hukm, which is only valid when the 'illa is itself a ruling. You will see this principle in action in the famous Hanafi-Shafi'i ikhtilaf on the punishment of married disbelievers for adultery.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of mu'aradah
Find where the passage defines mu'aradah as 'presenting evidence contrary to the opponent's evidence'. Note that it can be pure or contain contradiction.
The passage first gives a general definition then splits into types.
2
Identify the two types of mu'aradah
The passage states mu'aradah has two types: one 'containing contradiction' (qalb) and one 'pure' (without contradiction). Distinguish them.
The type containing contradiction is the focus here.
3
Understand the first type of qalb
Qalb of 'illa and hukm means inverting the cause and ruling. This is like turning a vessel upside down. It only works when the 'illa used by the opponent is itself a ruling, not a pure attribute.
The condition is key: 'innama yasihhu hadha fima yakunu al-ta'lil bihi bi al-hukm'.
4
Analyze the example: Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute
The Shafi'is analogize disbelievers to Muslims: flogging for unmarried, stoning for married. The Hanafis perform qalb by inverting the cause: in Muslims, it is stoning (the threat) that causes flogging, not the reverse. This shows the Shafi'i 'illa is actually a ruling, so the analogy fails.
The Hanafi position: Islam is a condition for ihsan, so disbelievers are never muhsan and only face flogging.
5
Apply the condition
Check that in the example, the 'illa (the ruling of flogging) is indeed a ruling, not a pure attribute, so qalb is valid. If the 'illa were a pure attribute (e.g., intoxicating), this type would not apply.
Recognizing the nature of the 'illa is crucial for using qalb correctly.

باب القياس
فصل في المعارضة
أنواع المعارضة
أما المعارضة فهي نوعان معارضة فيها مناقضة، ومعارضة خالصة.
النوع الأول
النوع الثاني
أما المعارضة التي فيها مناقضة فالقلب، وهو نوعان، أحدهما قلب العلة حكماً والحكم علة، وهو مأخوذ من قلب الإناء، وإنما يصح هذا فيما يكون التعليل فيه بالحكم، مثل قولهم الكفار جنس يجلد بكرهم مائة، فيرجم تيبهم كالمسلمين. قلنا: أي الشافعية المسلمون إنما يجلد بكرهم مائة؛ لأنه يرجم ثيبهم، المعارضة: وهي إقامة الدليل على خلاف ما أقام الدليل عليه الخصم، فإن كان هو ذلك الدليل الأول بعينه فهو النوع الأول وإلا فهو النوع الثاني. معارضة فيها إلخ فمن حيث تدلّ على نقيض مدعى المعلل تسمّى معارضة، ومن حيث أن دليله لم يصح دليلاً له، بل صار دليلا للخصم تسمّى مناقضة لخلل في الدليل، ولما كان المعارضة أصلا فيه والنقض ضمنياً؛ لأن النقض القصدي لا يرد على الدليل المؤثر، سميت معارضة فيها المناقضة، لا مناقضة فيها المعارضة. فالقلب : أي هي القلب في اصطلاح الأصول والمناظرة، والقلب تغيير التعليل إلى هيئة تخالف الهيئة التي كان عليها، بأن يجعل المعلول علة والعلة معلولاً مثلا على مثال قلب الإناء. قلب الإناء: أي جعل أعلاها أسفلها وأسفلها أعلاها، فإن العلة لكونها أصلاً كانت أعلى من الحكم والحكم لكونه تبعا كان أسفل منها، وبهذا القلب يصير أعلى التعليل أسفله وأسفله أعلاه، فكان كقلب الإناء. بالحكم بأن يجعل المستدلّ حكم الأصل علة لحكم آخر فيه ثم عداه إلى الفرع، وأما إذا كانت العلة وصفاً محضاً فلا يقبل هذا النوع كالمسلمين والحاصل أن عندهم الإسلام ليس بشرط للإحصان، فكما أن المحصنين من المسلمين يرجمون وغير المحصنين يجلدون فكذا الكفار يجب أن يرجم المحصنون منهم ويجلد غيرهم، فجعلوا جلد المائة علة لرجم الثيب بالقياس على المسلمين، وهو في الواقع حكم شرعي، وعندنا لما كان الإسلام شرطاً للإحصان فالكفّار كلهم غير محصنين فليس عليهم إلا الجلد بكرهم وثيبهم فيه سواء، عارضناهم بالقلب. قلنا : المسلمون إلخ : أعني لانسلّم أن الجلد علة للرجم في المسلمين، حتى يقال: إن الجلد يوجد في ثيبي الكفار، فيجب الرجم أيضاً بل الأمر بالعكس، وهو أن الرجم علة لجلد المائة في المسلمين، فلما احتمل الانقلاب فسد الأصل وبطل القياس، وهذا القلب معارضة صورة حيث علّل السائل بتعليل يدلّ على خلاف حكم الذي أوجبه المعلّل، وهو رجم ثيبهم، وفيها معنى المناقضة حيث فسد دليلهم، بأنه لا يصلح علة.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Opposition. Types of Opposition: As for opposition, it is of two types: opposition containing contradiction, and pure opposition. First type, second type. As for opposition containing contradiction, it is inversion (qalb), and it is of two types. One of them is inverting the cause into a ruling and the ruling into a cause, and it is derived from inverting a vessel. This is only valid when the reasoning is by means of a ruling, like their statement: 'The disbelievers are a category: their unmarried are flogged one hundred, and their married are stoned, like Muslims.' We say: i.e., the Shafi'is: Muslims are flogged one hundred as unmarried only because their married are stoned. Opposition: it is to present evidence contrary to what the opponent presented as evidence. If it is the very same first evidence, it is the first type; otherwise it is the second type. 'Opposition containing etc.' So from the aspect that it indicates the opposite of the claim of the proponent, it is called opposition; from the aspect that his evidence did not stand as evidence for him, but rather became evidence for the opponent, it is called contradiction due to a defect in the evidence. Since opposition is fundamental and contradiction is implicit, because intended contradiction does not affect probative evidence, it is called 'opposition containing contradiction', not 'contradiction containing opposition'. 'Al-qalb': i.e., it is qalb in terminology of usul and debate, and qalb is changing the reasoning to a form contrary to the form it was upon, such as making the effect a cause and the cause an effect, analogously to inverting a vessel. 'Inversion of a vessel': i.e., making its top its bottom and its bottom its top. For the cause, being original, was higher than the ruling, and the ruling, being derivative, was lower than it. By this inversion, the higher of the reasoning becomes its lower and its lower its higher, thus resembling inverting a vessel. 'By means of a ruling': that the arguer makes the ruling of the original a cause for another ruling in it, then transfers it to the branch. But if the cause is a pure attribute, this type is not accepted. The summary is that according to them (Shafi'is), Islam is not a condition for ihsan; so just as married Muslims are stoned and unmarried are flogged, likewise disbelievers: their married should be stoned and their unmarried flogged. Thus they made flogging one hundred a cause for stoning the married by analogy to Muslims, whereas in reality it is a legal ruling. According to us, since Islam is a condition for ihsan, all disbelievers are non-muhsan, so they receive only flogging; their unmarried and married are equal. We countered them with inversion. 'We say: Muslims etc.': I mean, we do not concede that flogging is the cause for stoning in Muslims, such that it could be said that flogging exists among married disbelievers and therefore stoning must also apply. Rather, the opposite is true: stoning is the cause for flogging one hundred in Muslims. Since inversion is possible, the original argument is invalid and the analogy is nullified. This qalb is opposition in form, since the questioner gave a reasoning that contradicts the ruling that the proponent established (stoning of their married), and it contains the meaning of contradiction because their evidence is corrupted, as it does not qualify as a cause.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of mu'aradah (opposition) in qiyas. The author first distinguishes two types of opposition: one that involves naqd (contradiction) and one that is pure (without contradiction). The type containing contradiction is called qalb (inversion). Qalb itself has two types. The first type, which is the focus here, involves inverting the 'illa (cause) and the hukm (ruling). This is like turning a vessel upside down: what was the cause becomes the ruling, and the ruling becomes the cause. This type of qalb is only valid when the 'illa used by the opponent is itself a hukm (ruling), not a pure attribute. The author illustrates with a famous example from the debate between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the punishment of adulterers among non-Muslims. The Shafi'is argued that just as Muslims are flogged when unmarried and stoned when married, so too should the same apply to disbelievers. They made the flogging of the unmarried the 'illa for stoning the married by analogy. The Hanafis countered by inverting the 'illa: they argued that in Muslims, stoning is the 'illa for flogging (i.e., the threat of stoning is why the unmarried are flogged), not the other way around. Since inversion is possible, the Shafi'i evidence becomes invalid. This qalb serves as opposition (mu'arada) because it contradicts the opponent's claim, and it contains contradiction (naqd) because the opponent's evidence fails to actually support his claim. The Hanafi position is that Islam is a condition for ihsan (being muhsan, i.e., married and free), so all disbelievers are non-muhsan and only face flogging, whether married or not.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'aradah): Presenting evidence contrary to the opponent's evidence
القلب (al-qalb): Changing the reasoning to a contrary form, e.g., making the effect a cause
المناقضة (al-munaqadah): Contradiction in the opponent's evidence, making it invalid
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that justifies the ruling in qiyas
الحكم (al-hukm): The legal ruling that is being reasoned from the cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of mu'aradah with qalb, what is the condition for the first type of qalb to be valid?
A) The 'illa must be a pure attribute.
B) The 'illa must be a hukm (ruling).
C) The 'illa must be from the Quran or Sunnah.
D) The 'illa must be agreed upon by all schools.

Key Takeaway
The first type of qalb is a powerful tool in Hanafi usul for rebutting analogies that misuse rulings as causes, but it only works when the 'illa is itself a ruling.

Second Type of Qalb: Inverting the Attribute
Defines qalb al-wasf with metaphor and example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qalb al-wasf, identify its condition of an additional explanatory attribute, and distinguish it from pure opposition using the fasting example.

Core Idea
Qalb al-wasf turns an opponent's attribute against them by adding a qualifying description without changing the original attribute.

This lesson introduces the second type of qalb (inversion) in Hanafi jurisprudential debate: inverting the attribute (wasf) rather than the ruling. Understanding this subtle tool is essential for analyzing how Hanafi scholars refute opposing arguments by using the same attribute against them. We will explore the saddlebag metaphor and the classic fasting dispute with the Shafi'is.

Guided Path
1
Understand the saddlebag metaphor
Visualize a saddlebag (jirab) turned inside out: the back becomes the front. Similarly, an attribute initially facing the opponent (witness for the proponent) is inverted to face the proponent (witness against him).
The metaphor emphasizes that the attribute itself is not changed; only its orientation relative to the two parties.
2
Identify the condition: additional attribute
Qalb al-wasf requires adding an attribute (wasf za'id) that explains or confirms the first attribute, not replacing it. Without this, it becomes pure opposition (mu'arada) not qalb.
The added attribute must be an explanation (tafsir) of the first, not a change.
3
Work through the fasting example
The Shafi'is argue: 'Ramadan fast is obligatory (fard) so it requires specific intention.' The Hanafis respond by keeping the attribute 'obligation' but adding that obligation itself obviates the need for specific intention. Thus the same attribute (fardiyyah) is inverted.
Notice the Hanafis do not deny the attribute; they use it to oppose the Shafi'i claim.
4
Distinguish qalb al-wasf from pure opposition
In pure opposition, you introduce a completely different attribute. In qalb al-wasf, you attach an explanatory attribute to the original, leaving the original intact but altering its legal implication.
The text says: if the added attribute changes the original, it becomes a different cause and thus pure opposition, not qalb.

والثاني قلب الوصف شاهدا على المعلّل بعد أن كان شاهداً له، وهو مأخوذ من قلب الجراب، فإنه كان ظهره إليك، أي ظهر الوصف فصار وجهه إليك، إلا أنه لا يكون إلا بوصف زائد فيه تفسير للأول. لكن الفرق بين صوم القضاء وصوم رمضان مثاله قولهم في صوم رمضان إنه صوم فرض فلا يتأدّى إلا بتعيين النية أي الشافعية = فسد الأصل وبطل القياس، فهذا القلب معارضة صورة حيث علّل السائل بتعليل يدلّ على خلاف حكم الذي أوجبه المعلّل، وهو رجم ثيبهم، وفيها معنى المناقضة حيث فسد دليلهم، بأنه لا يصلح علة. شاهدا له: أي للمعلل بأن جعل السائل وصف المعلل شاهداً نفسه بعد أن كان شاهداً له. وهو: أي هذا القلب. الجواب: الجراب بالفتح والكسر توشه، دان، والجراب إذا يقلب يجعل ظاهره باطناً وباطنه ظاهراً. فإنه : الضمير للشأن أو للوصف وهذا أرجح إليك: حيث كان شاهداً لك يحاج عنك كمن يقدم ليخاصم ووجهه كان إلى الخصم وهو السائل حيث كان يحاجه ويقابله، فإذا قلب بعده فصار وجهه إليك. وجهه إليك وظهره إلى الخصم حيث صار شاهداً عليك يحاجك عن خصمك، هذا إذا يراد من كاف الخطاب المعلّل، فإن يراد السائل كان معناه : كان ظهر الوصف إليك يا أيها السائل حيث كان معرضا عنك، كمن يذهب معرضاً عن رجل يصير ظهره إليه، فحينئذ كان الوصف شاهداً عليك، فإذا قلب صار مقبلاً إليك ومعرضاً عن المعلّل، فحينئذ صار شاهداً على المعلل، فهذا القلب معارضة من حيث إنه يدل على خلاف مدعى الخصم، وفيه مناقضة من حيث أن دليله لم يدلّ على مدعاه وأهل المناظرة يسمونه بالمعارضة بالقلب. تفسير للأول: أي هذا النوع من القلب لا يتحقق إلا بوصف زائد على وصف المعلل يكون في ذلك الوصف تفسير وتقرير للوصف الأول، لا أنه تغيير له فاندفع مايتوهّم وروده من أن القلب لا يتحقق إلا بتعليق الحكم بعين ذلك الوصف، فإذا زيد عليه وصف آخر لم يبق بعينه علة، فيكون هذا تعليق الحكم بعلة أخرى، فيكون معارضة محضة غير متضمّنة للإبطال، فإذا قال هذه الزيادة تفسير للوصف الأول لا تغيير له فاندفع. مثاله : أي هذا النوع من القلب. إنه صوم فرض إلخ : فجعلوا الفرضية علة التعيين، فعارضناهم بالقلب وجعلنا الفرضية دليلا على عدم التعيين.
The second type is inverting the attribute (wasf), [turning it] as a witness against the proponent after it was a witness for him. It is derived from inverting a saddlebag (jirab): its back was towards you, i.e., the back of the attribute, so its face became towards you, but it only occurs with an additional attribute that explains the first. However, the difference between fast of make-up and fast of Ramadan. An example: their statement about Ramadan fasting: 'It is an obligatory fast, so it is not fulfilled except with specific intention' (i.e., the Shafi'is). Then the original becomes invalid and the analogy nullified. This qalb is opposition in form... 'Witness for him': i.e., for the proponent, because the questioner made the proponent's attribute a witness for himself after it was a witness for the proponent. 'It': i.e., this qalb. 'The answer: al-jirab with fatha and kasra toshah dan...' 'For it': the pronoun refers to the situation or the attribute, and this is more likely. 'To you': where it was a witness for you arguing on your behalf, like someone presenting to dispute, his face was to the opponent, i.e., the questioner, where he was disputing and confronting him. When it is inverted later, its face becomes to you. Its face to you and its back to the opponent, where it became a witness against you arguing on behalf of your opponent. This is if the address is intended for the proponent. If it is intended for the questioner, the meaning is: the back of the attribute was towards you, O questioner, as it was turning away from you, like someone who leaves turning his back to a man. Then the attribute was a witness against you. When inverted, it becomes facing you and turning away from the proponent, then it becomes a witness against the proponent. So this qalb is opposition insofar as it indicates the opposite of the opponent's claim, and it contains contradiction insofar as his evidence did not indicate his claim. Disputation experts call it 'opposition by inversion'. 'Explanation of the first': i.e., this type of qalb only occurs with an attribute additional to the proponent's attribute, in which there is an explanation and affirmation of the first attribute, not a change of it. Thus it repels the mistaken notion that qalb only occurs by attaching the ruling to that same attribute, for if another attribute is added, it is no longer the same cause, making this a pure opposition not containing invalidation. So if it is said that this addition is an explanation of the first attribute, not a change, then it is repelled. 'Its example': i.e., this type of qalb. 'It is an obligatory fast etc.': they made obligation (fardiyyah) the cause for requiring specific intention, so we countered them with inversion and made obligation a proof against requiring specific intention.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage explains the second type of qalb, which involves inverting the attribute (wasf) rather than the ruling. The analogy is with a saddlebag: originally the attribute faces the opponent, providing evidence for the proponent's claim. By adding an additional attribute that explains or qualifies the first, the attribute is turned around, so that the same attribute now becomes evidence against the proponent. The author gives the example of fasting: the Shafi'is argue that since Ramadan fast is obligatory (fard), it requires a specific intention (niyyah) to be valid. The Hanafis counter by inverting the attribute: they use the very same attribute of obligation to argue that no specific intention is needed, because the obligation itself is sufficient. Thus the attribute (fardiyyah) is turned from a witness for the opponent to a witness against him. This type of qalb is only valid when the added attribute explains or determines the first, not when it changes it entirely. The commentary elaborates on the metaphor of the saddlebag, describing how the direction of the attribute shifts.

Key Terms
قلب الوصف (qalb al-wasf): Inverting the attribute so that what was evidence for the proponent becomes evidence against him
الجراب (al-jirab): A saddlebag; used as a metaphor for the attribute changing orientation
الوصف الزائد (al-wasf al-za'id): An additional attribute that explains the first without changing it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the essential condition for the validity of qalb al-wasf according to the Hanafi usul text?
A) The attribute must be completely replaced by a new one.
B) There must be an additional attribute that explains and confirms the first attribute.
C) The ruling must be inverted, not the attribute.
D) The opponent must agree to the inversion.

Key Takeaway
Qalb al-wasf inverts an opponent's attribute by adding an explanatory description, turning their own evidence against them.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qalb: The Inversion Technique in Mu'arada
Defining qalb as a type of mu'arada with two illustrative ikhtilaf examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qalb, apply it to differentiate Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on intention for Ramadan fasting, and evaluate its validity conditions.

Core Idea
Qalb inverts the opponent's attribute with an extra qualifier, turning their proof into your own.

In Hanafi usul, debating through qiyas often involves mu'arada—counter-arguments that challenge the opponent's analogy. One powerful form is 'qalb' (inversion), where you take the very attribute your opponent relied upon and, by adding a precise qualifier, argue for the opposite ruling. This lesson dissects the definition of qalb through the classic dispute over intention in Ramadan fasting, showing how the Hanafi school used qalb to refute the Shafi'i insistence on daily niyyah renewal. By mastering qalb, you learn a key tool of Hanafi dialectic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core attribute
Find the wasf (attribute) that the opponent uses to support their ruling. In the first example, the Shafi'is used 'obligation' (fardiyyah) to require specification of intention.
The attribute is the common factor in both sides' analogies.
2
Understand the inversion mechanism
See how the Hanafis invert the attribute without changing it: they add the qualifier 'after its specification' (ba'da ta'ayyunihi) to argue that obligation after specification removes the need for further specification.
The inversion does not deny the attribute; it redirects its implication.
3
Trace the added qualifier
Note the extra interpretive element (ziyada) that makes qalb valid. Without this, it would be a mere counter-claim (mu'arada mahda).
The qualifier must be derived from the source text or evident context.
4
Apply to the supererogatory example
Examine the second example (nawafil vs wudu) and see how the same method works, though the text notes this form is weaker.
Not all inversions are equally strong; some require more careful justification.
5
Distinguish qalb from simple change
The passage warns that qalb must interpret, not alter, the attribute. If the attribute is completely changed, it becomes a different argument, not qalb.
Valid qalb preserves the original attribute's essence but reinterprets its legal significance.

باب القياس
فصل في المعارضة
فلما احتمل الانقلاب فسد الأصل وبطل القياس، والثاني قلب الوصف من القلب، وهو مأخوذ من قلب الجراب، فإنه كان ظهره إليك، أي ظهر الوصف فصار وجهه إليك، إلا أنه لا يكون إلا بوصف زائد فيه تفسير للأول.
مثاله قولهم في صوم رمضان إنه صوم فرض فلا يتأدّى إلا بتعيين النية، فعارضناهم بالقلب وجعلنا الفرضية دليلا على عدم التعيين، فقلنا: لما كان صوماً فرضاً استغني عن تعيين النية بعد تعينه، كصوم القضاء لكنه إنما يتعين بعد الشروع، وهذا تعيّن قبل الشروع.
وقد يقلب من وجه آخر، وهو ضعيف.
مثاله: قولهم هذه عبادة لا يمضى في فاسدها، بل فاسد النوافل فوجب أن لا يلزم بالشروع كالوضوء، فيقال لهم: لما كان كذلك وجب.. تعينه من جانب الشارع كصوم القضاء: فإنه يحتاج إلى تعيّن واحد فكذا صوم رمضان، فهما سويان في ذلك.
تعيّن من جانب الشارع حيث قال: "إذا انسلخ شعبان فلا صوم إلا عن رمضان"، فصوم رمضان والقضاء سويّان في أنه لا يحتاج إلى تعين آخر بعد تعين، لكن رمضان لما كان متعينا من قبل الشارع فلايحتاج إلى تعين العبد، وصوم القضاء لما لم يكن كذلك يحتاج إلى تعين العبد.
وحاصل المقام أن أصحاب الشافعي قالوا: يجب تعين النية لكل يوم من رمضان، واستدلوا عليه بأنه صوم فرض كصوم القضاء، فكما يجب تعين صوم القضاء بوجه الفرضية فكذا يجب تعين صوم رمضان، فجعلوا الفرضية علة للتعين وقاسوا على القضاء، فعارضناهم بالقلب وجعلنا علة عدم التعين ما جعلوه علة التعين وهو الفرضية، ولما أبهم الخصم الفرضية ولم يبيّن أن الفرضية علة للتعين قبل التعين أو بعده ففسرنا الفرضية التي كان وصفاً شاهداً لهم، وزدنا في القلب لفظ "بعد تعينه"، وقلنا: إن الصوم الفرض بعد تعيينه لا يحتاج إلى تعين آخر، وصوم رمضان متعين بتعيين الشارع قبل الشروع فيه، وصار كصوم القضاء بعد تعينه بسبب الشروع، فكما أن صوم القضاء بعد تعيين العبد لايحتاج إلى تعين آخر، صوم رمضان بعد تعينه من جانب الشارع لا يحتاج إلى تعين آخر وهو تعيين العبد، فوصف الفرضية كان لهم حيث كان علة للتعين، وما فسرناه في القلب وقلنا هذا الوصف تعين لا يحتاج إلى تعين آخر صار شاهداً لنا، وفي هذا التفسير ليس تغيير الوصف بل تقريره وتفسيره.
وجه آخر سوى الوجهين المذكورين، ويسمّى قلب التسوية.
قولهم أي أصحاب الشافعي في حق النوافل حيث لاتحب بالشروع ولاتقضى بإفسادها عندهم عبادة لا يمضي في فاسدها: أي إذا فسدت بنفسها بظهور الحدث من المصلّي لا يجب إتمامها، وهذا بخلاف الحجّ فإنه يجب بالشروع؛ لأن المضي يجب فيه بعد الفساد.
فاسدها وفي نسخة "فسادها كالوضوء" فأصحاب الشافعي جعل علة عدم اللزوم في النوافل عدم الإمضاء في الفساد وقاسوا على الوضوء حيث لا يمضى في فساده، فقالوا كما أن الوضوء لايلزم بالشروع لعدم الإمضاء في الفساد فكذا النوافل لا تجب بالشروع لعدم الإمضاء في الفساد.
لما كان كذلك: أي لما كانت هذه النوافل لاتمضي في فسادها وصارت كالوضوء حيث لا يمضى في فساده.
Chapter on Qiyas. Section on Mu'arada. Since inversion is possible, the foundation becomes corrupt and the analogy invalid. The second type is inversion of the attribute from qalb, derived from turning a bag, which had its back to you, meaning the back of the attribute became its face toward you, but only with an additional attribute that interprets the first. For example, their statement about the fast of Ramadan: it is an obligatory fast so it cannot be performed except with specified intention. We countered them by inversion and made obligation a proof for non-specification, saying: since it is an obligatory fast, specification of intention is dispensed with after its specification, like the fast of qada', but that becomes specified only after commencement, whereas this is specified before commencement. It may be inverted from another perspective, which is weak. Example: their statement: this act of worship does not proceed in its invalid state — rather the invalid supererogatory — so it is not binding upon commencement, like wudu'. So it is said to them: since that is the case, its specification from the Lawgiver is necessary, like the fast of qada', for it needs one specification, and so the fast of Ramadan, both are equal in that. Specification from the Lawgiver where He said: 'When Sha'ban ends, there is no fasting except for Ramadan.' So both the fast of Ramadan and qada' are equal in that they do not need another specification after specification, but Ramadan, since it is specified by the Lawgiver, does not need specification by the slave, whereas the fast of qada', since it is not so, needs specification by the slave. In summary, the followers of al-Shafi'i said: specification of intention is obligatory for each day of Ramadan, and they argued that it is an obligatory fast like the fast of qada', so as specification is obligatory for qada' due to obligation, so must specification be for Ramadan. They made obligation the cause for specification and analogized to qada'. We countered them by inversion and made the cause for non-specification that which they made the cause for specification, namely obligation. Since the opponent left the term 'obligation' ambiguous and did not clarify whether obligation is a cause for specification before or after specification, we interpreted the obligation that was an attribute witnessing for them, and we added the phrase 'after its specification' in the inversion, and we said: the obligatory fast after its specification does not need another specification, and the fast of Ramadan is specified by the Lawgiver before commencement, and it becomes like the fast of qada' after its specification due to commencement. So as the fast of qada' after specification by the slave does not need another specification, the fast of Ramadan after its specification from the Lawgiver does not need another specification, i.e., specification by the slave. So the attribute of obligation was for them where it was a cause for specification, and what we interpreted in the inversion — saying this attribute is specification needing no other specification — became a witness for us. In this interpretation, there is no change of the attribute, but rather its consolidation and interpretation. Another aspect besides the two mentioned, called inversion of equalization. Their statement — the followers of al-Shafi'i regarding supererogatory acts that are not binding upon commencement and are not made up if invalidated according to them — an act of worship that does not proceed in its invalid state: i.e., if it becomes invalid by itself due to the emergence of an event from the worshipper, it is not obligatory to complete it. This is contrary to Hajj, for it becomes binding upon commencement because proceeding is obligatory after invalidation. 'Its invalid state' in another version 'its invalidation like wudu'. The followers of al-Shafi'i made the cause for non-binding in supererogatory acts the lack of proceeding in invalidation and analogized to wudu, which does not proceed in its invalidation. They said: just as wudu is not binding upon commencement due to lack of proceeding in invalidation, so supererogatory acts are not binding upon commencement due to lack of proceeding in invalidation. 'Since that is the case': i.e., since these supererogatory acts do not proceed in their invalidation and become like wudu, which does not proceed in its invalidation.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an extended definition and illustration of 'qalb' (inversion) as a type of mu'arada (counter-argument) in qiyas. The author begins by stating that when inversion is possible, the original analogy becomes invalid. The second type of mu'arada is qalb, derived from turning a bag inside out: the attribute that previously supported the opponent's claim is turned to support one's own claim. However, this is only valid if there is an additional qualifier that interprets the original attribute without changing it entirely. The author then provides two key examples from Hanafi fiqh. The first involves the requirement of specifying intention (niyyah) for each day of Ramadan fasting. The Shafi'is argued that since Ramadan fast is obligatory, like qada' fast, it requires specific intention. The Hanafis countered by inverting the attribute: they argued that obligation, after specification, actually eliminates the need for further specification, because Ramadan is already specified by the Lawgiver (by the hadith 'No fasting except for Ramadan'), whereas qada' requires specification by the slave. Thus, the same attribute (obligation) is used to support the opposite ruling. The author stresses that this inversion does not change the attribute but interprets it more precisely. The second example involves supererogatory prayers (nawafil): the Shafi'is argued that since these prayers do not require completion if invalidated (unlike Hajj), they are not binding upon commencement, analogizing to wudu. The Hanafis would counter by noting that the attribute of 'not proceeding in invalidity' is also present in Hajj after invalidation? Actually, the text becomes less clear, but the point is to illustrate qalb. The author concludes by mentioning another weak form called 'qalb al-taswiya' (inversion of equalization). This passage is dense but essential for understanding Hanafi usul methodology in debate.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): A type of mu'arada where the attribute used by the opponent is inverted to support the opposite ruling, typically with an additional qualifier that interprets the attribute
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): A counter-argument in qiyas that either invalidates the opponent's analogy or provides a conflicting analogy
الوصف (al-wasf): The attribute or quality used as the effective cause (illa) in qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi counter-argument (qalb) regarding intention for Ramadan fast, what additional qualifier did the Hanafis add to the attribute of obligation?
A) After the fast has commenced
B) Before the month begins
C) After its specification (ba'da ta'ayyunihi)
D) As an absolute attribute

Key Takeaway
Qalb is a valid mu'arada only when the attribute is turned with an additional interpretive qualifier, not merely reversed.

Pure Counter-argument: Definition and Types
Defines pure counter-argument in qiyas and outlines its two main types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define pure counter-argument (mu'āraḍa khāliṣa) and distinguish it from qalb based on Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Pure counter-argument directly contradicts the opponent's qiyas without inverting the 'illa.

Hanafi usul recognizes several methods of rebutting an opponent's qiyas. One key method is pure counter-argument (mu'āraḍa khāliṣa), which directly contradicts the ruling or 'illa without relying on inversion (qalb). This lesson examines its definition, two types, and the critical distinction from qalb, using the classical example of supererogatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Define pure counter-argument
From the passage, state that pure counter-argument is a rebuttal that directly contradicts the opponent's qiyas without employing qalb (inversion of the 'illa).
The term 'khāliṣa' means pure or free from mixing.
2
Identify the two types
The passage mentions two types of pure counter-argument: one in the ruling of the branch (ḥukm al-far‘) and another (likely in the 'illa, though not detailed). Focus on the first type, which is valid.
The second type is not elaborated due to the cut-off text.
3
Examine the example
Work through the supererogatory prayer example: the Shafi'is analogized supererogatory prayers to wudu for non-bindingness; the Hanafi counter-argument tried to enforce equality between vow and commencement, but this turned into qalb because equality differed in meaning between original and branch.
This example shows the danger of accidental qalb.
4
Distinguish from qalb
Recognize that pure counter-argument must be free from any element of qalb. The passage criticizes the argument that used qalb, showing it is not pure counter-argument.
True pure counter-argument directly contradicts the opponent's position without manipulation.
5
Apply the definition
Given a new qiyas scenario, decide whether a proposed counter-argument qualifies as pure counter-argument or as qalb.
Practice with additional examples from usul texts.

المعارضة الخالصة في حكم الفرع]
وأما المعارضة الخالصة ،فنوعان أحدهما في حكم الفرع، وهو صحيح
فيه: أي فيما شرع من العبادة النافلة عمل النذر إلخ أي كما يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الوضوء حيث لا يلزم الوضوء بهما، والوضوء كان عندكم أصلا ومقيساً عليه كذلك يجب أن يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الفرع وهو النوافل، والاستواء في النوافل لا يمكن أن يكون بعدم اللزوم؛ إذ النوافل بالنذر تلزم بالإجماع، فوجب أن تجب بالشروع أيضاً ليتحقق الاستواء فيهما، فالوصف الذي جعله أصحاب الشافعي الله علة عدم اللزوم وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علةً للاستواء ويلزم منه اللزوم بالشروع، فكان قلبا من هذا الوجه. من وجوه القلب من وجهين أحدهما ما بينه المصنف بقوله : لأنه إلخ. والثاني ما بينه المصنف في هذا القول: ولأن إلخ. بحكم :آخر أي لما جاء السائل بحكم آخر وهو التسوية، وهو ليس بمناقض للحكم الأول وهو عدم لزوم النوافل بالشروع؛ لأن المستدلّ لم ينف التسوية لكون إثباتها مناقضاً لمدّعاه. المناقضة: التي هي شرط لصحة القلب والاستواء الذي أثبته الخصم بالعلة المذكورة مختلف في المعنى إذ الاستواء بين النذر والشروع في الأصل أي الوضوء باعتبار عدم الإلزام، فإن الوضوء كما لا يلزم بالنذر لا يلزم بالشروع أيضا، فعلى هذا الاستواء سقوط، وفي الفرع أي النوافل باعتبار الإلزام، فعلى هذا هو ثبوت، وإليه أشار بقوله: ثبوت من وجه إلخ. على وجه التضاد: فإن الاستواء في الأصل باعتبار عدم الإلزام، وفي الفرع باعتبار الإلزام. وذلك: أي اختلاف الاستواء في الأصل والفرع ثبوتاً وسقوطاً للقياس : أي قياس المعارض بالقلب؛ لأن من شروط القياس أن يتعدّى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع بعينه أي بلا تفاوت وهو ههنا منتف؛ إذ الاستواء الذي في الأصل متضادّ للاستواء الذي أثبته المعارض في الفرع؛ إذ في الأول سقوط وفي الثاني ثبوت، وأن يشارك أحدهما الآخر في الاسم أي في اسم الاستواء؛ لأنه لا اعتبار للألفاظ، وإنما المقصود المعنى، وبين الاستوائين في فكيف صريح، يصح القياس. المعارضة الخالصة عن معنى المناقضة، وأهل المناظرة يسمونها بالمعارضة بالغير حكم الفرع بأن يقول المعترض: لنا دليل يدلّ على خلاف حكمك الذي أثبته في =
Pure counter-argument in the ruling of the branch] As for pure counter-argument, it is of two types: one is in the ruling of the branch, and it is valid. In it: i.e., regarding the supererogatory act of worship that is legislated, the act of a vow, etc. i.e., just as the act of a vow and commencement are equal in wudu, where wudu is not binding by either, and wudu was for you the original and the analogized-to; likewise, the act of a vow and commencement must be equal in the branch, i.e., supererogatory acts. But equality in supererogatory acts cannot be by non-bindingness, because supererogatory acts by a vow are binding by consensus. So they must become binding by commencement as well to realize equality in them. So the attribute that the followers of al-Shafi'i made the 'illa for non-bindingness, i.e., non-proceeding in corruption, we made it the 'illa for equality, and from it follows bindingness by commencement. Thus it was a qalb from this perspective. From two aspects of qalb: one is what the author explained by his saying 'because' etc.; the second is what the author explained in this statement: 'and because' etc. A ruling: i.e., when the questioner brought another ruling, i.e., equality, it is not contradictory to the first ruling, i.e., non-bindingness of supererogatory acts by commencement, because the proponent did not negate equality, since proving it contradicts his claim. The contradiction: which is a condition for the validity of qalb, and the equality that the opponent established by the mentioned 'illa differs in meaning: equality between vow and commencement in the original, i.e., wudu, in terms of non-obligation, because wudu is neither binding by vow nor by commencement. In this sense, equality is negation. In the branch, i.e., supererogatory acts, in terms of obligation, so in this sense it is affirmation. And to this he referred by his saying: 'affirmation in one aspect' etc. In a contradictory manner: equality in the original is in terms of non-obligation, and in the branch in terms of obligation. That is: the difference of equality in original and branch in affirmation and negation invalidates the qiyas, i.e., the qiyas countered by qalb, because one of the conditions of qiyas is that the ruling transfers from the original to the branch exactly, i.e., without discrepancy, and here it is absent: the equality in the original is contradictory to the equality that the opponent established in the branch; in the first it is negation, in the second affirmation. And that one shares with the other in name, i.e., the name of equality, because one does not consider wording, only meaning. Between the two equalities there is clear contradiction. Pure counter-argument is free from the meaning of contradiction, and the dialecticians call it counter-argument by 'other' in the ruling of the branch, as the objector says: we have a proof that indicates contrary to your ruling that you established in =
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage defines pure counter-argument (mu'āraḍa khāliṣa) in qiyas. It states that it has two types: one concerning the ruling of the branch (ḥukm al-far‘), which is valid. The text uses the earlier example of supererogatory prayers to illustrate how the Shafi'i argument is countered. The Shafi'is had analogized supererogatory prayers to wudu, claiming non-bindingness. The Hanafi counter-argument attempts to enforce equality (taswiya) between the act of vow and commencement, but this is criticized because the equality differs in meaning between the original (wudu) and the branch (supererogatory prayers). In the original, equality means non-bindingness; in the branch, it would require bindingness (since vows are binding by consensus). This difference violates the condition of qiyas that the ruling must transfer identically. The passage also distinguishes mu'āraḍa khāliṣa from qalb, noting that true pure counter-argument does not rely on qalb but directly presents a contradictory proof.

Key Terms
المعارضة الخالصة (al-mu'āraḍa al-khāliṣa): Pure counter-argument that directly contradicts the opponent's qiyas without using qalb.
القلب (al-qalb): Inversion of the 'illa; here it is contrasted with pure counter-argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid type of pure counter-argument (mu'āraḍa khāliṣa)?
A) Qalb (inversion of the 'illa).
B) Counter-argument in the ruling of the branch (ḥukm al-far‘).
C) Counter-argument by consensus (ijma‘).
D) Counter-argument by textual evidence (nass).

Key Takeaway
Pure counter-argument directly contradicts the opponent's qiyas without using qalb; it is valid when it meets this condition.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Mu'arada Khalisa fi Hukm al-Far': Valid Counter-Argument in Qiyas
Explains the validity of mu'arada targeting the ruling of the subsidiary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify mu'arada khalisa targeting the ruling of the subsidiary, distinguish it from qalb (inversion), and evaluate its validity using the condition of consistent 'illa transfer.

Core Idea
Mu'arada khalisa is valid if it establishes a different ruling through a new 'illa without direct contradiction.

In Hanafi usul, not every counter-argument in qiyas is invalid. This passage clarifies a specific type: pure counter-argument (mu'arada khalisa) directed at the ruling of the subsidiary (far'). Understanding this concept sharpens your ability to analyze and construct qiyas-based arguments, especially when facing objections from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate mu'arada khalisa from qalb
Mu'arada khalisa does not invert the opponent's 'illa; it introduces a different 'illa to establish a different ruling. Qalb uses the same 'illa to prove the opposite. Here the Hanafi responder does not invert the Shafi'i's 'illa but proposes a new equality-based 'illa.
The passage first rejects a weak form of mu'arada (by inversion) then affirms the pure form.
2
Identify the two types of mu'arada
The text states pure mu'arada is of two types: one in the ruling of the subsidiary (valid) and one in the ruling of the original (discussed elsewhere). Focus on the first type.
The passage under analysis is about mu'arada in the ruling of the subsidiary.
3
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over nafl obligations
The Shafi'i argues that starting a nafl act makes it obligatory, analogizing to a vow (nadhr). The Hanafi counters by proposing a different 'illa: 'equality of vow and initiation' derived from wudu. This is mu'arada khalisa because it does not directly contradict but offers an alternative basis.
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi holds breaking nafl is makruh not haram; Shafi'i holds it is obligatory to complete.
4
Check consistency of the 'illa transfer
The Hanafi then shows that if equality is taken as the 'illa, it leads to contradictory results: in the original (wudu) equality means non-obligation, but in the subsidiary (nafl) it would mean obligation (since vowed nafl is obligatory). This inconsistency invalidates the opponent's qiyas because the ruling must transfer identically.
The condition for valid qiyas is that the ruling transfers without difference (bi la tafawut).
5
Conclude the validity of mu'arada khalisa
Because the counter-argument establishes a different ruling without directly contradicting the proponent's claim, and it exposes a flaw in the opponent's reasoning, it is a valid form of mu'arada. The Hanafi position that nafl is not obligatory by start is upheld.
This type of mu'arada is called 'pure' because it is free from direct contradiction (munafada).
