باب القياس
فصل في المعارضة
أن يستوي فيه عمل النذر والشروع كالوضوء، وهو ضعيف من وجوه القلب؛ لأنه هذا النوع من القلب لما جاء بحكم آخر ذهبت المناقضة، ولأن المقصود من الكلام معناه، والاستواء ولا ينظر في الألفاظ مختلف في المعنى ثبوت من وجه وسقوط من وجه على وجه التضاد، وذلك مُبطل للقياس.
المعارضة الخالصة في حكم الفرع]
وأما المعارضة الخالصة ،فنوعان أحدهما في حكم الفرع، وهو صحيح
فيه: أي فيما شرع من العبادة النافلة عمل النذر إلخ أي كما يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الوضوء حيث لا يلزم الوضوء بهما، والوضوء كان عندكم أصلا ومقيساً عليه كذلك يجب أن يستوي عمل النذر والشروع في الفرع وهو النوافل، والاستواء في النوافل لا يمكن أن يكون بعدم اللزوم؛ إذ النوافل بالنذر تلزم بالإجماع، فوجب أن تجب بالشروع أيضاً ليتحقق الاستواء فيهما، فالوصف الذي جعله أصحاب الشافعي الله علة عدم اللزوم وهو عدم الإمضاء في الفساد جعلناه علةً للاستواء ويلزم منه اللزوم بالشروع، فكان قلبا من هذا الوجه. من وجوه القلب من وجهين أحدهما ما بينه المصنف بقوله : لأنه إلخ. والثاني ما بينه المصنف في هذا القول: ولأن إلخ. بحكم :آخر أي لما جاء السائل بحكم آخر وهو التسوية، وهو ليس بمناقض للحكم الأول وهو عدم لزوم النوافل بالشروع؛ لأن المستدلّ لم ينف التسوية لكون إثباتها مناقضاً لمدّعاه. المناقضة: التي هي شرط لصحة القلب والاستواء الذي أثبته الخصم بالعلة المذكورة مختلف في المعنى إذ الاستواء بين النذر والشروع في الأصل أي الوضوء باعتبار عدم الإلزام، فإن الوضوء كما لا يلزم بالنذر لا يلزم بالشروع أيضا، فعلى هذا الاستواء سقوط، وفي الفرع أي النوافل باعتبار الإلزام، فعلى هذا هو ثبوت، وإليه أشار بقوله: ثبوت من وجه إلخ.
على وجه التضاد: فإن الاستواء في الأصل باعتبار عدم الإلزام، وفي الفرع باعتبار الإلزام. وذلك: أي اختلاف الاستواء في الأصل والفرع ثبوتاً وسقوطاً للقياس : أي قياس المعارض بالقلب؛ لأن من شروط القياس أن يتعدّى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع بعينه أي بلا تفاوت وهو ههنا منتف؛ إذ الاستواء الذي في الأصل متضادّ للاستواء الذي أثبته المعارض في الفرع؛ إذ في الأول سقوط وفي الثاني ثبوت، وأن يشارك أحدهما الآخر في الاسم أي في اسم الاستواء؛ لأنه لا اعتبار للألفاظ، وإنما المقصود المعنى، وبين الاستوائين في فكيف صريح، يصح القياس. المعارضة الخالصة عن معنى المناقضة، وأهل المناظرة يسمونها بالمعارضة بالغير حكم الفرع بأن يقول المعترض: لنا دليل يدلّ على خلاف حكمك الذي أثبته في =
المعنى اختلاف بل تضاد
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Mu'arada. That the action of vow and initiation should be equal like wudu, and it is weak from aspects of inversion; because this type of inversion when it came with another ruling, the contradiction disappeared; and because the purpose of speech is its meaning, and equality without regarding wording differs in meaning: establishment from one aspect and negation from another in a contradictory manner, and that invalidates qiyas. The pure mu'arada in the ruling of the subsidiary: As for pure mu'arada, it is of two types: one in the ruling of the subsidiary, and it is valid. In it: i.e., regarding what is legislated of supererogatory worship, the action of vow etc. I.e., just as the action of vow and initiation are equal in wudu where wudu is not obligatory by either, and wudu was for you an original and measured upon, likewise should the action of vow and initiation be equal in the subsidiary which is supererogatory acts. And equality in supererogatory acts cannot be by non-obligation, because supererogatory acts by vow become obligatory by consensus, so it was necessary that they become obligatory by initiation also so that equality is realized in both. So the attribute which the Shafi'is made the cause of non-obligation, which is non-validity upon invalidity, we made it the cause of equality, and from it follows obligation by initiation, so it was an inversion from this aspect. From the aspects of inversion: two aspects: one is what the author explained by saying 'because...', and the second is what the author explained in this statement: 'and because...'. By 'another ruling', i.e., when the questioner came with another ruling which is equalization, and it is not contradictory to the first ruling which is non-obligation of supererogatory acts by initiation; because the proponent did not negate equalization since its establishment would contradict his claim. 'Contradiction' which is a condition for the validity of inversion. And the equality which the opponent established by the mentioned cause differs in meaning: equality between vow and initiation in the original i.e., wudu, in terms of non-imposition, for as wudu is not obligatory by vow, it is also not obligatory by initiation, so in this respect equality is negation; and in the subsidiary i.e., supererogatory acts, in terms of imposition, so in this respect it is establishment. And he alluded to that by saying: 'establishment from one aspect etc.' 'In a contradictory manner': for equality in the original is by non-imposition, and in the subsidiary by imposition. 'And that': i.e., the difference of equality in the original and subsidiary in establishment and negation, 'invalidates qiyas': i.e., the qiyas of the one who opposes by inversion; because among the conditions of qiyas is that the ruling transfers from the original to the subsidiary exactly without difference, and here it is absent; for the equality in the original is contradictory to the equality that the opponent established in the subsidiary; for in the first it is negation and in the second it is establishment. And that one shares the other in name, i.e., in the name of equality; because words are not considered, only meaning matters. And between the two equalities, how can qiyas be valid? Pure mu'arada without the meaning of contradiction, and the disputants call it mu'arada by other than the ruling of the subsidiary, where the objector says: we have a proof indicating contrary to your ruling which you established in = meaning difference, rather contradiction.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul work discussing the topic of mu'arada (counter-argument) in qiyas. The author first states that an attempted mu'arada by inversion (qalb) claiming that the action of a vow and starting an act should be equal (like in wudu) is weak. He then transitions to the first type of pure mu'arada: that which targets the ruling of the subsidiary (far'). He affirms its validity. The author explains this with an example: the Shafi'i argued that supererogatory (nafl) acts become obligatory by starting them, analogous to how a vow makes them obligatory. The Hanafi responder counters by inverting the 'illa: the attribute used by the Shafi'i (non-validity upon invalidity) is made the cause of equality, implying that just as wudu is not obligatory by vow or start, supererogatory acts should also not be obligatory by start. But this leads to a contradiction because supererogatory acts by vow are obligatory by consensus. The Hanafi then analyzes the inversion further, showing that the equality in the original (wudu) is in non-obligation, while in the subsidiary (nafl) it would be in obligation—thus the 'illa is not consistent. The passage emphasizes that for qiyas to be valid, the ruling must transfer identically; here the two equalities are opposite, so the qiyas fails. The author notes that this type of mu'arada is valid because it does not involve direct contradiction but establishes a different ruling through a new 'illa.

Key Terms
المعارضة الخالصة (al-mu'arada al-khalisa): The pure counter-argument that does not involve direct contradiction but rather establishes a different ruling by a different cause.
القلب (al-qalb): Inversion; a method of counter-argument where the opponent's own 'illa is used to prove the opposite of what they intended.
العلة (al-'illa): The legal cause or ratio legis that justifies the ruling in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the condition for mu'arada in the ruling of the subsidiary to be valid?
A) The counter-argument must directly contradict the original ruling.
B) The counter-argument must establish a different ruling through a new 'illa without contradiction.
C) The counter-argument must use the same 'illa as the original.
D) The counter-argument must be rejected by the proponent.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada khalisa targeting the ruling of the subsidiary is a valid usul tool to expose inconsistency in an opponent's qiyas, provided it introduces a new 'illa that yields a consistent counter-ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
Invalid Mu'arada: Objecting to the Cause of the Original
Explains invalidity of mu'arada in the cause of the original

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a mu'arada khalisa fi 'illat al-asl as invalid and explain the Hanafi position using the principle that absence of a cause does not necessitate absence of the ruling.

Core Idea
Absence of a specific cause does not disprove the ruling; rulings may have multiple causes.

In qiyas disputations, an opponent may object by claiming that the cause (illa) you have identified in the original (asl) is not present in the subsidiary (far'). This passage explains why such a counter-argument (mu'arada) is invalid according to the Hanafi school: it does not address the ruling itself and fails to undermine the analogy. Let us follow the author's reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of mu'arada
Recognize that this is a pure mu'arada that attacks the cause of the original (asl) rather than the ruling. The objector claims that the cause in the original is different and not present in the subsidiary.
The author calls this 'mu'arada khalisa fi 'illat al-asl'.
2
Understand the invalidity
The author states it is invalid for two reasons: first, it does not have a ruling (i.e., it fails to produce a legal effect), and second, even if it were transitive, it is corrupt. The core reason is that absence of a particular cause does not necessitate absence of the ruling.
The ruling may be based on multiple causes; removing one does not remove the ruling.
3
Examine the examples
The passage gives two examples: the wiping (mash) analogy (which is actually a valid mu'arada in the ruling) and the iron/gypsum analogy (which is the invalid type). Focus on the invalid example: the Shafi'i argues that the cause in gold/silver is thimaniyya, not weight and genus, and this is absent in iron.
The wiping example is given to contrast; the author later clarifies the invalid type.
4
Distinguish transitive vs non-transitive causes
The objector's alternative cause may be transitive (like staple food) or non-transitive (like thimaniyya). In either case, the mu'arada is invalid: if non-transitive, it cannot transfer to other cases; if transitive, it still does not disprove the proponent's cause, because the ruling can stand on another cause.
The key is that the mu'arada does not connect to the ruling itself.
5
Apply the rule
Any mu'arada that only challenges the existence of a specific cause without refuting the ruling itself is invalid. To be valid, the objection must target the ruling or show that the cause does not lead to the ruling.
This principle is widely accepted among Hanafi usulis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعارضة الخالصة في علة الأصل]
والثاني في علة الأصل، وذلك باطل لعدم حكمه، ولفساده لو أفاد تعديته؛ لأنه لا معارضة النوع من المعارضة اتصال له بموضع النزاع إلا من حيث أنه ينعدم تلك العلة فيه، وعدم العلة لا يوجب عدم الحكم، =
المقيس، ولها خمسة أقسام كلها مذكورة بالتفصيل في المطوّلات. ولما أعرض المصنف عن ذكرها فناسب لنا الإعراض صحيح لما فيه من إثبات حكم مخالف للحكم الأول بإثبات علة أخرى في ذلك المحل بعينه. مثاله ما إذا قال الشافعي له: إن المسح ركن في الوضوء فيسن تثليثه ،كالغسل، فنقول في المعارضة: المسح في الرأس فلا مسح يسن تثليثه كمسح الخف، فجعل الركنية علة للتثليث وقاس على غسل الأعضاء المفروضة، ونحن أثبتنا حكما مخالفا لما أثبته الشافعي محله، وهو عدم تثليث المسح بإثبات علة أخرى وهي المسح، وقسنا على الخف، فكما لايسن التثليث فيه لايسنّ في الرأس؛ لأن المسح الذي علة لعدم التثليث موجود فيهما. الأصل: أي المقيس عليه، وسميت بالمفارقة بأن يقول: عندي دليل يدلّ على أن العلة في المقيس عليه شيء آخر لم يوجد في الفرع وهي ثلاثة أقسام كلها مشروحة في المطولات. مثاله: ما إذا عللنا في بيع الحديد بأنه موزون قوبل بجنسه فلا يجوز بيعه متفاضلاً كالذهب والفضة، فيعارضه الشافعي الله بأن العلة في الأصل أي الذهب والفضة ليست ما قلت وهو اتحاد القدر مع الجنس بل هي الثمنية، وتلك لاتوجد في الحديد. باطل لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يثبت المعارض في مقابلة علة المستدلّ علة متعدية، كما إذا عللنا في حرمة بيع الجص بالجص متفاضلا بالكيل والجنس كالحنطة والشعير فيعارضه السائل ويثبت علة أخرى، وهي الاقتيات والاذخار، وهي متعدية توجد في غير الحنطة والشعير كالأرز والدخن ويقول تلك العلة لاتوجد في الجص، فلا يحرم البيع متفاضلاً، أو علة غير متعدّية كما أثبت الشافعي له في الذهب والفضة علة أخرى وهي الثمنية، وتلك غير متعدية لاتوجد إلا في الذهب والفضة، فعلى الثاني لا يصح تعليله في المعارضة. لعدم حكمه إذ حكم التعليل التعدية كما مرّ سابقاً، فإذا أثبت علة غير متعدّية يفسد التعليل لعدم حصول الغرض منه، وعلى الأول التعليل أيضاً فاسد، وإليه أشار بقوله: "ولفساده" وبين وجه الفساد بقوله: لأنه لا اتصال إلخ. والحاصل أن المعارضة لا تعلق لها بالمتنازع فيه إلا أنها تفيد عدم تلك العلة فيه، وعدم العلة لا يوجب عدم الحكم؛ إذ الحكم يثبت بعلل شتى، فبعد فساد تلك العلة تبقى علة أخرى وهي تكفي، ولما كان المعارضة في علة المستدل فاسداً عند الأكثر بين قاعدة بعد بيان تلك المعارضة؛ ليكون تلك المعارضة مقبولة إذا أوردت بهذه القاعدة فقال: وكل كلام إلخ.
The pure mu'arada in the cause of the original: And the second is in the cause of the original, and that is invalid due to lack of its ruling, and due to its corruption even if it benefits its transitivity; because there is no connection of this type of mu'arada to the point of dispute except that it negates that cause in it, and the absence of the cause does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. = The measured (al-maqis), and it has five divisions all mentioned in detail in the lengthy works. And when the author omitted mentioning them, it befits us to omit as well, valid because it involves establishing a ruling contrary to the first ruling by establishing another cause in that exact place. Example: if the Shafi'i says: 'Wiping (mash) is a pillar of wudu, so it is recommended to be done thrice like washing,' then in mu'arada we say: 'Wiping on the head, so wiping is not recommended to be done thrice like wiping on the khuff.' Thus he made being a pillar the cause for thrice, and analogized to washing the obligatory limbs. And we established a contrary ruling to what the Shafi'i established in that place, which is non-recommendation of thrice by establishing another cause, which is wiping, and we analogized to the khuff. So just as thrice is not recommended there, it is not recommended on the head; because the wiping which is the cause for non-recommendation exists in both. 'The original' means the one measured upon, and it is called 'mufaraqa' (differentiation), as in: I have a proof that the cause in the original is something else which is not found in the subsidiary, and it has three divisions all explained in the lengthy works. Example: if we argue in the sale of iron that it is weighed and meets its genus, so it is not permissible to sell it with disparity like gold and silver, then the Shafi'i objects that the cause in the original (gold and silver) is not what you said (unity of measure with genus) but rather being a medium of exchange (thimaniyya), and that is not found in iron. This is invalid because either the objector establishes in opposition to the proponent's cause a transitive cause, as if we argue in the prohibition of selling gypsum for gypsum with disparity by measure and genus like wheat and barley, then the objector objects and establishes another cause, which is being a staple and storage, which is transitive and found in things other than wheat and barley like rice and millet, and says that cause is not found in gypsum, so the sale with disparity is not prohibited; or a non-transitive cause as the Shafi'i established for gold and silver another cause which is thimaniyya, and that is non-transitive, not found except in gold and silver. In the second case, his ta'lil (causation) is not valid in mu'arada due to lack of its ruling, for the ruling of ta'lil is transitivity as previously. So if he establishes a non-transitive cause, the ta'lil is corrupted due to lack of achieving its purpose. In the first case, the ta'lil is also corrupt, and he alluded to that by saying: 'and due to its corruption' and explained the aspect of corruption by saying: 'because there is no connection etc.' The conclusion is that the mu'arada has no connection to the point of dispute except that it implies the absence of that cause in it, and the absence of the cause does not necessitate the absence of the ruling; for the ruling is established by various causes. So after the corruption of that cause, another cause remains, and it suffices. And since mu'arada in the cause of the proponent is invalid according to most, he laid down a rule after explaining that mu'arada, so that mu'arada becomes acceptable if brought with this rule, and he said: 'And every speech etc.'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage deals with the second type of pure mu'arada: that which targets the 'illa (cause) of the original (asl) rather than the ruling. The author declares this type invalid for two reasons: first, it does not have a ruling (i.e., it fails to produce a legal consequence), and second, even if it were transitive, it is corrupt. The reason is that such mu'arada only negates the specific 'illa in the subsidiary, but the absence of that 'illa does not entail the absence of the ruling because the ruling could be based on another 'illa. The author gives examples: a Shafi'i might argue that wiping (mash) is recommended thrice because it is a pillar, analogizing to washing. The Hanafi counters by citing wiping on khuff, which is not recommended thrice, using a different 'illa (the act of wiping itself). This is actually a valid mu'arada in the ruling, not in the cause? The author then moves to the invalid type: if someone argues that iron is like gold/silver (weighed and same genus) so disparity is prohibited, the Shafi'i might say the cause in gold/silver is thimaniyya, not measure, and this is not in iron. The author analyzes two possibilities: either the objector proposes a transitive 'illa (like staple/storage) or a non-transitive one (like thimaniyya). Both are invalid: the non-transitive because it doesn't transmit, and the transitive because even if 'illa exists in the original, its absence in the subsidiary does not disprove the ruling since the proponent's 'illa could still be valid. The author concludes that mu'arada in the 'illa is generally invalid because it fails to address the ruling directly.

Key Terms
العلة المتعدية (al-'illa al-muta'addiya): A transitive cause; one that can be found in other cases beyond the original.
العلة غير المتعدية (al-'illa ghayr al-muta'addiya): A non-transitive cause; one that is specific to the original and not found elsewhere.
المفارقة (al-mufaraqa): Differentiation; a form of mu'arada where the objector claims the cause in the original is different and not present in the subsidiary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is mu'arada in the cause of the original considered invalid according to this passage?
A) Because it establishes a new ruling that contradicts the original.
B) Because it only negates the presence of that cause but does not negate the ruling.
C) Because it uses a non-transitive cause.
D) Because it is only valid if the objector uses a transitive cause.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada that only challenges the existence of the cause without attacking the ruling is invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Mu'arada in the 'Illa of the Asl and the Rule of Mumana'a
Usul rule on invalid counter-arguments in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why mu'arada in the 'illa of the asl is invalid and apply the rule to convert mufaraqa into mumana'a in a qiyas argument.

Core Idea
Absence of a specific 'illa does not necessitate absence of the ruling; mu'arada in the asl's 'illa is invalid.

In Hanafi usul, when an opponent challenges a qiyas by proposing a different 'illa for the asl, this is called mu'arada in the 'illa of the asl. This passage explains why such a challenge is invalid and provides a practical rule: if the opponent's point is correct regarding the asl, it must be presented as mumana'a (preventing the analogy) rather than as mufaraqa (creating a distinction). Understanding this distinction is essential for properly rebutting counter-arguments in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Invalidity of Mu'arada in the 'Illa of the Asl
The passage states that this type of mu'arada is invalid because it lacks connection to the dispute: the absence of a specific 'illa does not prove the ruling is absent (the ruling can have multiple causes).
This is a key principle: rulings are not dependent on a single 'illa.
2
Identify the Rule for Converting Mufaraqa to Mumana'a
The author introduces a rule: any correct statement concerning the asl that is presented as mufaraqa (distinction) must be reformulated as mumana'a (prevention). This transformation makes the argument acceptable.
Mufaraqa is invalid because it assumes authority to create distinctions; mumana'a blocks the analogy instead.
3
Analyze the Example of Freeing a Mortgaged Slave
The example: the Hanafi analogizes freeing a mortgaged slave to selling it (both nullify the mortgagee's right). The opponent (Shafi'i) objects that freeing is unlike sale because it cannot be rescinded. This objection, if presented as mufaraqa, is invalid; it should be presented as mumana'a, i.e., showing that the common 'illa (nullification of right) does not apply to freeing because freeing is irreversible.
This illustrates the practical application of the rule.
4
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The Hanafi position: if the pledgor is insolvent, the freeing is invalid. The Shafi'i position may differ. The method of argumentation (mufaraqa vs. mumana'a) determines which position is accepted in debate.
The rule ensures that disputes are resolved systematically.

Source Text

باب القياس
فصل في المعارضة
المعارضة الخالصة في علة الأصل
والثاني في علة الأصل، وذلك باطل لعدم حكمه، ولفساده لو أفاد تعديته؛ لأنه لا اتصال له بموضع النزاع إلا من حيث أنه ينعدم تلك العلة فيه، وعدم العلة لا يوجب عدم الحكم، =
المقيس، ولها خمسة أقسام كلها مذكورة بالتفصيل في المطوّلات. ولما أعرض المصنف عن ذكرها فناسب لنا الإعراض صحيح لما فيه من إثبات حكم مخالف للحكم الأول بإثبات علة أخرى في ذلك المحل بعينه. مثاله ما إذا قال الشافعي: إن المسح ركن في الوضوء فيسن تثليثه، كالغسل، فنقول في المعارضة: المسح في الرأس فلا مسح يسن تثليثه كمسح الخف، فجعل الركنية علة للتثليث وقاس على غسل الأعضاء المفروضة، ونحن أثبتنا حكما مخالفا لما أثبته الشافعي محله، وهو عدم تثليث المسح بإثبات علة أخرى وهي المسح، وقسنا على الخف، فكما لايسن التثليث فيه لايسنّ في الرأس؛ لأن المسح الذي علة لعدم التثليث موجود فيهما. الأصل: أي المقيس عليه، وسميت بالمفارقة بأن يقول: عندي دليل يدلّ على أن العلة في المقيس عليه شيء آخر لم يوجد في الفرع وهي ثلاثة أقسام كلها مشروحة في المطولات. مثاله: ما إذا عللنا في بيع الحديد بأنه موزون قوبل بجنسه فلا يجوز بيعه متفاضلاً كالذهب والفضة، فيعارضه الشافعي بأن العلة في الأصل أي الذهب والفضة ليست ما قلت وهو اتحاد القدر مع الجنس بل هي الثمنية، وتلك لاتوجد في الحديد. باطل لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يثبت المعارض في مقابلة علة المستدلّ علة متعدية، كما إذا عللنا في حرمة بيع الجص بالجص متفاضلا بالكيل والجنس كالحنطة والشعير فيعارضه السائل ويثبت علة أخرى، وهي الاقتيات والاذخار، وهي متعدية توجد في غير الحنطة والشعير كالأرز والدخن ويقول تلك العلة لاتوجد في الجص، فلا يحرم البيع متفاضلاً، أو علة غير متعدّية كما أثبت الشافعي في الذهب والفضة علة أخرى وهي الثمنية، وتلك غير متعدية لاتوجد إلا في الذهب والفضة، فعلى الثاني لا يصح تعليله في المعارضة. لعدم حكمه إذ حكم التعليل التعدية كما مرّ سابقاً، فإذا أثبت علة غير متعدّية يفسد التعليل لعدم حصول الغرض منه، وعلى الأول التعليل أيضاً فاسد، وإليه أشار بقوله: "ولفساده" وبين وجه الفساد بقوله: لأنه لا اتصال إلخ. والحاصل أن المعارضة لا تعلق لها بالمتنازع فيه إلا أنها تفيد عدم تلك العلة فيه، وعدم العلة لا يوجب عدم الحكم؛ إذ الحكم يثبت بعلل شتى، فبعد فساد تلك العلة تبقى علة أخرى وهي تكفي، ولما كان المعارضة في علة المستدل فاسداً عند الأكثر بين قاعدة بعد بيان تلك المعارضة؛ ليكون تلك المعارضة مقبولة إذا أوردت بهذه القاعدة فقال: وكل كلام صحيح في الأصل يذكر على سبيل المفارقة فاذكره على سبيل الممانعة كقولهم في إعتاق الراهن؛ لأنه تصرف يلاقي حق المرتمن بالإبطال فكان مردوداً كالبيع، فقالوا: ليس هذا كالبيع؛ لأنه يحتمل الفسخ بخلاف العتق، والوجه فيه أن الأصل هو البيع ههنا أي توقف في الابتداء يقول: القياس لتعدية حكم الأصل دون تغيره، وحكم الأصل وقف ما يحتمل الرد إنما يكون والفسخ، وأنت في الفرع تبطل أصلاً ما لا يحتمل الفسخ. أي الإعتاق أي إبطالا كليا بعد الثبوت الأصل: أي في وضعه وأصل جوهره. سبيل المفارقة التي هي باطلة عند الأصوليين. سبيل الممانعة التي هي طريق مقبول عندهم، فحينئذ يخرج ذلك الكلام من حيز الفساد إلى حيز الصحة، ويكون مقبولاً بأصله ووصفه جميعاً. إعتاق الراهن عبده المرهون عند المرتمن أنه لا ينفذ إعتاقه إذا كان معسراً، ولهم قولان في الموسر كالبيع فكما لاينفذ بيع العبد المرهون لاينفذ إعتاقه والعلة المشتركة بينهما تصرف يلاقي حق المرتمن بالإبطال. فقالوا : في جوابه، اعلم أن المعارضة في علة الأصل سميت بالمفارقة؛ لأنه أتى السائل بعلة يقع بها الفرق بين الأصل والفرع، وهي فاسدة عند الأكثر، فمن جوّز تلك المفارقة منا قال في جوابه: ليس هذا إلخ. بخلاف العتق فإنه لا يحتمل الفسخ، فحصل الفرق بين البيع والعتق فعلة عدم جواز البيع هي كونه محتملاً للفسخ بعد وقوعه، وهذه العلة لاتوجد في الفرع أي الإعتاق فلايصح أن يقاس الإعتاق على البيع، فهذا الفرق في نفسه، لكنه لما جاء به السائل الذي ليس له ولاية الفرق فلايقبل منه فحقه أن يورده على سبيل الممانعة، ليكون مقبولاً ومسموعاً، وإليه أشار بقوله: والوجه فيه إلخ. صحيح ما لا يحتمل الفسخ والرد وهو الإعتاق، والحاصل لانسلّم أن قياسكم صحيح؛ لأن الأصل هو البيع، والفرع هو العتق، وحكم الأصل هو التوقف؛ لأن بيع الرهن موقوف على إجازة المرتهن لا أنه باطل وفاسد في نفسه، فهذا الحكم لا يوجد في الفرع، فإن العتق لا يتوقف على إجازة المرتمن ولا يحتمل الفسخ بعد وقوعه، فعلى قياسكم كان أن يثبت التوقف فيه ولكنكم لما أثبتم أن هذا الحكم فاسد في الفرع أثبتم حكماً آخر وهو البطلان، فقلتم: إن الفرع وهو العتق باطل، وهذا الحكم حكم جديد لم يتعد من الأصل، ومع البيع لأن ذلك الحكم لم يكن موجوداً فيه، فكيف تعدّى منه إلى الفرع، فهل هذا إلا تغيير حكم الأصل. ولما فرغ عن بيان المعارضة شرع في بيان دفعها. كونه: وإنما جعلنا علة عدم جواز البيع كونه محتملا للفسخ؛ لأن حق المرتمن فيه باق حيث يمنع البيع من بخلاف العتق، فإنه صدر من أهله في محلّه، ولا يمكن للمرتهن المنع من نفاذه
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Mu'arada. The second type is mu'arada in the 'illa of the asl, and that is invalid due to lack of its ruling, and due to its corruption if it were to cause transference; because it has no connection to the point of dispute except insofar as it negates that 'illa in it, and the absence of the 'illa does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. ... And every correct statement in the asl that is mentioned by way of mufaraqa, mention it by way of mumana'a, like their statement regarding the freeing of a slave by the pledgor: because it is an action that meets the right of the mortgagee by way of nullification, so it is rejected like a sale. They said: This is not like a sale; because it (sale) is subject to rescission unlike freeing. The explanation is that the asl is sale here, i.e., suspension in the beginning. The analogy is to transfer the ruling of the asl without changing it, and the ruling of the asl is suspension of what is subject to rejection and rescission, and you in the far' nullify absolutely what is not subject to rescission. ...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of mu'arada (counter-argument) in the 'illa of the asl (cause of the original case) within qiyas (analogy). The author explains that this type of mu'arada is invalid according to most jurists because it does not properly connect to the disputed point. The opponent tries to establish a different 'illa for the asl to break the analogy, but this is ineffective because the absence of a particular 'illa does not entail the absence of the ruling; the ruling can have multiple causes. The author then presents a key rule: when an opponent brings a valid point in the asl by way of mufaraqa (distinction), the respondent should convert it into mumana'a (prevention) to make it acceptable. This is illustrated with the example of a pledgor freeing a mortgaged slave. The Hanafi position is that such a freeing is not valid if the pledgor is insolvent, and it is analogized to sale of the slave (which is suspended). The opponent (Shafi'i) argues that freeing is not like sale because freeing cannot be rescinded. The author shows that this distinction, if presented as mufaraqa, is invalid because the opponent has no authority to make distinctions; instead, it should be presented as mumana'a, i.e., blocking the analogy by denying the common 'illa. The passage thus teaches the proper method of responding to mu'arada in qiyas.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'arada): A counter-argument in qiyas where the opponent challenges the 'illa or the analogy.
مفارقة (mufaraqa): An argument that distinguishes between the asl and far' by proposing a different 'illa for the asl, causing a differentiation.
ممانعة (mumana'a): An argument that prevents the analogy by showing that the common 'illa is absent or that the ruling cannot be transferred.
علة ('illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies the ruling in qiyas.
تعدية (ta'diya): The transference of the ruling from the asl to the far' via the 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should be done if an opponent presents a valid point in the asl by way of mufaraqa (distinction)?
A) Accept the distinction and abandon the analogy.
B) Convert the mufaraqa into mumana'a (prevention).
C) Reject the point as irrelevant.
D) Demand textual proof for the distinction.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, mu'arada in the 'illa of the asl is invalid; valid objections about the asl must be presented as mumana'a, not mufaraqa.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Mu'arada vs Mufaraqa: Presenting Valid Objections in Qiyas
Usul rule on opposing qiyas with mu'arada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mu'arada and mufaraqa in qiyas and apply the Hanafi method of presenting objections to analogies.

Core Idea
Mu'arada is a valid opposition in qiyas; mufaraqa is invalid—present differences as mu'arada to be accepted.

In Hanafi usul, when challenging an analogy (qiyas), the manner of objection matters. Simply pointing out a difference between the original case and the new case may be dismissed as mufaraqa. But if the difference is framed as a valid counter-argument (mu'arada), it becomes an accepted method to defeat the analogy. This passage walks through the classic example of freeing a pawned slave vs selling it, illustrating how to correctly oppose an analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Asl and Far'
In the example, the asl (original case) is the sale of a pawned slave; the far' (new case) is the freeing of a pawned slave by the pawner. The opponent argues both should have the same ruling.
The ruling of the asl is tawaqquf (suspension) on the mortgagee's permission.
2
Examine the Proposed Illa
The opponent claims the illa (cause) is 'a disposition that meets the mortgagee's right with annulment'. This illa would apply to both sale and freeing.
The Hanafi rebuttal begins by questioning the validity of this illa.
3
Understand the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response explains that the illa for sale is its susceptibility to rescission (i.e., the sale can be reversed). Freeing, however, does not admit rescission. Therefore, the illa of the asl does not exist in the far', so the analogy fails.
The ruling for freeing becomes nullity (butlan) instead of suspension, a new ruling.
4
Distinguish Mu'arada from Mufaraqa
The opponent's objection, if phrased as a pure difference (mufaraqa), is rejected. But if presented as mu'arada—showing a valid opposition to the cause—it is accepted. The text emphasizes this procedural point.
Mu'arada is a valid method because it does not break the analogy but contests the cause.
5
Apply the Principle
When you encounter a qiyas argument from another school, first identify the asl, far', and claimed illa. Then check if the illa truly applies. If not, raise the objection as mu'arada, citing the absence of the illa in the far'.
This method preserves the structure of qiyas while showing why it fails.

Section on Opposition. And every correct statement about the original case that is mentioned as a distinction (mufaraqa) should be mentioned as an opposition (mu'arada). Like their statement regarding the freeing by the pawner: because it is a transaction that meets the right of the mortgagee with annulment, so it is rejected, like sale. That is, the followers of al-Shafi'i. That is, the freeing by the pawner. Like sale. Then they said: This is not like sale because it admits rescission unlike freeing. And the point therein is that (the freeing). (the sale). And it is the sale here, that is, suspension. In the beginning. He says: Analogy is to extend the ruling of the original without changing it, and the ruling of the original is suspension of what admits rejection and rescission, while you in the branch annul something that does not admit rescission. That is, the freeing, that is, total annulment after confirmation. The original, that is, in its position and its essence. The path of mufaraqa is invalid according to the usulis. The path of mu'arada is an accepted method with them. Then that statement exits from the realm of invalidity to validity, and becomes accepted in its essence and description. Freeing a pawned slave by the pawner - according to the mortgagee, his freeing is not effective if he is insolvent, and they have two opinions regarding the solvent one. Like sale, just as the sale of a pawned slave is not effective, his freeing is not effective, and the common cause between them is a transaction that meets the right of the mortgagee with annulment. Then they said in response: Know that the opposition in the cause of the original is called mufaraqa because the questioner brings a cause by which a difference occurs between the original and the branch, and it is invalid according to the majority. So whoever among us permits that mufaraqa said in response: This is not like sale, etc. Unlike freeing, for it does not admit rescission. Thus a difference occurs between sale and freeing. So the cause for the impermissibility of sale is that it admits rescission after its occurrence, and this cause does not exist in the branch, i.e., the freeing. So it is not valid to analogize freeing to sale. So this difference is in itself, but since it was brought by the questioner who has no authority for differentiation, it is not accepted from him. His right is to present it as mu'arada so that it becomes accepted and heard. And to this he pointed with his saying: and the point therein, etc. Correct. That which does not admit rescission and rejection, i.e., freeing. And the sum: We do not concede that your analogy is correct because the original is sale, and the branch is freeing, and the ruling of the original is suspension, because the sale of a pawn is suspended upon the mortgagee's permission, not that it is invalid and corrupt in itself. So this ruling does not exist in the branch, for freeing is not suspended upon the mortgagee's permission and does not admit rescission after its occurrence. So according to your analogy, suspension should have been established in it, but since you established that this ruling is corrupt in the branch, you established another ruling, which is nullity, so you said the branch, i.e., freeing, is null. This is a new ruling not transmitted from the original, despite the sale, because that ruling did not exist in it. So how was it transmitted from it to the branch? Is this not a change of the original ruling? When he finished explaining mu'arada, he began explaining its rebuttal. KON: And we only made the cause for impermissibility of sale its being susceptible to rescission because the right of the mortgagee remains in it, as it prevents sale, unlike freeing, for it issues from its proper subject in its proper place, and the mortgagee cannot prevent its effectiveness.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule on how to respond to an objection in qiyas. The author explains that when an opponent raises a difference between the original case (asl) and the new case (far') that breaks the analogy, the correct way is to present it as mu'arada (opposition) rather than mufaraqa (separation). Mufaraqa is invalid according to most usulis, but mu'arada is a valid method. The example given is the case of a pawner (raahin) freeing a pawned slave. The opponent (apparently Shafi'i) argues that freeing is like selling a pawned slave in that both are dispositions that nullify the mortgagee's right, so both should be invalid. The Hanafi response is that this analogy fails because sale admits rescission (i.e., can be reversed), while freeing does not. The ruling for sale of a pawned slave is suspension (tawaqquf) - it is not entirely invalid but hangs on the mortgagee's permission. For freeing, however, there is no possibility of rescission, so the ruling cannot be suspension; it is either valid or invalid. In the case of an insolvent pawner, it is invalid (butlan). Since the ruling of the original (suspension) does not apply to the branch, the analogy is not sound. The author emphasizes that the opponent should present this objection as mu'arada to be accepted. The section then transitions to explaining how to rebut such opposition.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'arada): Presenting an objection that shows a difference between the original and branch, but as a valid opposition to the analogy, not as a separation (mufaraqa). It is an accepted method in usul.
مفارقة (mufaraqa): A statement that distinguishes the original from the branch by introducing a difference that invalidates the analogy; considered invalid by most usulis.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension; the ruling that a contract (like sale of a pawned slave) is suspended upon the mortgagee's permission, not immediately effective nor entirely void.
بطلان (butlan): Nullity; the ruling that an act is entirely invalid and produces no legal effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of freeing a pawned slave, what is the ruling for the sale of a pawned slave according to the Hanafi position?
A) It is completely void (bāṭil) from the start.
B) It is suspended (mawqūf) upon the mortgagee's permission.
C) It is valid and enforceable immediately.
D) It is valid only if the pawner is solvent.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada is the valid method to oppose a qiyas by showing the absence of the illa in the far'; mufaraqa (mere distinction) is not accepted.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
The Principle of Tarjih: Preponderance by Quality, Not Quantity
Defines tarjih and explains how preponderance works among conflicting evidences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct basis for tarjih between conflicting evidences and apply the rule that preponderance is by intrinsic quality (wasf) not by accumulation of evidence.

Core Idea
Tarjih is by a quality within the evidence itself, not by adding more evidences.

When two evidences conflict, how do we decide which to follow? The Hanafi method is not to count how many evidences each side has, but to look for a quality (wasf) within the evidence that makes it stronger. This lesson unpacks the principle of tarjih and its application to qiyas, Quran, hadith, and even a practical fiqh example of blood money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict (ta'arud)
Recognize that two valid evidences appear to contradict each other. This triggers the need for tarjih.
If there is no conflict, tarjih is not required.
2
Recall the definition of tarjih
Tarjih is making one evidence preponderant by a quality (wasf) within it, not by an external independent proof.
The passage emphasizes 'by a quality' – not by another evidence.
3
Examine the possible qualities
Look for intrinsic strengths: decisiveness (qat'i vs. zanni), fame (mashhur vs. ahad), strength of cause in qiyas, etc.
Examples: muhkam qat'i over zanni, mashhur over khabar wahid, sound istihsan over weak qiyas.
4
Apply the principle to the example
In the wound example, multiple wounds do not create preponderance because each wound is a complete cause; quantity does not add quality.
This illustrates that tarjih is not about counting but about intrinsic strength.
5
Derive the operative rule
Whenever two evidences conflict, the one with a stronger intrinsic quality (wasf) is given preponderance and followed.
If neither has a distinguishing quality, other methods like tasqit (dropping both) may be used.

Section on Preponderance. Section on Preponderance. And when opposition occurs, the way is preponderance (tarjih). It is the superiority of one of the two similars over the other by a quality (wasf). So they said: A qiyas is not given preponderance by another qiyas, and likewise the Book and the Sunnah. Rather, some are given preponderance over others by a strength within it. And likewise, the owner of multiple wounds is not given preponderance over the owner of a single wound. (Commentary) Correct. In it, i.e., opposition, and the masculine pronoun refers to the source. Tarjih: i.e., making one of the two opposing things preponderant such that the opposition is repelled. If the arguer brings preponderance, the opposition of the questioner is repelled and the claim of the arguer is established without issue. If he does not bring it, he becomes cut off, and the questioner may oppose him with another preponderance. 'Expression of superiority etc.' For if it is said: superiority of one of two similars over the other is itself preponderance (rujhan), not tarjih (making preponderant), as is clear, so how is tarjih interpreted as rujhan? The first is the source and the second is the result. I say: The statement can be directed in two ways: first, by ellipsis of the genitive construct from 'superiority of one of two similars', so the meaning is 'expression of superiority of one over the other'. Second, by taking tarjih to mean rujhan, so the meaning is 'it, i.e., rujhan, is expression of...' And his saying 'by a quality' means that the thing by which preponderance occurs is not an independent evidence but a meaning within the evidence. 'By another qiyas' i.e., a third qiyas that supports it, because then on one side there would be one qiyas and on the other side two qiyases. Just as the testimony of four is not given preponderance over the testimony of two witnesses, because the basis of tarjih is an additional quality, such that the testimony of a just person is given preponderance over a sinful one, not by independent increase. So if a qiyas were given preponderance by another qiyas joining it, this would be necessary. But if one of the two qiyases is strong and the other weak, then the strong one is given preponderance over the weak by the quality of strength. 'The Book and the Sunnah' i.e., a verse is not given preponderance by a third verse supporting it, and likewise a hadith is not given preponderance over a conflicting hadith by a third hadith supporting it. Rather, preponderance is by a strength within it. Thus, sound istihsan is given precedence over clear qiyas that is corrupt in effect, and the Book that is decisive (muhkam qat'i) is given precedence over what is speculative (zanni), and the well-known hadith (mashhur) is given precedence over the solitary report (khabar wahid). 'The owner of multiple wounds etc.' For if a man inflicts a single wound on a person that is potentially fatal by mistake, and another inflicts multiple wounds also potentially fatal, and the person dies from them, then the blood money is on both their 'aqilas equally. The owner of multiple wounds is not given preponderance over the owner of a single wound by making his blood money full or extra, because each of his wounds is a complete cause that is suitable to oppose the wound of the single wound owner, so it is not a quality, so preponderance does not occur by it. Yes, if the wound of one of them=
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage defines tarjih (preponderance) in usul al-fiqh. When two evidences conflict (mu'arada), the method to resolve is tarjih. Tarjih is not just any superiority but giving preference by a quality (wasf) inherent in the evidence, not by bringing another independent evidence. The author clarifies that a qiyas cannot be preponderated by another separate qiyas, similarly the Quranic verses and hadiths are not preponderated by additional verses or hadiths. Preponderance is by a strength within the evidence itself, e.g., the strength of being decisive (qat'i) over speculative (zanni), or the fame of a hadith (mashhur) over a solitary report. The example of wounds illustrates: if two people cause fatal wounds, one with a single wound and one with multiple, the blood money is equal because each wound is a complete cause; the multiplicity does not give preponderance because it is not a qualitative difference but a quantitative one. The exception is if one wound is qualitatively stronger (e.g., more severe). The commentary also addresses a linguistic point: tarjih (making preponderant) and rujhan (being preponderant) are related; the definition uses 'superiority' to mean the result of preponderance. The passage establishes the principle that tarjih depends on qualitative strength within the evidence, not external accumulation.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving preponderance to one of two conflicting evidences by a quality (wasf) within the evidence, not by an independent proof.
وصف (wasf): A quality inherent in the evidence that gives it strength, such as decisiveness, fame, justice of narrator, etc.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; in this context, a qiyas is not preponderated by another qiyas, but by a quality like strength of the cause.
جراحات (jurahat): Wounds; the example shows that multiple wounds do not preponderate over a single wound in blood money because each wound is a complete cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the owner of multiple wounds not given preponderance over the owner of a single wound in the blood money example?
A) Because multiple wounds are less likely to be fatal.
B) Because each wound is a complete cause, so no qualitative difference exists.
C) Because the single wound was inflicted intentionally.
D) Because blood money is fixed and cannot be increased.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih is determined by intrinsic quality (wasf) within the evidence, not by the number of evidences.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Definition and Rules of Tarjih (Preponderance)
Explaining the definition of tarjih and the rule that preponderance is by an inherent strength not by adding independent evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarjih according to Hanafi usul and distinguish between preponderance by inherent description versus by independent evidence.

Core Idea
Tarjih is by a description within the evidence, not by adding more evidence.

This passage explains the concept of tarjih (preponderance) when two evidences conflict. The key principle is that preponderance is achieved by an inherent quality of the evidence itself, such as strength of transmission or clarity, and not by the sheer number of evidences. The author supports this with analogies and then addresses a dispute among scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the occasion for tarjih
Recognize that tarjih is needed when two evidences (adillah) are in opposition (ta'āruḍ) and are equal in strength otherwise.
2
Define tarjih as preference by a description
Tarjih is defined as preferring one of two similar evidences over the other by a description (waṣf) that inheres in the evidence itself, not by an independent proof.
The waṣf is a quality like strength of transmission (qawwat al-athar) or decisiveness (qaṭ'ī).
3
Apply the rule to examples
Consider the examples given: a qiyas is not preponderated by another qiyas; a verse is not preponderated by another verse; multiple wounds do not preponderate over a single wound because each wound is an independent cause.
Each independent cause opposes the other, so they cancel out; no waṣf appears.
4
Examine the dispute on multiple independent evidences
Some scholars (including some Hanafis and Shafi'is) argue that a third independent evidence can tip the balance. Understand their reasoning: two evidences on one side cancel one opponent, leaving the third unopposed.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjih
The majority Hanafi position is that an independent evidence remains independent and cannot become a waṣf; it only adds to the opposition. Therefore, multiplicity does not preponderate. The text declares this the sounder view (هذا هو الصحيح).
The analogy with witnesses: four witnesses do not preponderate over two; each wound is a complete cause.

باب القياس
فصل في الترجيح
فصل في الترجيح
وإذا قامت المعارضة كان السبيل فيه الترجيح، وهو عبارة عن فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر وصفاً، حتى قالوا: إن القياس لا يترجّح بقياس آخر، وكذلك الكتاب والسنة، وإنما يترجّح البعض على البعض بقوة فيه، وكذلك صاحب الجراحات لا يترجّح على صاحب جراحة واحدة.
:
يصح
فيه : أي المعارضة، وضمير المذكر باعتبار المصدر. الترجيح : أي ترجيح أحد المعارضين على الآخر بحيث تندفع المعارضة، فإن أتى المستدلّ بالترجيح تندفع بمعارضة السائل ويثبت دعوى المستدل بلا مرة، فإن لم يأت به صار منقطعاً، وللسائل أن يعارضه بترجيح آخر. عبارة عن فضل إلخ : فإن قيل : فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر رجحان وليس بترجيح كما لا يخفى، فكيف تفسير الترجيح بالرجحان؟ فإن الأول هو المصدر والثاني هو الحاصل بالمصدر أقول: توجيه الكلام على وجهين، الأول على حذف المضاف من فضل أحد المثلين فتقدير الكلام هو عبارة عن بيان فضل أحد المثلين على الآخر، والثاني المراد من الترجيح الرجحان، فتقدير الكلام وهو أي الرجحان عبارة الخ، ومعنى قوله: "وصفا" أن لا يكون ذلك الشيء الذي يقع به الترجيح دليلاً مستقلا بل معنى في الدليل. بقياس :آخر ثالث يؤيده فإنه يكون حينئذ في جانب قياس وفي جانب آخر قياسان، كما لا يترجح شهادة أربعة على شهادة شاهدين؛ لأن مدار الترجيح على وصف زائد حتى يترجّح شهادة عادل على شهادة فاسق لا على زيادة مستقلة، فلو ترجّح قياس بانضمام قياس آخر إليه يلزم هذا نعم لو كان أحد القياسين قويا والآخر ضعيفاً فحينئذ يترجّح القوي على الضعيف بزيادة وصف القوة. الكتاب والسنة حتى لا يترجّح على آية بآية ثالثة تؤيدها، وكذلك الحديث لا يترجح على حديث يعارضه بحديث ثالث يؤيده بقوة فيه فيكون الاستحسان الصحيح الأثر مقدما على القياس الجلي الفاسد الأثر، والكتاب الذي هو محكم قطعي مقدّما على ما هو ظني، والحديث المشهور مقدما على الخبر الواحد. صاحب الجراحات لايترجّح إلخ: فإن جرح رجل رجلا جراحةً واحدةً صالحة للقتل خطاً، وجرحه آخر جراحات متعددة كذلك ومات من ذلك كانت الدية على عاقلتهما سواء، ولا يرجح صاحب الجراحات المتعددة على صاحب جراحة واحدة بأن يجعل ديته كاملة أو زائدة على ديته؛ لأن كل جراحة من جراحاته علة تامة تصلح معارضة لجراحة صاحب الواحدة، فلم يكن وصفاً، فلايقع بها الترجيح. نعم لو كانت جراحة أحدهما=
أقسام المعنى الذي يقع به الترجيح]
والذي يقع به الترجيح أربعة : الترجيح بقوة الأثر ؛ لأن الأثر معنى في الحجة، فمهما

الأول
قوي كان أولى لفضل في وصف الحجة على مثال الاستحسان في معارضة القياس،
الأثر الاحتجاج به

الثاني
أي ثبات الوصف
: أقوى من الآخر ينسب الموت إليه بأن قطع واحد يد رجل والآخر جز رقبته، فكان القاتل هو الجاز؛ إذ لا يتصوّر البقاء بدون الرقبة بخلاف اليد فحينئذ يصح الترجيح.
ف: اعلم - أرشدك الله تعالى - هذا ما ذهب إليه أكثر الأصوليين من أنه لا يصح الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة، وذهب بعض أهل النظر من أصحابنا وبعض أصحاب الشافعي إلى أنه صحيح؛ لأن الدليل الواحد لا يعارض إلا دليلا واحداً من جنسه فيتساقطان بالتعارض، فيبقى الدليل الآخر سالماً عن المعارضة، فيصح به الترجيح، ولأن المقصود من الترجيح قوة الظن في الدليل الذي عاضده دليل آخر مثله في إثبات الحكم، فيترجح على الآخر بلا مزيّة، ودليل الفريق الأول هو أن الشيء إنما يتقوّى بصفة توجد في ذاته لا بانضمام مثله إليه كما ترى في المحسوسات، وهذا لأن الوصف لا يتقوم بنفسه، فلا يوجد إلا تبعاً لغيره، فيتقوّى به الموصوف الذي قام به هذا الوصف، وأما الدليل الذي مستقل بنفسه فلايوجد في غيره حتى يقوى به الغير، فيكون كل واحد معارضاً للدليل الذي أوجب الحكم على خلافه، فيتساقط الكل بالتعارض. ف اختلف العلماء فقال بعضهم: إذا تعارض نصان ترجّح أحدهما بالقياس؛ لأن القياس غير معتبر في مقابلة النص، فكان بمنزلة الوصف للنص الذي يوافقه وتابعاً له فيصلح مرجّحاً، وقال الآخرون: لايصح، وهذا هو الصحيح؛ لأن القياس وإن لم يعتبر في مقابلة النص ولكنه دليل مستقل بنفسه لا يوجد في غيره كالأوصاف، والترجيح إنما يقع بها كما علمت آنفاً. الترجيح أي ترجيح أحد القياسين على الآخر على وجه معنى في الحجة لا أمر مستقل بنفسه لا توجد تبعاً لغيره. وصف الحجة وصف الحجة هو الأثر، فلما قوي حصل فيه فضل وزيادة وهي القوة في معارضة القياس فإنه إذا يكون الأثر في الاستحسان أقوى يرجح* على القياس وإن كان مؤثرا، وكذا عكسه.
الصحة.
يرجح: فإن قيل: فعلى هذا يلزم أن يكون الشاهد الأعدل راجحاً على العادل؛ لأن أثره قوي، فيقال: إنا لا نسلم الاختلاف بعدالته بالزيادة والنقصان فليس لها أنواع متفاوتة بعضها فوق بعض؛ لأنها أمر مضبوط لا يتعدّد، وهو الاجتناب عن الكبائر وعدم الإصرار على الصغائر.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Tarjih. Section on Tarjih. When opposition occurs, the course therein is tarjih, which is the preference of one of the two similar things over the other by a description. So they said: A qiyas is not given preponderance by another qiyas, and likewise the Book and the Sunnah, rather some are given preponderance over others by strength within [the evidence]. Likewise, the one with multiple wounds is not given preponderance over one with a single wound. ...
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the principle of tarjih (preponderance) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by defining tarjih as preferring one of two conflicting evidences over the other by means of an inherent description (wasf), not by an independent evidence. The key rule is that preponderance is achieved by an intrinsic quality (like strength of transmission, clarity, or reliability) and not by adding another independent evidence. Examples illustrate: a qiyas is not preponderated by a second qiyas supporting it; a verse is not preponderated by another verse; multiple wounds do not preponderate over a single wound in diyah because each wound is an independent cause that opposes the other. The author then introduces the four types of tarjih (by strength of effect, by strength of its persistence, etc.) and discusses a dispute: whether an additional independent evidence can serve as a preponderator. The majority of usul scholars (including most Hanafis) say no, because tarjih is by a description within the evidence, not by an external independent proof. Some scholars (including some Hanafis and Shafi'is) accept it, arguing that a supporting evidence strengthens probability. The author sides with the majority, stating that an independent evidence remains in opposition and cancels out, so it cannot preponderate. The discussion ends with a clarification about the equality of witnesses in 'adalah (uprightness) — since 'adalah is a single quality, one witness cannot be preponderated over another by degree of 'adalah.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The preference of one of two conflicting evidences over the other by an inherent description (wasf).
الأثر (al-athar): The effect or strength of the evidence that serves as the description (wasf) for tarjih.
الوصف (al-wasf): The description or quality inherent in the evidence that gives preponderance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a person who inflicted multiple wounds not preponderate over a person who inflicted a single wound in diyah liability?
A) Because the multiple wounds are independent causes each opposing the single wound, so they are not a description (wasf) that can preponderate.
B) Because the multiple wounds are weaker than the single wound.
C) Because the single wound is more severe.
D) Because diyah is divided equally regardless of number of wounds.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih is by an inherent description (wasf), not by the number of evidences; an independent evidence cannot preponderate because it remains in opposition.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
The Four Means of Preferencing in Qiyas (Tarjih)
Lists four means of tarjih and debates two types of abundance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four means of tarjih in qiyas according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the dispute over tarjih by abundance of proofs versus abundance of usul.

Core Idea
Tarjih in qiyas occurs through strength of effect, stability, abundance of usul, or the ruling itself — but abundance of mere proofs does not strengthen an analogy.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul work, the author delineates four means by which one analogy can be preferred over another when they appear to conflict. This is a critical skill for the mufti and mujtahid, as it resolves apparent contradictions between analogical arguments. The text then delves into a key debate: whether the sheer number of supporting proofs can tip the scales. Both sides are presented, and the preferred Hanafi position is that an intrinsic quality within the evidence must be the basis for preferencing, not mere multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four means of tarjih
Locate the four categories listed: (1) strength of the effect (quwwat al-athar), (2) strength of stability (quwwat al-thubat), (3) abundance of usul (kathrat al-usul), and (4) the ruling testified to (al-hukm al-mashhud bihi). Note how the author introduces each.
The fourth is mentioned briefly; the passage focuses on the first three.
2
Analyze the dispute on tarjih by abundance of proofs
Read the section beginning 'ف: اعلم' where the author states the majority view and then presents an opposing view. Identify the two arguments: the majority says a thing is only strengthened by an intrinsic attribute, not by adding similar independent proofs; the opponents say multiple proofs leave one proof unopposed and strengthen speculation.
This is a rationalist debate (dalil aqli) about the nature of proofs.
3
Understand tarjih by abundance of usul
Examine the example of wiping the head in wudu. The author uses three usul (tayammum, khuff, splints) to support the view that wiping is not repeated, against the Shafi'i argument from ghusl. Note that this is tarjih by abundance of analogical origins, not by number of proofs.
Abundance of usul is accepted by most scholars, unlike abundance of proofs.
4
Distinguish between proofs and usul
The passage contrasts kathrat al-adilla (abundance of proofs) with kathrat al-usul (abundance of origins). The former is rejected, the latter accepted by the majority. Understand that usul are concrete analogical bases, while proofs are independent rational arguments. The Hanafi position is that each usul adds weight to the attribute, not to the proof itself.
This distinction is crucial for accurate application of tarjih.

أركان الصلاة تمامها بالإكمال دون أي الشافعية التكرار، فأما أثر المسح في التخفيف فلازم في كل ما لا يعقل تطهيراً كالتيمم ونحوه. والترجيح بكثرة الأصول؛ لأن كثرة الأصول زيادة لزوم الحكم معه، الثالث مسح عدم الحكم المشهود به بأن يكون وصف أحد القياسين ألزم للحكم المتعلق به من وصف القياس الآخر. إنه مسح فلايسنّ تكراره فالحكم المشهود به هنا عدم تكرار المسح وعلته المسح فهذا الوصف ألزم لإثبات هذا الحكم. أثبت له زيادة تأثير كالتيمم ونحوه والحاصل أن أصحاب الشافعي له يقولون: يُسنّ تكرار الرأس، وعندنا لايسن، فجعل أصحاب الشافعي علة التكرار الركنية، ونحن جعلنا علة التكرار الذي هو التخفيف المسح، فنحن نقول لهم: وصفكم وهو الركنية ليس بألزم لهذا الحكم وهو التكرار؛ لأن هذا الوصف عام يشمل أركان الوضوء والصلاة وغيرهما، وهي لا توجب سنية التكرار في غير الوضوء، بل من قضية الركن في الصلاة إتمامه بالإكمال دون التكرار حتى لم يشرع تكرار القيام والركوع والسجود للإكمال، وأما السجدة فتكرارها ليس من باب التكميل بل كل سجدة ركن عليحدة حتى لايجوز الصلاة. ترى في التيمم الخف والجبائر فصار وصف المسح ألزم للحكم المذكور، واحترز بقوله في كل ما لا يعقل تطهيرا" عن ومسح الاستنجاء بغير الماء، فإنه مسح شرع فيه التكرار إذ إزالة النجاسة بتكرار مسح الحجارة معقول. بكثرة الأصول: بأن يشهد لأحد الوصفين أصل واحد وللآخر أصلان، أو أصول كوصف المسح في مسألة التثليث، فإنه يشهد بصحته أصول ثلاثة مثل مسح الخف والجبيرة ،والتيمم، ولم يشهد لوصف الخصم وهو الركنية إلا أصل واحد وهو الغسل فحينئذ يترجّح وصفنا عليه والمراد بالأصل المقيس عليه كما علمت من المثال، فهذا القسم من الترجيح عند الجمهور صحيح. معه أي مع الوصف؛ لأن الحجة هي الوصف لا الأصل المستنبط منه، لكن كثرة الأصول توجب زيادة تأكيد ولزوم الحكم بذلك الوصف من وجه آخر غير ما ذكرنا من شدة التأثير والثبات على الحكم، فيحدث بها قوة في نفس الوصف، فلذلك صلحت للترجيح، وقال بعض أصحابنا وبعض أصحاب الشافعي له: إن الترجيح بكثرة الأصول غير صحيح؛ لأن كثرة الأصول في القياس بمنزلة كثرة الرواة في الخبر، والخبر لاترجح بكثرة الرواة على ما مرّ فكذا هذا، أو لأنه من جنس الترجيح بكثرة العلة؛ إذ شهادة كل أصل بمنزلة شهادة كل علة عليحدة، فيكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية أو كثرة وجه الشبه لشيء، فإن هذه كلها لاتصلح للترجيح.
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Tarjih. Categories of the meaning by which tarjih occurs. That by which tarjih occurs is four: First: Tarjih by strength of the effect, because the effect is a meaning in the evidence, so whenever it is strong it is more deserving due to superiority in the attribute of the evidence, like the example of istihsan in opposing qiyas. Second: Tarjih by strength of its stability [i.e., the stability of the attribute]. Someone stronger than another is attributed to death: one cut the hand of a man and another severed his neck, so the killer is the one who severed, because remaining without a neck is inconceivable unlike the hand, so here tarjih is valid. Then know—may Allah guide you—this is what most usul scholars held: that tarjih by abundance of proofs is not valid. Some of the theoreticians among our [Hanafi] scholars and some of al-Shafi'i's scholars held that it is valid, because a single proof does not oppose except a single proof of its kind, so they both fall due to opposition, leaving the other proof free from opposition, so tarjih is valid. And because the purpose of tarjih is strength of speculation in the proof that is supported by another similar proof in establishing the ruling, so it is preferred over the other without any superiority. The proof of the first group is that a thing is only strengthened by an attribute that exists in its essence, not by the addition of something similar to it, as you see in tangible things. This is because the attribute does not subsist by itself, so it only exists as dependent on something else, so the described thing that bears this attribute is strengthened by it. As for the proof that is independent by itself, it does not exist in something else so that the other is strengthened by it, so each one opposes the proof that necessitates the ruling contrary to it, so all fall due to opposition. Some scholars disagreed: when two texts oppose each other, one is preferred by analogy, because analogy is not considered in the face of text, so it is like an attribute of the text that agrees with it and a follower to it, so it is suitable as a preferrer. Others said: it is not valid, and this is the correct view, because analogy, even if not considered in the face of text, is an independent proof by itself, it does not exist in something else like attributes, and tarjih only occurs by them as you learned earlier. Tarjih means preferring one of two analogies over the other, as a meaning in the evidence, not an independent matter that does not exist as dependent on something else. The attribute of the evidence is the effect, so when it strengthens, a superiority and increase occurs, that is strength in opposing qiyas, because if the effect in istihsan is stronger, it is preferred over qiyas even if [qiyas] is effective, and likewise the opposite. If it is said: thus it would follow that the more just witness is preferred over the just one, because his effect is strong; we say: we do not concede that justice varies in increase and decrease, so it has no types some above others, because it is a defined matter that does not multiply, namely avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins. Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Tarjih. The ruling testified to: like our saying regarding wiping the head: it is wiping, because it is established in indicating leniency; their saying: it is a pillar in indicating repetition. For the pillars of prayer are completed by completion without repetition. As for the effect of wiping in leniency, it is necessary in everything that is not understood as purification, like tayammum and the like. Third: Tarjih by abundance of usul, because abundance of usul increases the obligation of the ruling with it. [Regarding] the ruling testified to: the attribute of one of the two analogies is more binding for the ruling related to it than the attribute of the other analogy. 'It is wiping, so its repetition is not sunna.' So the ruling testified to here is the non-repetition of wiping, and its cause is wiping, so this attribute is more binding to establish this ruling. It gave it increased effect like tayammum and the like. In summary, al-Shafi'i's scholars say: repetition of the head is sunna, while in our [Hanafi] view it is not sunna. So al-Shafi'i's scholars made the cause of repetition the pillar-ness, while we made the cause of non-repetition the leniency of wiping. So we say to them: your attribute—pillar-ness—is not more binding for this ruling—repetition—because this attribute is general, including the pillars of wudu, prayer, etc., which do not necessitate the sunna of repetition in other than wudu. Rather, the requirement of the pillar in prayer is its completion by completion without repetition, so repetition of standing, bowing, and prostration for completion is not prescribed. As for the sajdah, its repetition is not from the chapter of completion, rather each sajdah is a separate pillar such that prayer is not valid [without it]. You see in tayammum, the khuff, and splints, so the attribute of wiping became more binding for the mentioned ruling. And he cautions by his saying 'in everything not understood as purification' excluding wiping in istinja' with other than water, for that is wiping for which repetition is prescribed, because the removal of impurity by repeated wiping with stones is understood. [Tarjih] by abundance of usul: that one of the two attributes is supported by one asl, and the other by two or more usul. Like the attribute of wiping in the issue of tathlith (threefold), for it is supported by three usul: wiping over the khuff, the splint, and tayammum; while the opponent's attribute—pillar-ness—was supported by only one asl, namely ghusl. Therefore our attribute is preferred over his. And what is meant by asl is the maqis 'alayhi, as you know from the example. This type of tarjih is valid according to the majority. 'With it' meaning with the attribute, because the evidence is the attribute, not the asl derived from it. However, abundance of usul produces increased confirmation and obligation of the ruling by that attribute from another aspect besides what we mentioned of strength of effect and stability upon the ruling, so it creates strength in the attribute itself, therefore it is suitable for tarjih. Some of our scholars and some of al-Shafi'i's scholars said: tarjih by abundance of usul is not valid, because abundance of usul in qiyas is like abundance of narrators in a report, and a report is not preferred by abundance of narrators as previously mentioned; or because it is of the type of tarjih by abundance of cause, since the testimony of each asl is like the testimony of each cause separately, so this falls under abundance of analogical proofs or abundance of aspect of similarity for something, and these are all not suitable for tarjih.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work discusses the means by which one analogy (qiyas) can be preferred over another, a process called tarjih. The author states that tarjih occurs through four means: (1) strength of the effect (quwwat al-athar), (2) strength of stability (quwwat al-thubat), (3) abundance of usul (kathrat al-usul), and (4) something about the ruling testified to (al-hukm al-mashhud bihi). The passage then focuses on the first two and includes a significant dispute about whether tarjih can be done by abundance of proofs (kathrat al-adilla). The preferred view is that it cannot, because a proof is only strengthened by an intrinsic quality, not by the addition of similar proofs. However, some scholars, including some Hanafis and Shafi'is, disagree. The passage then gives an example for tarjih by stability: if one person cuts a hand and another severs the neck, the latter is the killer because life cannot continue without the neck. The third means, tarjih by abundance of usul, is illustrated with the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over repeating the wiping of the head in wudu. Hanafis hold that wiping is for leniency, so it is not repeated, while Shafi'is consider it a pillar and thus it is repeated. The Hanafi argument uses several analogical origins: wiping over khuffs, splints, and tayammum all support non-repetition, whereas the Shafi'i reliance on ghusl as an origin is insufficient. The passage ends by noting that some scholars reject tarjih by abundance of usul, comparing it to rejecting tarjih by abundance of narrators.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preferencing one analogy over another based on criteria such as strength of effect, stability, or abundance of origins
الأثر (al-athar): The effect or impact of a legal attribute in the evidence; strength of effect indicates greater suitability for tarjih
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-usul): Abundance of analogical origins (usul) supporting a particular attribute; one attribute supported by more origins is preferred

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi usul scholars, which of the following is a valid basis for preferencing (tarjih) between two analogies?
A) Abundance of independent proofs (kathrat al-adilla)
B) Strength of effect (quwwat al-athar)
C) Abundance of narrators in a hadith
D) Personal preference of the jurist

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in qiyas is based on intrinsic qualities of the evidence—like strength of effect, stability, and abundance of analogical origins—not on the sheer number of independent proofs.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Methods of Tarjīḥ in Qiyās: Stronger Effect, Multiple Uṣūl, and Converse
Explaining four methods of preferring one qiyās over another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain three methods of tarjīḥ (stronger effect, multiplicity of principles, and ṭard wa ‘aks) and apply them to evaluate conflicting qiyās arguments.

Core Idea
Tarjīḥ in qiyās depends on the strength of the description, multiplicity of its bases, and its converse — all tracing to stronger legal effect.

When two qiyās arguments conflict, we need a method to prefer one over the other. This passage from a Hanafi uṣūl text presents three key methods: preferring the description with a stronger effect (e.g., lightness vs. pillarhood), preferring the description supported by more analogous bases (multiple uṣūl), and preferring the description that shows both correspondence and converse (ṭard wa ‘aks). The author also notes a dispute about the validity of the second method and emphasizes that all three ultimately reduce to the strength of the description’s effect. Understanding these tools is essential for resolving apparent conflicts in analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting qiyās arguments
Find the two descriptions (wiping vs. pillarhood) and the rulings they support (non-repetition vs. repetition of wiping the head). Note which school holds each.
The Hanafīs say wiping is not repeated; the Shāfi‘īs say it is sunna to repeat.
2
Apply tarjīḥ by stronger effect
Analyze why the description 'wiping' is more binding for the ruling of non-repetition than 'pillarhood' is for repetition. Consider the scope and implications of each description across different acts.
The author argues that pillarhood is too general (it includes standing, bowing, etc., which are not repeated), while wiping specifically indicates lightness.
3
Evaluate tarjīḥ by multiplicity of uṣūl
Count the number of analogous bases supporting each description: wiping is supported by khuff, splint, and tayammum; pillarhood only by washing. Understand why the majority accepts this as valid tarjīḥ and why some scholars reject it.
The objection compares multiplicity of uṣūl to multiplicity of narrators, which is not a valid ground for tarjīḥ in khabar. The Hanafī response is that the description itself is the proof, and plurality of bases strengthens it indirectly.
4
Apply tarjīḥ by absence (converse)
Check whether the ruling is absent when the description is absent. If it is, the description is converse and more preponderant than one that only shows correspondence (ruling exists when description exists).
In the wiping example, non-repetition is absent when the act is not wiping (e.g., washing the face), so the description is converse.

Source Text
