فصل في الترجيح
الحكم المشهود به كقولنا في مسح الرأس : إنه مسح؛ لأنه أثبت في دلالة التخفيف قولهم: "إنه "ركن" في دلالة التكرار ؛ فإن أركان الصلاة تمامها بالإكمال دون التكرار، فأما أثر المسح في التخفيف فلازم في كل ما لا يعقل تطهيراً كالتيمم ونحوه.
والترجيح بكثرة الأصول؛ لأن كثرة الأصول زيادة لزوم الحكم معه،
الثالث
مسح
عدم
الحكم المشهود به بأن يكون وصف أحد القياسين ألزم للحكم المتعلق به من وصف القياس الآخر. إنه مسح فلا يسَنّ تكراره فالحكم المشهود به هنا عدم تكرار المسح وعلته المسح فهذا الوصف ألزم لإثبات هذا الحكم. أثبت له زيادة تأثير كالتيمم ونحوه والحاصل أن أصحاب الشافعي له يقولون: يُسَنّ تكرار الرأس، وعندنا لا يسن، فجعل أصحاب الشافعي علة التكرار الركنية، ونحن جعلنا علة التكرار الذي هو التخفيف المسح، فنحن نقول لهم: وصفكم وهو الركنية ليس بألزم لهذا الحكم وهو التكرار؛ لأن هذا الوصف عام يشمل أركان الوضوء والصلاة وغيرهما، وهي لا توجب سنية التكرار في غير الوضوء، بل من قضية الركن في الصلاة إتمامه بالإكمال دون التكرار حتى لم يشرع تكرار القيام والركوع والسجود للإكمال، وأما السجدة فتكرارها ليس من باب التكميل بل كل سجدة ركن على حدة حتى لا تجوز الصلاة. ترى في التيمم والخف والجبائر فصار وصف المسح ألزم للحكم المذكور، واحترز بقوله في كل ما لا يعقل تطهيرا عن الاستنجاء بغير الماء، فإنه مسح شرع فيه التكرار إذ إزالة النجاسة بتكرار مسح الحجارة معقول. بكثرة الأصول: بأن يشهد لأحد الوصفين أصل واحد وللآخر أصلان، أو أصول كوصف المسح في مسألة التثليث، فإنه يشهد بصحته أصول ثلاثة مثل مسح الخف والجبيرة والتيمم، ولم يشهد لوصف الخصم وهو الركنية إلا أصل واحد وهو الغسل فحينئذ يترجح وصفنا عليه والمراد بالأصل المقيس عليه كما علمت من المثال، فهذا القسم من الترجيح عند الجمهور صحيح. معه أي مع الوصف؛ لأن الحجة هي الوصف لا الأصل المستنبط منه، لكن كثرة الأصول توجب زيادة تأكيد ولزوم الحكم بذلك الوصف من وجه آخر غير ما ذكرنا من شدة التأثير والثبات على الحكم، فيحدث بها قوة في نفس الوصف، فلذلك صلحت للترجيح، وقال بعض أصحابنا وبعض أصحاب الشافعي له: إن الترجيح بكثرة الأصول غير صحيح؛ لأن كثرة الأصول في القياس بمنزلة كثرة الرواة في الخبر، والخبر لا ترجح بكثرة الرواة على ما مر فكذا هذا، أو لأنه من جنس الترجيح بكثرة العلة؛ إذ شهادة كل أصل بمنزلة شهادة كل علة على حدة، فيكون هذا من قبيل كثرة الأدلة القياسية أو كثرة وجه الشبه لشيء، فإن هذه كلها لا تصلح للترجيح.
والترجيح بالعدم عند عدمه، وهو أي عدم الحكم
أضعف من وجوه الترجيح؛ لأن العدم لا يتعلق به حكم، لكن الحكم إذا تعلق بوصف ثم عدم عند عدمه كان أوضح لصحته.
الرابع
ف: وهذه الوجوه الثلاثة ترجع إلى معنى واحد وهو الترجيح بقوة تأثير الوصف ولكن تعدّدت باختلاف الجهات، فإن الترجيح في الأول بالنظر إلى نفس الوصف، وفي الثاني بالنظر إلى الحكم، وفي الثالث بالنظر إلى الأصل، فتفكر في هذا المقام فإنه من مزال الأقدام. عند عدمه : أي عدم الوصف ويسمى هذا بالعكس، والطرد أن يوجد الحكم عند وجود الوصف فالوصف الذي يطرد وينعكس بأن يوجد الحكم عند وجوده وينعدم عند انعدامه أولى وأرجح من الوصف الذي يطرد، بأن يوجد الحكم عند وجود الوصف ولا ينعكس بأن لا ينعدم عند انعدامه مثاله قولنا في مسح الرأس: إنه مسح في الوضوء فلا يسن تثليثه، فإن هذا الوصف ينعكس إلى قولنا ما لا يكون مسحاً فيسن تثليثه كغسل الوجه ونحوه، بخلاف وصف الركنية، فإنه لا ينعكس إلى قولنا ما ليس بركن لا يسن تثليثه فإن المضمضة والاستنشاق في الوضوء وتسبيحات الركوع والسجود في الصلاة إنها ليست بركن في الوضوء وفي الصلاة، ومع هذا يسن تثليثها، فهذا القسم من الترجيح صحيح عند عامة الأصوليين؛ لأن عدم الحكم عند عدم الوصف دليل على اختصاص الحكم بذلك الوصف.
لأن العدم لا يتعلق به إلخ لأن العدم ليس بشيء، فكيف يتعلق به الرجحان؟ فلهذا لو عارضه قسم من الأقسام الثلاثة كان راجحاً عليه
Chapter on Preponderance. The ruling witnessed by the description, like our statement concerning wiping the head: it is wiping, because it is more established in indicating lightness, while their statement: 'It is a pillar' indicates repetition; for the pillars of prayer are completed by perfection without repetition. As for the effect of wiping in lightness, it is necessary in everything not understood as purification, like tayammum and the like. And preponderance by multiplicity of principles, because multiplicity of principles increases the binding of the ruling with it. The third: the ruling witnessed by the description being that the description of one of the two analogies is more binding for the ruling attached to it than the description of the other analogy. Its wiping so its repetition is not sunna; the ruling witnessed here is non-repetition of wiping, and its cause is wiping, so this description is more binding for establishing this ruling. It is established for him increased effect like tayammum and the like. The conclusion is that the followers of al-Shafi'i say: repetition of the head is sunna, while with us it is not sunna. So the followers of al-Shafi'i made the cause of repetition the pillarhood, and we made the cause of repetition which is lightness the wiping. So we say to them: your description, which is pillarhood, is not more binding for this ruling, which is repetition; because this description is general encompassing the pillars of ablution and prayer and others, and these do not necessitate the sunna of repetition in other than ablution. Rather, from the requirement of the pillar in prayer is its completion by perfection without repetition such that repetition of standing, bowing, and prostration for completion is not prescribed. As for the prostration, its repetition is not from the category of completion, but each prostration is a separate pillar such that prayer is not valid. Consider tayammum, the khuff, and splints; so the description of wiping becomes more binding for the mentioned ruling. And he restricted by his statement 'in everything not understood as purification' to exclude cleansing with other than water, because it is wiping in which repetition is prescribed since removing impurity by repeating the wiping with stones is understood. By multiplicity of principles: that one single principle witnesses for one of the two descriptions, and two principles or more for the other, like the description of wiping in the issue of tathlith, for three principles witness its validity: wiping the khuff, the splint, and tayammum; and for the opponent's description, which is pillarhood, only one principle witnesses, which is washing; then our description is given preponderance. And what is meant by principle is the analogized base, as you have learned from the example. So this type of preponderance is valid according to the majority. 'With it' meaning with the description; because the proof is the description, not the principle derived from it. But multiplicity of principles necessitates increase of confirmation and binding of the ruling by that description from another perspective besides what we mentioned of intensity of effect and steadfastness upon the ruling, so it generates strength in the description itself; therefore it is suitable for preponderance. And some of our companions and some followers of al-Shafi'i said: preponderance by multiplicity of principles is not valid; because multiplicity of principles in analogy is like multiplicity of narrators in reports, and a report is not given preponderance by multiplicity of narrators as passed, so this is the same. Or because it is of the type of preponderance by multiplicity of causes, since the testimony of each principle is like the testimony of each cause separately, so this is from the category of multiplicity of analogical evidences or multiplicity of aspects of similarity for something, for all these are not suitable for preponderance. And preponderance by absence at the time of its absence, i.e., the absence of the ruling is weaker than the types of preponderance; because absence is not attached to a ruling, but when a ruling is attached to a description and then is absent upon its absence, it is clearer for its validity. The fourth: then these three aspects go back to one meaning, which is preponderance by the strength of the effect of the description, but they are multiplied by difference of perspectives. For preponderance in the first is with respect to the description itself, in the second with respect to the ruling, and in the third with respect to the principle. So reflect on this place, for it is a place where feet slip. 'Upon its absence' meaning upon absence of the description, and this is called the converse. And correspondence is that the ruling exists upon existence of the description, so the description that corresponds and is converse, such that the ruling exists upon its existence and is absent upon its absence, is more appropriate and more preponderant than the description that corresponds but does not converse, i.e., the ruling exists upon existence of the description but does not become absent upon its absence. Its example is our statement concerning wiping the head: it is wiping in ablution so its triple repetition is not sunna, for this description is converse to our statement: that which is not wiping has its triple repetition sunna, like washing the face and the like. Contrary to the description of pillarhood, for it is not converse to our statement: that which is not a pillar does not have its triple repetition sunna; for rinsing the mouth and snuffing water in ablution and the tasbihat of bowing and prostration in prayer are not pillars in ablution and prayer, yet their triple repetition is sunna. So this type of preponderance is valid according to the generality of usuliyyun; because the absence of the ruling upon absence of the description is evidence of the specification of the ruling to that description. Because absence is not attached to... for absence is nothing, so how is preponderance attached to it? Therefore, if it is opposed by a type from the three types, it is preponderant over it.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the types of tarjīḥ (preponderance) in qiyās. The author begins with tarjīḥ by the stronger effect of the description, using the example of wiping the head in wuḍū': the Hanafis hold that repetition of wiping is not sunna, because the description 'wiping' indicates lightness, while the Shāfi'īs argue that wiping is a pillar (rukn) and repetition is sunna. The author argues that the description of wiping is more binding for the ruling of non-repetition because it is general in light acts, while pillarhood is general in all pillars and does not necessitate repetition. Then tarjīḥ by multiplicity of uṣūl (principles) is discussed: if one description has multiple analogous bases (like wiping in khuff, splint, tayammum) and the other has only one (washing), the first is preponderant. This is valid according to the majority, though some Ḥanafīs and Shāfi'īs reject it, arguing that it is like multiplicity of narrators in reports or multiplicity of causes, which are not valid grounds for tarjīḥ. The third type is tarjīḥ by 'adam (absence) at the time of absence, meaning the converse: a description for which the ruling exists when the description exists and is absent when it is absent is stronger than one that only corresponds. This is illustrated again with wiping: the ruling of non-repetition is present with wiping and absent with washing, so the description 'wiping' is converse. The author notes that this type is weaker because absence is not a positive thing, but it still provides clarity. Finally, the three types (stronger effect, multiple uṣūl, and ṭard wa 'aks) are summarized as all going back to the strength of the description's effect, differing only in perspective. The passage includes the rulings and the disputes among scholars.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Giving preponderance to one evidence over another when conflicting
الطرد والعكس (al-ṭard wa al-'aks): Correspondence and converse: the ruling exists with the description and is absent in its absence
الأصل (al-aṣl): The base case in qiyās from which the ruling is derived

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is wiping the head not repeated in wuḍū'?
A) Because it is not a pillar
B) Because the description 'wiping' indicates lightness and is more binding
C) Because the Qur'an commands once
D) Because the head is not impure

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī method of tarjīḥ focuses on the description's binding effect, supported by multiplicity of principles and converse regularity — but acknowledges that absence-based tarjīḥ is weakest.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Conflict of Tarjīḥ Factors in Qiyas
Classification and prioritization rule for conflicting tarjīḥ factors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify conflicts between tarjīḥ factors into three categories and apply the rule that intrinsic tarjīḥ outweighs circumstantial.

Core Idea
Intrinsic tarjīḥ trumps circumstantial when they conflict.

When two analogies each have a preponderance factor, those factors themselves can conflict. The author of Al-Ḥusāmī lays out a clear classification: three types of conflict, and a prioritization rule. Understanding this ensures you can correctly resolve apparent stalemates in qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting tarjīḥ factors
Determine if the preponderance in each analogy is intrinsic (related to the description's essence) or circumstantial (related to context).
2
Classify the conflict into one of three types
Both intrinsic, both circumstantial, or one of each.
3
Apply the resolution rule
If same type, try to find stronger factor; if impossible, both cancel. If mixed, intrinsic takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ف واعلم أنه كما يقع التعارض بين الأدلة فيحتاج إلى الترجيح كذلك يقع بين وجوه الترجيح، بأن يكون لكل من القياسين ترجيح من وجه وهو أي التعارض بين الترجيحين على ثلاثة أقسام؛ لأنه لا يخلو من أن يقع كل واحد من الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى الذات أو إلى الحال، أو أحدهما بمعنى راجع إلى الذات والآخر بمعنى راجع إلى الحال، ففي القسمين الأولين أي التعارض بين الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى الذات والتعارض بين الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى (الحال يطلب الترجيح بقوة المعاني إن أمكن وإلا بقي التعارض وتحقق التساقط، وفي القسم الثالث (أي التعارض بين الترجيحين أحدهما بحسب معنى راجع إلى الذات والآخر إلى الحال كان الترجيح بحسب معنى راجع إلى الذات أولى وأحق من الترجيح الذي بحسب معنى راجع إلى الحال، وإليه أشار المصنف بقوله: وإذا تعارض إلخ.
Then know that just as conflict occurs between evidences and needs preponderance, similarly it occurs between aspects of preponderance, such that each of the two analogies has a preponderance from one perspective. This conflict between the two preponderances is of three divisions: because it is not free from either that each of the two preponderances is with a meaning returning to the essence (dhāt) or to the circumstance (ḥāl), or one of them with a meaning returning to the essence and the other with a meaning returning to the circumstance. So in the first two divisions, i.e., conflict between two preponderances with a meaning returning to the essence, and conflict between two preponderances with a meaning returning to the circumstance, preponderance is sought by the strength of meanings if possible; otherwise the conflict remains and the fall (tasāquṭ) occurs. In the third division, i.e., conflict between two preponderances, one according to a meaning returning to the essence and the other to the circumstance, preponderance according to a meaning returning to the essence is more appropriate and more deserving than preponderance which is according to a meaning returning to the circumstance. And the author alluded to this by his saying: 'And when they conflict...' etc.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when two analogies both have a tarjīḥ factor, but the tarjīḥ factors themselves conflict. The author classifies this conflict into three types: (1) both tarjīḥ factors are intrinsic (related to the essence of the description), (2) both are circumstantial (related to the situation), or (3) one is intrinsic and the other circumstantial. In the first two cases, one must try to find a stronger meaning within that category; if not possible, both preponderances cancel each other out. In the third case, the intrinsic tarjīḥ takes precedence over the circumstantial one. This is a standard Hanafi usul principle.

Key Terms
الذات (al-dhāt): The intrinsic essence or meaning of the description, not dependent on external circumstances
الحال (al-ḥāl): The circumstance or context surrounding the description
التساقط (al-tasāquṭ): The fall or cancellation of both conflicting evidences when no tarjīḥ is possible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when two tarjīḥ factors conflict, one intrinsic and one circumstantial, what is the rule?
A) Intrinsic yields to circumstantial
B) Both factors cancel
C) The intrinsic factor preponderates
D) The circumstantial factor preponderates because it is more specific

Key Takeaway
In conflicts between tarjīḥ factors, intrinsic meanings take priority over circumstantial ones, but if both are of the same type, seek a stronger factor or else both cancel.

Tarjīḥ by 'Aks (Inverse) and Its Strength
Explanation of tarjīḥ by absence of ruling at absence of description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a description that is both ṭard and ʿaks is stronger for tarjīḥ and identify the example of wiping the head.

Core Idea
Absence of ruling at absence of description indicates specification, making the description a stronger candidate for the effective cause.

In usul al-fiqh, when two descriptions compete to be the effective cause (ʿillah) of a ruling, one method of preference is the inverse (ʿaks): if the ruling disappears when the description disappears, the description is more likely to be the cause. This lesson examines the strength of such preference.

Guided Path
1
Define ṭard and ʿaks
Understand the two terms: ṭard is the existence of the ruling with the existence of the description; ʿaks is the absence of the ruling with the absence of the description.
2
Understand the argument for ʿaks
The passage argues that a description showing both ṭard and ʿaks is stronger because the absence of ruling at absence of description indicates that the ruling is specifically tied to that description.
This is evidence for specification (ikhtiṣāṣ).
3
Analyze the example of wiping the head
The example: wiping the head is not repeated thrice because it is wiping. Non-wiping acts (like washing face) are repeated thrice. This shows ṭard and ʿaks. Contrast with 'being a pillar' which is only ṭard.
The description 'wiping' is both ṭard and ʿaks; 'pillar' is only ṭard.
4
Recognize the weakness of preference by absence
The author notes that this type is weak because absence (ʿadam) is a non-entity. However, the strength comes from the implied specification, not from absence itself.
Some later scholars rejected it entirely, but the majority accept it as valid albeit weak.
5
Distinguish between types of descriptions
A description that is only ṭard (ruling exists with description but does not cease without it) is weaker than one that is both ṭard and ʿaks.

والترجيح بالعدم عند عدمه، وهو أي عدم الحكم. أضعف من وجوه الترجيح؛ لأن العدم لا يتعلّق به حكم، لكن الحكم إذا تعلق بوصف ثم عدم عند عدمه كان أوضح لصحته. الرابع. ف: وهذه الوجوه الثلاثة ترجع إلى معنى واحد وهو الترجيح بقوة تأثير الوصف ولكن تعدّدت باختلاف الجهات، فإن الترجيح في الأول بالنظر إلى نفس الوصف، وفي الثاني بالنظر إلى الحكم، وفي الثالث بالنظر إلى الأصل، فتفكر في هذا المقام فإنه من مزال الأقدام. عند عدمه : أي عدم الوصف ويسمّى هذا بالعكس، والطرد أن يوجد الحكم عند وجود الوصف فالوصف الذي يطرد وينعكس بأن يوجد الحكم عند وجوده وينعدم عند انعدامه أولى وأرجح من الوصف الذي يطرد، بأن يوجد الحكم عند وجود الوصف ولا ينعكس بأن لا ينعدم عند انعدامه مثاله قولنا في مسح الرأس: إنه مسح في الوضوء فلايُسَنّ تثليثه، فإن هذا الوصف ينعكس إلى قولنا ما لايكون مسحاً فيسن تثليثه كغسل الوجه ونحوه، بخلاف وصف الركنية، فإنه لا ينعكس إلى قولنا ما ليس بركن لايسن تثليثه فإن المضمضة والاستنشاق في الوضوء وتسبيحات الركوع والسجود في الصلاة إنها ليست بركن في الوضوء وفي الصلاة، ومع هذا يسن تثليثها، فهذا القسم من الترجيح صحيح عند عامة الأصوليين؛ لأن عدم الحكم عند عدم الوصف دليل على اختصاص الحكم بذلك الوصف. لأن العدم لا يتعلق به إلخ لأن العدم ليس بشيء، فكيف يتعلّق به الرجحان؟ فلهذا لو عارضه قسم من الأقسام الثلاثة كان راجحاً عليه وقال بعض المتأخرين لا عبرة؛ لأن العدم لا يتعلّق به شيء، فلا يوجب عدم العلة عدم الحكم، ولا وجوده؛ لأنه ليس بشيء، والرجحان إنما يحصل بأمر وجودي، فدفع المصنف هذا الاستدلال بقوله: "لكن الحكم ؛ لأن الوصف الذي يوجد الحكم عند وجوده وينعدم عند انعدامه أوضح وصفاً من الذي لا ينعدم الحكم عن انعدامه فالرجحان إنما يضاف حقيقة وبحسب المعنى إلى الاختصاص المستفاد من عدم الحكم عند انعدامه إن كان إضافته بحسب الظاهر إلى العدم، ولهذا يضعف هذا القسم.
And preference by absence at its absence, that is, absence of the ruling. It is the weakest of the aspects of preference because absence is not subject to a ruling, but when a ruling is attached to a description and then is absent at its absence, it is clearer for its validity. The fourth. Then: These three aspects return to one meaning, which is preference by the strength of the description's effect, but they are multiple due to difference of perspectives: preference in the first is with regard to the description itself, in the second with regard to the ruling, and in the third with regard to the origin (aṣl). So reflect on this place, for it is a slipping of feet. 'At its absence' means absence of the description, and this is called 'inverse' ('aks). 'Ṭard' is that the ruling exists with the existence of the description. So the description that is both ṭard and 'aks—i.e., the ruling exists with its existence and ceases with its cessation—is more worthy and preferable than a description that is only ṭard—i.e., the ruling exists with the existence of the description but does not cease with its cessation. An example is our statement regarding wiping the head: it is wiping in ablution, so its threefold repetition is not Sunnah. Indeed, this description is inverted to our statement: whatever is not wiping, its threefold repetition is Sunnah, like washing the face and the like. Contrary to the description of being a pillar (rukniyyah), for it is not inverted to our statement: whatever is not a pillar, its threefold repetition is not Sunnah. Indeed, rinsing the mouth and sniffing water in ablution, and the glorifications of bowing and prostration in prayer—they are not pillars in ablution and in prayer, yet their threefold repetition is Sunnah. So this type of preference is valid according to the generality of uṣūliyyīn because the absence of the ruling at the absence of the description is evidence for the specification of the ruling to that description. 'Because absence is not connected to...' etc. Because absence is not a thing, so how can preference be connected to it? Hence if another type from the three types opposes it, that type is preponderant over it. And some later scholars said: there is no consideration because absence is not connected to anything; so it does not necessitate the absence of the ruling from the absence of the cause, nor its existence, because it is not a thing, and preferential weight is only attained by an existent matter. So the author (muṣannif) refuted this inference by saying: 'But the ruling... because the description with which the ruling exists at its existence and ceases at its cessation is clearer in description than that with which the ruling does not cease at its cessation. So preference is actually attributed, in meaning, to the specification derived from the absence of the ruling at its cessation, even if apparently it is attributed to absence. For this reason this type is weak.'
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific type of tarjīḥ (preference) in qiyās known as 'preference by absence' (al-tarjīḥ bi al-ʿadam). The author explains that this type is the weakest among the aspects of tarjīḥ because absence (ʿadam) is a non-entity and cannot itself be a basis for preference. However, he clarifies that when a ruling is attached to a description and the ruling is absent when the description is absent, this indicates a clear specification of the ruling to that description. The strength actually comes from the evident specification, not from the absence itself. The passage distinguishes between two types of descriptions: those that are both ṭard (the ruling exists with the description) and ʿaks (the ruling ceases when the description ceases), and those that are only ṭard. The former is stronger because the inverse correlation confirms the causal link. An example is given from fiqh: wiping the head in wuḍūʾ is not repeated thrice because it is wiping; this description (being wiping) is ṭard and ʿaks—since non-wiping acts like washing the face are repeated thrice. In contrast, the description 'being a pillar' (rukniyyah) is only ṭard: acts that are not pillars (like rinsing the mouth) are still repeated thrice. The author notes that some later scholars rejected this type of tarjīḥ altogether, but the muṣannif refutes them by arguing that the real basis is the specification evident from the absence. The passage concludes that this type is weak relative to others.

Key Terms
الطرد (al-ṭard): The existence of the ruling with the existence of the description.
العكس (al-ʿaks): The absence of the ruling with the absence of the description.
العدم (al-ʿadam): Absence or non-existence of the ruling or description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the description that is both ṭard and ʿaks stronger than one that is only ṭard?
A) Because it is based on absence, which is a strong proof.
B) Because the inverse correlation indicates clear specification of the ruling to that description.
C) Because it is accepted by all uṣūliyyīn without exception.
D) Because it involves a rational proof rather than textual proof.

Key Takeaway
A description that is both ṭard and ʿaks is stronger for tarjīḥ because the inverse correlation indicates specification of the ruling to that description.

Resolving Conflicting Tarjīḥs: Essential vs. Accidental Attributes
Rule for when two tarjīḥs contradict, one based on essence, the other on state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an essential-based tarjīḥ (dhātī) outweighs a state-based tarjīḥ (ḥālī) and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf in the fasting intention case.

Core Idea
When two tarjīḥs conflict, the one based on essence (dhātī) always prevails over the one based on state (ḥālī).

In advanced uṣūl al-fiqh, conflicts can also occur between the very criteria of preference (tarjīḥ). This passage from al-Husāmī presents a fundamental rule: when one tarjīḥ rests on an essential attribute and the other on an accidental state, the essential one wins. The principle is illustrated with a concrete example from the validity of the Ramaḍān fast when intention is made before midday. Understanding this hierarchy is key to mastering Hanafi ijtihād.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios of conflict between tarjīḥs
The author states that conflict between two tarjīḥs can be: both based on essence, both on state, or mixed. In the first two, further tarjīḥ by strength of meanings is sought; otherwise both cancel. In the mixed case, essence wins.
Only the mixed case is the focus of this passage.
2
Understand the rationale for essence over state
The state (ḥāl) is subsistent by the essence (dhāt) and follows it. A follower cannot invalidate the original. Therefore, a tarjīḥ based on essence is more deserving.
This is a rational (ʿaqlī) argument, not based on a naṣṣ.
3
Examine the fasting example
In the Ramaḍān fast, the intention (niyyah) is an essential attribute for validity, while the description of worship (ʿibādah) is accidental. Some scholars preferred invalidity because of the worship aspect; Hanafis preferred validity because intention is essential.
The passage also mentions 'abundance' (kathrah) as supporting validity, but the primary basis is essential vs. accidental.
4
Formulate the rule
When two tarjīḥs conflict, the one based on an essential description (al-waṣf al-dhātī) takes precedence over the one based on an accidental description (al-waṣf al-ʿāriḍī).
This rule is applied in various qiyās disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الترجيح ... ف واعلم أنه كما يقع التعارض بين الأدلة فيحتاج إلى الترجيح كذلك يقع بين وجوه الترجيح، بأن يكون لكل من القياسين ترجيح من وجه وهو أي التعارض بين الترجيحين على ثلاثة أقسام؛ لأنه لا يخلو من أن يقع كل واحد من الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى الذات أو إلى الحال، أو أحدهما بمعنى راجع إلى الذات والآخر بمعنى راجع إلى الحال، ففي القسمين الأولين أي التعارض بين الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى الذات والتعارض بين الترجيحين بمعنى راجع إلى (الحال يطلب الترجيح بقوة المعاني إن أمكن وإلا بقي التعارض وتحقق التساقط، وفي القسم الثالث (أي التعارض بين الترجيحين أحدهما بحسب معنى راجع إلى الذات والآخر إلى الحال كان الترجيح بحسب معنى راجع إلى الذات أولى وأحق من الترجيح الذي بحسب معنى راجع إلى الحال، وإليه أشار المصنف بقوله: وإذا تعارض إلخ.  ... وإذا تعارض ضربا ترجيح كان الرجحان بالذات أحيّ منه بالحال؛ لأن الحال قائمة بالذات تابعة له، والتبع لا يصلح مُبطلا للأصل، وعلى هذا قلنا في صوم رمضان: إنه يتأدّى بنية قبل انتصاف النهار؛ لأنه ركن واحد يتعلق بالعزيمة، فإذا وجدت في البعض دون البعض تعارضا فرجّحنا بالكثرة؛ لأنه من باب الوجود ... أي الكثرة ... ضربا :ترجيح بأن يكون لكل واحد من القياسين المتعارضين ترجيح، فأحد الترجيحين بحسب معنى في الذات والآخر بحسب معنى في الحال فحينئذ كان الرجحان بالذات أحق منه بالحال بالحال والحاصل أن الترجيح بحسب الوصف الذاتي أحق من الترجيح بحسب الوصف العارض ... ولكنها تعارضت، فمنهم من رجّح الفساد بوصف العبادة، فإنها عبادة وصف عارضي، ومنهم من رجّح الصحة بالنية وهي وصف ذاتي، فقدمنا الصحة على الفساد لكون الوصف الذاتي أقوى من العارضي.
Chapter on Preference ... So know that just as conflict occurs between evidences requiring preference, similarly it occurs between aspects of preference, such that each of the two analogies has a preference from one aspect. And conflict between preferences is of three types: because it is either that each of the two preferences is based on a meaning referring to the essence (dhāt) or to the state (ḥāl), or one based on essence and the other on state. In the first two types (conflict between two preferences both referring to essence, or both referring to state), preference is sought by the strength of meanings if possible; otherwise conflict remains and cancellation (tasāquṭ) occurs. In the third type (conflict where one preference is based on essence and the other on state), the preference based on essence is more worthy and more deserving than the preference based on state. And to this the author (muṣannif) alluded by his saying: 'When they conflict...' etc. ... 'And when two types of preference conflict, the preponderance by essence is more alive than that by state, because the state is subsistent by the essence and follows it, and the follower is not suitable to invalidate the original.' And based on this, we said regarding the fast of Ramadan: It is fulfilled with an intention before midday, because it is a single pillar related to resolve (ʿazīmah). So when it (the intention) occurs in part (of the day) but not the other, they conflict, and we gave preference by abundance (kathrah) because it is from the category of existence. ... 'Two types of preference' meaning each of the two conflicting analogies has a preference; one of the two preferences is according to a meaning in the essence and the other according to a meaning in the state. Then the preponderance by essence is more deserving than the preponderance by state. The upshot is that preference by an essential description is more deserving than preference by an accidental description. ... But they conflicted; some gave preference to invalidity by the description of worship (ʿibādah), which is an accidental description, and others gave preference to validity by the intention, which is an essential description. So we gave precedence to validity over invalidity because the essential description is stronger than the accidental.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage addresses a more advanced issue: what happens when two different types of tarjīḥ (preference) conflict with each other in a qiyās dispute. The author classifies conflicts into three scenarios: both preferences based on essences (dhāt), both based on states (ḥāl), or mixed. In mixed conflicts, the essential-based preference always wins because the state is dependent on the essence. The text provides a concrete fiqh example from fasting in Ramadan: the intention before midday. The issue is whether a fast is valid if the intention occurs after dawn but before midday (in voluntary fasts, but here Ramadan). In the Hanafi view, the fast of Ramadan is a single pillar, so if the intention occurs in part of the day, there is a conflict between validity (because intention is present for some part) and invalidity (because intention missing for another part). The Shafiʿis might argue that the worship aspect (ʿibādah) requires continuity, so the fast is invalid. But the Hanafis rule that the intention is a dhātī (essential) description for the validity of the fast, while the worship aspect is ʿāriḍī (accidental). Since essential descriptions outweigh accidental ones, the fast is valid. The 'preference by abundance' (kathrah) refers to the fact that the intention covers most of the day (if made before midday), so it is preferred. This illustrates the rule: when two tarjīḥs conflict, the one based on an intrinsic attribute (dhātī) takes priority over one based on an extrinsic attribute (ḥālī). The passage notes that some later scholars might have reservations, but the relied-upon position is clear.

Key Terms
الذاتي (al-dhātī): An attribute intrinsic to the thing's essence, not separable.
العارضي (al-ʿāriḍī): An accidental attribute that comes and goes, not essential.
الكثرة (al-kathrah): Preference by abundance, i.e., the greater number of parts or instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the fast of Ramadan valid with intention before midday?
A) Because the intention covers the entire day.
B) Because the intention is an essential description (dhātī) and the worship description is accidental (ʿāriḍī).
C) Because the Hanafis prefer abundance (kathrah) over anything else.
D) Because the Shafiʿis also accept this ruling.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi uṣūl, when two tarjīḥs conflict, the one based on an essential attribute (dhātī) always outweighs the one based on an accidental state (ḥālī).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

8 min
Preferring Intrinsic Description in Conflicting Analogies
Establishes rule that intrinsic description outweighs accidental in analogy conflict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intrinsic description (al-wasf al-dhati) prevails over accidental description (al-wasf al-'aridi) in resolving conflicting analogies, and explain the Hanafi ruling on Ramadan fast intention before midday.

Core Idea
Intrinsic description outweighs accidental, even in acts of worship where precaution might suggest otherwise.

When two analogies conflict and each has a preferencing factor, which should we choose? The Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy: descriptions that are intrinsic to the essence (wasf dhati) take precedence over those that are accidental (wasf 'aridi). This rule is not merely theoretical; it yields a concrete ruling on the validity of the Ramadan fast when intention is made before midday. In this lesson, we will dissect the rule, its justification, and its application in a famous dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule of Tarjih
Extract the core rule from the passage: when two tarjih factors conflict, the one based on an intrinsic description is more worthy (ahaqq) than the one based on an accidental description.
2
Understand Intrinsic vs Accidental
Define wasf dhati (intrinsic, inseparable from essence) and wasf 'aridi (accidental, separable). The intrinsic description is such that the essence cannot exist without it; the accidental can be absent without destroying the essence.
E.g., 'existence' vs. 'worship' in the Ramadan fast.
3
Apply to the Ramadan Fast Case
Consider the scenario: A person intends the Ramadan fast before midday. Hanafis say the fast is valid because intention exists in most of the day (majority). This majority is an intrinsic description (by parts). The accidental description is 'worship', which would demand intention from the start.
Intention in most parts is intrinsic; worship is accidental.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Counter-Argument
Al-Shafi'i argues that the fast should be invalid because intention is required for worship from the beginning; the accidental description (worship) should be preferred as a precaution. The Hanafi response: the accidental is subordinate and cannot overcome the intrinsic.
Precaution (ihtiyat) does not override the rule.
5
State the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Hanafi: fast valid if intended before midday; Shafi'i: invalid. The difference stems from which description is given weight in tarjih.
This is the practical outcome when two analogies conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

على الوصف ولا كلام فيه، وإنما الكلام في وصفين، أحدهما وصف ذاتي والآخر وصف عارضي كما يدلّ عليه سياق الكلام، فالأولى أن يقال: إن الوصف ويوجد الذات بغيره، والوصف الذاتي لا ينفك فلا يوجد الذات بغيره، وترجيح الوصف الذي لا يوجد الذات بدونه ولا ينفك عنه على الوصف الذي ينفك ويوجد الذات بدونه ظاهر. وعلى هذا الأصل وهو أن الترجيح بالوصف الذاتي أولى من الوصف العارض ركن واحد بوحدة اعتبارية شرعية حيث لايتجزى بالعزيمة أي القصد والمراد النية، فإن الصوم لايصح بدون النية. تعارضا: أي البعضان، فإما أن يفسد الكل وإما أن يصح الكل، فلا بد من ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر، فالشافعي محليه رجّح الفاسد على الصحيح بوصف العبادة، فإنها وصف يوجب الفساد حيث لم توجد بعدم النية، فالعبادة وصف عارضي للإمساك المعروف؛ لأن الإمساك بحسب الذات ليس بعبادة بل صار عبادة بجعل الله تعالى، وهو أمر خارج عن الإمساك، وقد قلنا: الترجيح بوصف ذاتي أقوى من وصف عارضي فرجّحنا الصحيح الذي وجد فيه النية. بالكثرة : أي بكثرة أجزاء الصوم لوقوع النية في أكثر النهار، حيث نوى قبل انتصاف النهار، والترجيح بالكثرة ترجيح بوصف ذاتي؛ لأن المراد بالوصف الذاتي وصف يقوم بالشيء بحسب ذاته أو بحسب بعض أجزائه، والكثرة وصف بالكثير يقوم بحسب أجزاءه فتكون وصفاً ذاتيا؛ لأنه من باب الوجود. باب الوجود أي أمر وجودي، هو وصف ذاتي يقوم بالكثير بحسب أجزائه ويمكن التوجيه بوجه آخر ه آخر وهو الضمير في قوله: لأنه إلى الترجيح بالكثرة كما هو الظاهر، فالمعنى ورجّحنا بعض الصحيح بالكثرة؛ لأن هذا الترجيح من باب الوجود أي بوصف ذاتي؛ لأن الوصف العارض بمنزلة المعدوم في مقابلة الوصف الذاتي، فيصح اختصاص الوصف الذاتي ،بالوجود، ولي هنا توجيه آخر لانذكره لضيق المقام. و لم نرجح بالفساد احتياطاً في باب العبادات؛ لأنه ترجيح بمعنى في الحال. الباء زائدة ترجیح الفساد بالعبادة
Chapter of Qiyas. Section on Tarjih. Ruling on conflict in Tarjih: When two types of tarjih conflict, the preference by intrinsic quality is more worthy than by accidental quality, because the accidental is dependent on the intrinsic and subordinate to it, and the subordinate cannot nullify the primary. And on this we said regarding the Ramadan fast: that it is performed with intention before midday, because it is one integral act related to resolve. When intention occurs in some parts but not others, they conflict, and we give preponderance by the majority, because that is from the category of existence. The accidental may be separate from the intrinsic. The two types of tarjih: each of the conflicting analogies has a tarjih, one by an intrinsic meaning, the other by an accidental meaning, then the intrinsic tarjih is more worthy. The summary: tarjih by intrinsic description is more worthy than by accidental description. I say: there is consideration; the apparent meaning of his statement is tarjih of intrinsic over accidental, which is uncontested. The discussion is about two descriptions, one intrinsic and one accidental. It is more appropriate to say: the intrinsic description is inseparable, so the essence is not found without it, while the accidental can be separate. Preferring the inseparable over the separable is obvious. On this principle, that tarjih by intrinsic is better than accidental, the fast is a single integral unit legally indivisible. The intention is necessary for validity. The partial conflict: either all is invalid or all valid, so one must preponderate. Al-Shafi‘i favors invalidity due to the accidental description of worship, which causes invalidity when intention is absent. But worship is accidental to the abstention itself. We have said: tarjih by intrinsic is stronger, so we favor validity where intention exists. By majority: meaning multiplicity of parts, since intention occurs in most of the day when made before midday. Tarjih by majority is tarjih by intrinsic description, because intrinsic description subsists in the thing by its essence or its parts. Majority is a description of multiplicity that subsists by parts, so it is intrinsic, being from the category of existence. There is another interpretation. And we do not give preponderance to invalidity as a precaution in acts of worship, because that would be tarjih by an accidental meaning. The ba is extra. Tarjih of invalidity by worship.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule on tarjih when conflicting analogies each have a preferencing factor. The author states the rule that preference given by an intrinsic description (wasf dhati) is stronger than that given by an accidental description (wasf 'aridi). He illustrates with the Hanafi ruling on the Ramadan fast: if a person intends before midday, the fast is valid even without intention for the whole day, because intention occurs in most of the day (majority). The opposing view of al-Shafi‘i, who would rule invalidity due to lack of intention in the first part, is rejected because his preference is based on the accidental description of worship, whereas the Hanafi preference is based on the intrinsic description of existence (the presence of intention in most parts). The commentary further clarifies that intrinsic descriptions are inseparable from the essence, while accidental ones can be separated, so the intrinsic is more deserving of preponderance. The author also notes that in acts of worship, precaution might suggest preferring invalidity, but here the intrinsic/accidental rule overrides because the accidental is subordinate.

Key Terms
الوصف الذاتي (al-wasf al-dhati): A description that subsists in a thing by its very essence or by its parts, inseparable from the essence.
الوصف العارض (al-wasf al-'aridi): A description that is accidental to the essence, can be separated without affecting the essence.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Giving preponderance to one of two conflicting proofs or analogies over the other based on strength of description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule of tarjih discussed in this passage, which type of description is given preference when two conflicting analogies are compared?
A) The accidental description (al-wasf al-'aridi)
B) The intrinsic description (al-wasf al-dhati)
C) The description based on precaution (ihtiyat)
D) The description that appears first in the analogy

Key Takeaway
When analogies conflict, the intrinsic description (inseparable from essence) always outweighs the accidental description (separable), even in acts of worship where precaution might tempt a different conclusion.

The Three Categories of Rights of Allah: 'Ushr, Kharaj, and Khums
Commentary analyzing the three types of huquq Allah and their characteristics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any right of Allah into one of three categories (worship-dominant, punishment-dominant, or self-standing) using the Hanafi method of talil based on predominant meaning (ghalaba).

Core Idea
Rights of Allah are classified by their dominant meaning: worship, punishment, or inherent divine right.

In this passage, the commentator dissects three types of Huquq Allah — 'ushr, kharaj, and khums — using a sophisticated method of talil (causal reasoning). The key to distinguishing them lies in whether the dominant aspect is 'ibada (worship), 'uquba (punishment), or neither. This analysis determines who is initially obligated, who can be subject to continued obligation, and how the revenue is distributed. We will follow the commentator's reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Locate in the text the three distinct types of Huquq Allah: (1) rights with dominant meaning of worship ('ushr), (2) rights with dominant meaning of punishment (kharaj), and (3) rights established by themselves (khums). Note the key Arabic phrases: 'مؤونة فيها معنى القربة', 'مؤونة فيها معنى العقوبة', and 'حق قائم بنفسه'.
2
Understand the talil for 'ushr
The commentator explains that 'ushr has both a meaning of maintenance (mu'na) and worship ('ibada). The land is the origin (asl), and the produce is subordinate (tab'), so maintenance is original. Worship is subsidiary. This explains why it is not initially imposed on a disbeliever (since he is not eligible for worship) but can continue if a dhimmi acquires the land (since he is eligible for maintenance).
The dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on continuation hinges on which meaning is considered primary.
3
Understand the talil for kharaj
Kharaj also has maintenance as original, but it contains a meaning of punishment ('uquba) because it is a tax on land originally belonging to non-Muslims. Thus it is not initially imposed on a Muslim (not eligible for punishment), but can continue if a Muslim acquires kharaj land (since maintenance applies).
Kharaj is different from 'ushr in that it is not an act of worship at all.
4
Understand the nature of khums
Khums is a right that belongs to Allah Himself, not attached to any individual's liability (dhimma). It is established by itself, stemming from the fact that all spoils belong to Allah; He grants four-fifths to the fighters as a favor. Thus the ruler collects and distributes it, and it can be given to Banu Hashim.
Because it is not 'impurities' like zakat, it may go to the Prophet's family.
5
Apply the method to a new case
Using the same talil, consider a hypothetical new revenue: for example, a tax on mineral extraction. Determine whether it resembles 'ushr (worship element) or kharaj (punishment element) or is a standalone right like khums. Look for dominant meanings.
This strengthens your ability to derive rulings for novel cases using usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
حقوق الله تعالى ومؤونة فيها معنى القربة وهو العشر، ولهذا لا يبتدأ على الكافر، وجاز البقاء عليه عند محمد الله، ومؤونة فيها معنى العقوبة وهو الخراج، ولذلك لايبتدأ على المسلم وجاز البقاء عليه، وحق قائم بنفسه، وهو خمس الغنائم والمعادن، فإنه حق وجب الله تعالى ثابتاً بنفسه بناءً على أن الجهاد حقه، فصار المصاب به له كله، لكنه أوجب أربعة أخماسه للغانمين منّة منه، إلى مصارف الصدقات، ووجوبها على الإنسان بسبب رأس الغير، وكون الرأس فيه سبباً يدل على أن فيها معنى المؤونة كالنفقة ولكن لما كان معنى العبادة فيها غالباً قلنا: عبادة فيها معنى المؤونة، ولهذا لا يجب على الصبي والمجنون عند محمد كسائر العبادات. وهو العشر: فإنه في نفسه مؤونة الأرض التي يزرعها؛ إذ لو منعه لأخلص الأرض عنه السلطان، ولكن فيه معنى العبادة حيث لا يجب ابتداءً إلا على المسلم، ويصرف في مصارف الزكاة إلا أن الأرض أصل، والنماء وصف تابع، فكان معنى المؤونة فيه أصلاً ومعنى العبادة تبعاً. ولهذا: أي بسبب أن فيه معنى القربة. على الكافر: كما لايبتدئ سائر العبادات؛ لأنه ليس بأهل للعبادة. البقاء عليه بأن ملك الذمي أرضاً عشرية للمؤمن فيبقى عليه العشر كما كان عند محمد اعتبارا لمعنى المؤونة، فإن الكافر أهل المؤونة.
وهو الخراج فإنه في نفسه مؤونة للأرض التي يزرعها، حتى لو منعه لاستردّ السلطان منه الأرض ويعطيها الآخر، ولكن فيه معنى العقوبة على المسلم إذ المسلم ليس بأهل للعقوبة والذل في الابتداء، ولكن لما كان معنى المؤونة فيها أصلاً والمسلم أهل للمؤونة جاز البقاء عليه. البقاء عليه حتى لو اشترى مسلم من كافر أرض خراج، أو أسلم الكافر وله أرض خراجية يؤخذ الخراج منه دون العشر رعاية لمعنى المؤونة. قائم بنفسه: أي ثابت بذاته من غير أن يتعلق بذمة العبد شيء منه حتى يجب عليه أداؤه بل استبقاه الله تعالى لأجل نفسه وتولى السلطان الذي هو خليفة في الأرض أخذه وقسمته. وجب الله: ثبت له تعالى لا حق لأحد فيه ثابتا بنفسه: أي حال كون ذلك الحق ثابتاً من غير تعلقه بذمة المكلف حقه فإنه إعزاز لدينه، وفيه نفع للعالم المصاب به أي الحاصل بالجهاد وهو مال الغنيمة له منةً منه بغير استحقاقهم فيه، فإنهم عبيد له، ولا حق للعبد في ما يعمل لمولاه.
فلم يكن حقاً لزمنا أداؤه طاعةً له بل هو حق استبقاه لنفسه، فتولى السلطان أخذه الذي هو خليفته في الأرض
الخمس
وقسمته، ولهذا جوزنا صرفه إلى من استحق أربعة الأخماس من الغانمين بخلاف الزكاة والصدقات، وحلّ لبني هاشم؛ لأنه على هذا التحقيق لم يصر من الأوساخ
Chapter of Qiyas. The rights of Allah, the Exalted: and [among them is] the maintenance which contains the meaning of proximity (to Allah), and it is 'ushr; therefore it is not initiated upon the disbeliever, and its continuation is permissible upon him according to Muhammad. And [there is] maintenance which contains the meaning of punishment, and it is kharaj; therefore it is not initiated upon the Muslim, and its continuation is permissible upon him. And a right established by itself, and it is the khums of spoils and minerals; for it is a right that is obligatory for Allah, the Exalted, established by itself, based on the fact that jihad is His right, so what is acquired becomes entirely His, but He obligated four-fifths of it to the spoilers as a favor from Him, to the channels of charities. And its obligation upon a person due to the head [tax] of another, and that the head in it is a cause indicates that it contains the meaning of maintenance like nafaqah, but since the meaning of worship is predominant in it, we say: it is an act of worship with a meaning of maintenance. Therefore it is not obligatory upon the minor and the insane according to Muhammad like other acts of worship. And it is 'ushr: for it in itself is maintenance for the land that he cultivates; because if he withholds it, the ruler would take the land from him, but it contains the meaning of worship since it is not initially obligatory except upon a Muslim, and it is spent on the channels of zakat. But since the land is the origin and the produce is a subordinate description, the meaning of maintenance is original and the meaning of worship is subsidiary. And therefore, i.e., because it contains the meaning of proximity, it is not initiated upon the disbeliever, just as other acts of worship are not initiated, because he is not qualified for worship. Its continuation: such that if a dhimmi owns 'ushr land from a believer, the 'ushr remains upon him as it was, according to Muhammad, considering the meaning of maintenance, for the disbeliever is qualified for maintenance. And it is kharaj: for it in itself is maintenance for the land he cultivates; even if he withholds it, the ruler would take the land from him and give it to another, but it contains the meaning of punishment upon the Muslim, for the Muslim is not qualified for punishment and humiliation initially. But since the meaning of maintenance in it is original and the Muslim is qualified for maintenance, its continuation is permissible. Its continuation: even if a Muslim buys kharaj land from a disbeliever, or the disbeliever becomes Muslim and owns kharaj land, the kharaj is taken from him, not 'ushr, in consideration of the meaning of maintenance. Established by itself: i.e., established in its essence without any part of it being attached to the liability of the servant such that he must pay it; rather, Allah, the Exalted, retained it for His own sake, and the ruler who is His deputy on earth undertakes its collection and division. Obligatory for Allah: established for Him, the Exalted, no one has a right in it, established by itself: i.e., that right being established without attachment to the liability of the obligated person. For it is a strengthening of His religion, and in it is benefit for the world that is acquired, i.e., the property of spoils obtained through jihad. It is all His, as a favor from Him without them deserving it, for they are His slaves, and a slave has no right in what he does for his master. So it was not a right that we must fulfill as obedience to Him; rather, it is a right He retained for Himself, so the ruler, who is His deputy on earth, undertakes its collection and division. And therefore we permitted its expenditure to those who deserve four-fifths of the spoils, unlike zakat and charities, and it is permissible for Banu Hashim; because according to this verification, it did not become from the impurities.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the three categories of rights of Allah (huquq Allah) within the chapter on qiyas. The author explains each type: (1) rights with a predominant meaning of worship ('ubudiyya) like 'ushr (tithe on land), (2) rights with a predominant meaning of punitive sanction (uquba) like kharaj (land tax), and (3) rights that are inherently established (qa'im bi nafsihi) like khums (one-fifth of spoils and minerals). The commentary highlights the distinction between initial obligation and continuity: 'ushr is not initially imposed on a non-Muslim but can continue if a Muslim land passes to a non-Muslim (according to Imam Muhammad). Kharaj is not initially imposed on a Muslim but can continue if a Muslim acquires kharaj land. Khums is a right that belongs to Allah Himself, not as an obligation on individuals, hence it is collected by the ruler and can be given to the fighters and even to Banu Hashim, unlike zakat. The reasoning is based on the dominant aspect (ghalaba) of the meaning.

Key Terms
عشر ('ushr): A tithe on agricultural land, classified as a right of Allah with dominant meaning of worship ('ibada) but also containing meaning of maintenance (mu'na).
خراج (kharaj): A land tax on kharaj land, classified as a right of Allah with dominant meaning of punishment (uquba) but also maintenance.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of spoils and minerals, classified as a right established by itself (qa'im bi nafsihi), not attached to individuals' liability.
غلبة (ghalaba): Predominance; the principle that when a right has multiple meanings, the dominant one governs the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because Muslims are not qualified for punishment
B) Because kharaj is a form of worship
C) Because Muslims own the land
D) Because the ruler should collect it

Key Takeaway
The classification of a right of Allah depends on its predominant meaning (ghalaba), which determines initial obligation, continuity, and distribution rules.

The Real Cause (Sabab Haqiqi): Definition and Conditions
Defining sabab haqiqi with four conditions and distinguishing from illa, shart, and alama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sabab haqiqi, list its four conditions, and distinguish it from illa, shart, and alama using Hanafi usul criteria.

Core Idea
A real cause is a path to the ruling without attributing obligation or existence.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the real cause (sabab haqiqi) is essential for building sound qiyas. This passage precisely defines it through four negative conditions, setting it apart from the effective cause (illa), condition (shart), and sign (alama). We will unpack each condition and see the practical example of the thief's indication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four legal concepts introduced
The passage begins by listing sabab, illa, shart, and alama as the second division. Recognize that each plays a distinct role in linking an event to a ruling.
2
Extract the definition of sabab haqiqi
Find the core definition: 'a path to the ruling without attribution of obligation to it'. Note the three exclusionary phrases that follow.
The definition is built by negating attributes (obligation, existence, effect).
3
Analyze each of the four conditions
The passage uses four exclusions: (1) not atributing obligation → excludes illa; (2) not attributing existence → excludes shart; (3) not having any effect direct or indirect → excludes causes that contain meaning of illa; (4) not being a mere sign → excludes alama. Map each condition to the concept it excludes.
Condition (3) prevents sabab haqiqi from being confused with a cause that has influence.
4
Apply the definition to the thief example
Read the example: a person indicates a thief to steal. The indication leads to theft but does not necessitate it, and the thief's free act intervenes. Confirm that the indication meets all four conditions, so it is a real cause.
The thief's free will is an intervening cause (illa), but the indication remains a real cause because it does not necessitate nor have effect.
5
Distinguish sabab haqiqi from metaphorical cause
The passage notes that an oath by Allah is a metaphorical cause for expiation (kafarah) because it is not a path to the ruling in a real sense. Compare this with the real cause where the path is clear and the ruling is not attributed.
Metaphorical causes are not part of qiyas proper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني فأربعة: السبب والعلة والشرط والعلامة.
تعريف السبب وحكمه
أما السبب الحقيقي فما يكون طريقاً إلى الحكم من غير أن يضاف إليه وجوب للوصول إلى الحكم: أي مفضياً إلى الحكم في الجملة واحترز به عن العلامة، فإنها لاتفضي إلى الحكم بل هي دالة عليه، وعن سبب مجازي؛ فإنه لا يكون طريقاً إلى الحكم كاليمين بالله فإنه سبب مجازي للكفارة. وجوب: أي وجوب الحكم، واحترز بهذا القيد عن العلة؛ لأن الحكم يضاف وجوبه إلى العلة لكونها مؤثرا فيه.
ولا وجود أي لا يضاف إليه وجود الحكم كما يضاف إلى الشرط، فاحترز بهذا القيد عن الشرط. معاني العلل بوجه من الوجوه، أي لا يكون له تأثير في وجود الحكم أصلاً لا بواسطة ولا بغير واسطة؛ إذ لو كان كذلك لم يكن سبباً حقيقيا بل سببا له شبهة العلة أو سببا فيه معنى العلة والكلام في السبب الحقيقي عرفت من قوله : السبب الحقيقي واحترز بها عن هذين السببين ولما كان يتوهّم أن السبب الحقيقي هو الذي لا يتخلّل بينه وبين الحكم علة أصلاً دفعه بقوله: لكن يتخلل إلى إلخ.
الدلالة
العلة
وبين
إلى السبب المذكور؛ إذ لو تضاف العلة إلى السبب والحكم مضاف إلى العلة فيكون ذلك السبب علة العلة، ويسمّى سبباً فيه معنى العلة، فيكون سبباً حقيقياً. اعلم أن السبب أربعة أقسام: سبب حقيقي، فكما احترز عن العلة والشرط والعلامة كذلك احترز عن الأسباب الثلاثة، ولما رأى المصنف أن الرابع هو بعينه السبب المجازي، وعد المجازي من الأقسام ليس بمستحسن قسم السبب إلى ما فيه معنى العلة وإلى ما ليس كذلك، وسمى الثاني سبباً حقيقيا، ولما رأى أن اليمين وكذا التعليق سبب الكفارة والجزاء ليس بسبب حقيقي ولا سببا فيه معنى قال: فأما اليمين إلى أي هذا السبب مجازي، وهو قسم ثالث كما سيأتي تحقيقه. دلالة السارق على إلخ فمن دلّ السارق على مال رجل ليسرقه، فسرق السارق بدلالته، فدلالته سبب للسرقة؛ لأنها تفضي إليه من غير أن تكون موجبة له ولا تأثير لها في فعل السرقة ولكن تخلل بين السرقة علة، وهي فعل السارق المختار، وتلك العلة لاتضاف إلى الدلالة؛ إذ من دلالته لا يلزم أن يسرق السارق لا محالة بل قد لا يسرق - يوفقه الله على تركه والسبب لا يضاف إليه الحكم، فالسرقة لاتضاف إلى الدلالة، فلايضمن الدال شيئاً؛ لأنه صاحب سبب محض
And as for the second division, there are four: cause (sabab), effective cause (illa), condition (shart), and sign (alama). Definition of cause and its ruling: As for the real cause, it is that which is a path to the ruling without attribution of obligation to it, [leading] to the ruling in general. By this he excludes the sign, for it does not lead to the ruling but rather indicates it; and the metaphorical cause, for it is not a path to the ruling, like an oath by Allah, which is a metaphorical cause for expiation. 'Obligation': i.e., the obligation of the ruling, and by this restriction he excludes the effective cause (illa), because the obligation of the ruling is attributed to the illa due to it being influential in it. 'And no existence': i.e., existence is not attributed to it as it is attributed to the condition, so by this restriction he excludes the condition. 'Meanings of causes in any way': i.e., it has no effect in the existence of the ruling at all, neither directly nor indirectly. For if it were such, it would not be a real cause but rather a cause resembling the illa or a cause containing the meaning of illa. The discussion is about the real cause as known from his statement 'the real cause', and he excludes these two types. Since it might be misunderstood that the real cause is that which has no cause intervening between it and the ruling at all, he repels that by saying 'but there intervenes' etc. The indication, the illa, and between [them] to the mentioned cause; for if the intervening illa is attributed to the cause, and the ruling is attributed to the illa, then that cause becomes the cause of the illa, and it is called a cause containing the meaning of illa, and it becomes a real cause. Know that the cause has four divisions: a real cause, and just as he excluded the illa, condition, and sign, likewise he excluded the three types. And when the author saw that the fourth is the same as the metaphorical cause, and counting the metaphorical among the divisions is not commendable, he divided the cause into what contains the meaning of illa and what does not, and called the second a real cause. And when he saw that the oath and likewise the conditional clause are a cause for expiation and recompense, neither a real cause nor a cause containing meaning, he said: 'As for the oath' etc., i.e., this cause is metaphorical, and it is a third division as will come in its verification. The indication of the thief etc.: So he who indicates to a thief about a man's property to steal it, and the thief steals by his indication, his indication is a cause for the theft because it leads to it without being necessitating nor having effect in the act of theft, but there intervenes between [the indication] and the theft an illa, which is the free act of the thief, and that illa is not attributed to the indication; for from his indication it does not necessarily follow that the thief will steal, indeed he may not steal - God may guide him to leave it. And since the cause is not attributed to the ruling, the theft is not attributed to the indication, so the one who indicates does not guarantee anything because he is a mere cause-holder.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage defines the real cause (sabab haqiqi) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author explains that a real cause is a path leading to a ruling without the ruling's obligation or existence being attributed to it. This distinguishes it from the effective cause (illa), to which obligation is attributed; from the condition (shart), to which existence is attributed; and from the sign (alama), which only indicates the ruling. The real cause also lacks any effect on the ruling's existence, either directly or indirectly. The text then addresses a potential misunderstanding: some might think a real cause cannot have an intervening cause between it and the ruling. The author clarifies that an intervening cause is possible, as in the example of the thief's indication. In that example, the indication leads to theft but does not necessitate it; the thief's free will is the intervening cause. Therefore, the indicator is not liable because his action is a pure cause (sabab mahd). The passage also mentions that the author divided causes into real, those containing meaning of illa, and metaphorical. This is a key definition in Hanafi qiyas, setting the foundation for understanding how causes relate to rulings.

Key Terms
سبب حقيقي (sabab haqiqi): A real cause: that which is a path to the ruling without attribution of obligation or existence to it, and without having any effect in the existence of the ruling.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause: the ruling's obligation is attributed to it because it has influence (ta'thir) in the ruling.
الشرط (al-shart): Condition: that to which the existence of the ruling is attributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what distinguishes a real cause (sabab haqiqi) from an effective cause (illa)?
A) A real cause is always a path to the ruling, while an illa is not.
B) The obligation of the ruling is attributed to the illa, but not to a real cause.
C) A real cause has direct effect on the ruling's existence.
D) A real cause cannot have an intervening cause between it and the ruling.

Key Takeaway
A real cause (sabab haqiqi) is a path to a ruling without attributing its obligation, existence, or any effect to it, and it may have an intervening cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
The Effect of Immediate Divorce on Conditional Divorce: The Concept of Shubhat al-Haqiqah
Explains Hanafi ruling that tanjiz invalidates conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on why an immediate divorce (tanjiz) invalidates a conditional divorce (ta'liq) and apply the concept of shubhat al-haqiqah to distinguish it from Zufar's view.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce has a semblance of reality requiring a marital locus; an immediate divorce removes that locus.

In this lesson, we explore a key usul dispute within the Hanafi school: does an immediate divorce nullify a previously conditioned divorce? The majority Hanafi position, argued through shubhat al-haqiqah, holds that it does. Zufar disagreed, seeing the conditional divorce as pure metaphor. By examining the analogy with usurpation and the underlying logic, you will understand how Hanafi usul attributes legal effect to acts that are not real causes but have a resemblance to them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
What is the specific scenario? The husband says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced three times' and then immediately divorces her three times. She later remarries, is divorced, then returns to the first husband and enters the house. Does the conditional divorce take effect? This is the site of dispute between the Hanafis and Zufar.
This is a practical scenario that tests the interaction of two types of divorce: ta'liq (conditional) and tanjiz (immediate).
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof relies on the concept of shubhat al-haqiqah. The oath (or conditional divorce) is legislated to ensure fulfillment. Therefore, the penalty (divorce) has a semblance of obligation even before the condition occurs. This semblance requires a locus (the marriage). When the immediate divorce removes the marriage, the semblance's locus disappears, rendering the conditional divorce void.
The analogy with usurpation (ghasb) is used: just as the guarantee of value for a usurped object has a semblance of obligation requiring the object's existence, here too.
3
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that the conditional divorce is a pure metaphor with no semblance of reality. Therefore, it does not require a locus until the condition is actually fulfilled. The immediate divorce does not affect it because it only removes the locus for the conditional divorce's effect, but the conditional divorce itself remains in limbo.
Zufar analogizes to the case of a woman divorced three times: if a man says 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' the conditional divorce takes effect upon marriage even though the locus (marriage) did not exist at the time of the statement.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond by distinguishing the two cases. In the triple-divorce case, the condition (marriage) is the cause of the cause of divorce (ownership). Thus, the condition is like the cause itself, and suspending a ruling on its own cause is meaningless. That case is an exception and does not undermine the general principle that conditional divorces with shubhat al-haqiqah require a sustained locus.
The key distinction: in the triple-divorce case, the condition brings the cause into existence, so the semblance is different.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Consider a scenario where a husband conditionally divorces his wife upon her entering a house, then later kills her (removing the locus by death). Does the conditional divorce become void? Using the same logic, yes, because the locus (the wife) is gone. This shows the breadth of the principle.
This step helps solidify the concept of locus-dependence.

Source Text

شبهة الإيجاب. ذلك : أي كون هذا الشرط في حكم العلل السابقة عليه: أي على تحقق الشرط، والشبهة السابقة على تحقق الشرط وهي ثبوت السببية للمعلّق قبل تحقق الشرط، ووقوع الجزاء يقتضي وجود المحل كما مر ..... شبهة : أي شبهة السببية الحقيقة.
Chapter of Qiyas. Issue of Tanjiz. The cause and its ruling. Ruling, contrary to Zufar, may Allah be pleased with him, and that is clarified in the issue of tanjiz: does it invalidate the conditional suspension? According to us, it invalidates it because the oath is legislated for the fulfillment of the vow, so it is necessary that the fulfillment becomes guaranteed by the penalty. And when the fulfillment becomes guaranteed by the penalty, the thing by which the fulfillment is guaranteed acquires a semblance of obligation in the present moment... Likewise, the usurped object is guaranteed by its value, so for the usurpation, while the object still exists, there is a semblance of imposing the value after the loss... The meaning of the text: 'The thing by which the fulfillment is guaranteed (i.e., the penalty, such as emancipation or divorce) because the fulfillment is guaranteed by them, acquires a semblance of existence in the present moment, i.e., before the loss of the fulfillment.' So it is established that the oath is a metaphorical cause for the penalty and expiation, but not a pure cause; rather it has similarity to the real cause... The summary of this reasoning is that the conditional suspension, like the oath, even if not a real cause, has similarity to the real cause, and the real cause requires a locus, so similarly its semblance requires a locus... Zufar, because he did not pay attention to this, analogized it to the case where one suspends the divorce of a woman divorced three times or a foreign woman upon ownership by saying: 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' in which the divorce occurs after marriage, even though the initial locus did not exist. So he argued that the divorce in the disputed case is more likely because the locus exists at the end. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) responded by saying: 'Contrary to...' because the cause of divorce is ownership, which is obtained from marriage; thus the condition on which the divorce is suspended—i.e., marriage—is the cause of the cause of divorce, so it becomes in the ruling of the cause... And that condition is in the ruling of causes prior to it, and the semblance prior to the realization of the condition is the existence of causality for the suspended matter before the condition is realized, and the occurrence of the penalty requires the existence of the locus as mentioned...
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding whether an immediate divorce (tanjiz) invalidates a previously conditioned divorce (ta‘liq). The Hanafi position, as explained, is that it does invalidate it. The reasoning is based on the concept of 'shubhat al-haqiqah' (semblance of reality). A conditional divorce, like an oath, has a semblance of reality because it creates a guarantee of fulfillment (the penalty) even before the condition occurs. This semblance requires a locus (mahall), which is the marital bond. When the husband executes an immediate triple divorce, the locus is removed, and thus the conditional divorce becomes void. The opposing view of Zufar holds that the conditional divorce is purely metaphorical without any semblance, so it does not require a locus until the condition is fulfilled; thus the immediate divorce does not affect it. The Hanafi argument is supported by an analogy (qiyas) with a usurped object (ghasb): just as the guarantee of value for a usurped object has a semblance of obligation even before the object is lost, and this semblance requires the object's existence to be meaningful, so too does the conditional divorce's semblance require the continued existence of the marriage. The passage then distinguishes the case where a man says to a woman divorced three times, 'If I marry you, you are divorced.' Here, the condition (marriage) is the cause of the cause of divorce (ownership), so it is valid and the conditional divorce takes effect upon marriage, even though the initial locus (the marital bond) was absent. This is because the condition itself brings the cause into being, so the ruling is that the condition is like the cause itself, and suspending a ruling on its own cause is meaningless (like saying, 'If I free you, you are free' is void). Thus, the exception does not undermine the general principle.

Key Terms
شبهة الحقيقة (shubhat al-haqiqah): A semblance of reality that gives a legal construct (like a conditional divorce) some of the properties of a true cause, without being fully real.
تعليق (ta‘liq): Conditional suspension of a ruling upon the occurrence of a future event, e.g., divorce conditioned on entry into a house.
تنجيز (tanjiz): Immediate execution of a legal act without a condition, e.g., pronouncing divorce at once.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in the text, why does an immediate triple divorce invalidate a previously conditional divorce?
A) Because the conditional divorce becomes void as soon as the condition is stated.
B) Because the conditional divorce has a semblance of reality that requires a marital locus, and the immediate divorce removes that locus.
C) Because Zufar's ruling is weaker, so the Hanafi view must be followed.
D) Because the immediate divorce is stronger than the conditional one.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a conditional divorce, due to its semblance of reality, requires a sustained marital locus; an immediate full dissolution nullifies it.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Refuting Zufar's Qiyas: Direct Conditions vs. Causes of Causes
Refuting Imam Zufar's analogy by distinguishing direct conditions from causes of the cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a direct condition (ta'liq) and a condition that is a cause of the cause, and apply this distinction to evaluate the validity of analogies in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A direct condition requires its locus; a condition that brings about the cause does not.

This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami addresses a key dispute in Hanafi usul: what happens to a suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) when the husband later pronounces a triple divorce before the condition is fulfilled? Imam Zufar argues by analogy that the suspension remains valid, but the author rejects this as a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). By examining the distinction between a direct condition and a condition that is a cause of the cause, we uncover a fundamental principle about the role of shubhah (semblance) in causal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Find the case of ta'liq on entering the house (the disputed case) and the case of ta'liq on marriage to a thrice-divorced woman (the analogy). Note the conditions and loci involved.
The loci are marriage/ownership.
2
State the Hanafi position on the first case
The suspension becomes void because the marriage (the locus) is dissolved by the triple divorce, so the condition cannot be fulfilled.
This relies on the principle that shubhah (semblance of cause) needs a locus.
3
Understand Zufar's analogy
Zufar compares to the second case where the suspension is valid even though the locus (ownership) did not exist at the time of suspension.
He argues consistency: both have a future condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The condition in the second case (marriage) is not a direct condition but a cause of the cause (ownership). So it is treated as a cause-in-effect, not requiring prior locus. The first case's condition (entering) is direct and needs a locus at fulfillment.
This is the key distinction: direct condition vs. cause-of-cause.
5
Conclude the invalidity of Zufar's qiyas
Because the two cases differ in the nature of the condition, the analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The Hanafi ruling stands: the suspended divorce is void after triple talaq.
This illustrates the importance of precise causal analysis in usul.
