Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Two Ways the Nisāb Resembles a Sabab
Explaining the two ways nisāb resembles sabab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the two ways in which the nisāb resembles a sabab: (1) delay to what is not produced by it, and (2) delay to a description that is not an independent cause.

Core Idea
The nisāb resembles a sabab in two ways: its ruling is delayed to something external, and that something is not an independent cause.

In this lesson, we delve deeper into the two specific ways the nisāb of zakāh resembles a sabab, as outlined in the source passage. The first way is that the ruling is delayed to growth, which is not produced by the nisāb itself. The second way is that growth is not an independent 'illa but a description dependent on the nisāb. Understanding these two aspects clarifies why the nisāb is categorized as an 'illa resembling a sabab rather than a pure sabab or a pure 'illa.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Two Ways in the Text
The passage explicitly mentions 'بوجهين' (in two ways). Find these two explanations. The first is introduced by 'ألا ترى أنه إنما تراخى إلى ما ليس بحادث به' (Do you not see that it is delayed to what is not produced by it?). The second is 'وإلى ما هو شبيه بالعلل' (and to what is similar to causes). Identify each.
These two ways are the core of the resemblance to sabab.
2
Analyse the First Way: Delay to What Is Not Produced by the Nisāb
The text says the ruling is delayed to growth (namā'), which is not produced by the nisāb itself. Real growth (e.g., offspring, profit) and legal growth (yearly passage) do not arise from the nisāb alone; they depend on external factors like trade or pasture. This disconnection makes the nisāb resemble a sabab.
The commentary gives examples of real and legal growth to illustrate.
3
Analyse the Second Way: Delay to a Description That Resembles Causes
The second way is that the ruling is delayed to growth, which itself resembles a cause (شبيه بالعلل) but is not an independent 'illa. Growth is a description (waṣf) that is dependent on the nisāb (the root). Because this intermediate is not a fully independent cause, the nisāb's causal connection is weakened, making it resemble a sabab.
If growth were an independent 'illa, the nisāb would be a pure sabab. But it is not.
4
Compare the Two Ways with the Divorce Example
The text also gives the example of divorce pronounced for tomorrow. The pronouncement is an 'illa in name and meaning (it is the source of divorce), but its ruling is delayed to the future. This parallels the nisāb: the cause is there, but the effect is postponed.
This example reinforces the idea of deferred 'illa resembling sabab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
العلة وحكمها
وكذلك كل إيجاب مضاف إلى وقتٍ علةً اسما ومعنى لا حكماً لكنه يشبه الأسباب.
النصاب جعل علة بصفة النماء
وكذلك نصاب الزكاة في أول الحول علة اسماً؛ لأنه وضع له ومعنى لكونه مؤثراً أي النصاب في حكمه؛ لأن الغناء يوجب المواساة لكنه جعل علة بصفة النماء، فلما تراخي وهو الوجوب أي النصاب حكمه أشبه الأسباب. ألا ترى أنه إنما تراخى إلى ما ليس بحادث به، النصاب وهو علة إلى وقت مثل قوله: أنت طالق غداً، وهذا مثال ثالث له، فهذا الإيجاب علة اسما لكونه موضوعاً للحكم المضاف إليه، ومعنى لتأثيره في ذلك الحكم، لا حكما لتأخره إلى الزمان المضاف إليه وعدم ثبوته في الحال. يشبه الأسباب : لتخلّل الزمان بينه وبين الحكم، وعدم استناده إلى وجود العلة من حيث لا يثبت الحكم من وقت التكلم بل من غد علة لوجوب الزكاة، هذا مثال رابع.
بوجهين
لأنه إلخ : أي لأن نصاب الزكاة موضوع للوجوب شرعاً، ولذا يضاف الزكاة إليه. المواساة: أي الإحسان إلى الفقير، والغنى إنما يعتبر بالنصاب، فصار النصاب موجباً للمواساة التي يتحقق في أداء الزكاة. بصفة النماء: الذي أقيم حولان الحول مقامه، مثل إقامة السفر مقام المشقة كما ورد "لا زكاة في مال حتى يحول عليه الحول". حكمه أي حكم النصاب وهو وجوب الزكاة إلى وجود النماء، وهو ليس بعلة حقيقية؛ لأنه وصف غير مستقل بنفسه. الأسباب : نعم لو لم يكن الحكم متراخياً إلى النماء لكان النصاب علة من غير مشابهة بالأسباب، ولو كان النماء علة حقيقية للحكم لكان النصاب سبباً محضاً. ثم أوضح مشابهته بالأسباب أحدهما ما بينه بقوله : ألا ترى إلخ. بحادث به أعني النماء الذي تراخى إليه الحكم ليس بحادث أي ثابت بنفس النصاب؛ لأن النماء الحقيقي هو الدر والنسل والسمن في الحيوان وزيادة المال في التجارة، والحكمي هو حولان الحول، لا يحصل بنفس النصاب بل بسوم السائمة وعمل التجار وتغير الأسعار الحادث بصنعه تعالى، فلما تراخى الحكم إلى ما ليس بحادث به تأكد الانفصال بين النصاب وبين الحكم بأمر منفصل، وتحقق الشبهة بالسبب. أقول : فيه بحث؛ إذ لو كان ذلك علة لأوجب نفس السببية لا شبهها، فلذا حمل بعض الفضلاء هذا الكلام والكلام الآتي الذي هو دليل ثان على أنهما دليل واحد، بأن يقال: تراخى حكم النصاب إلى ما ليس بحادث به النماء الذي ليس بعلة مستقلة للحكم؛ لأنه وصف لا يستقل بنفسه، فيكون النصاب علة شبيها بالسبب.
وهو
وإلى ما هو شبيه بالعلل، ولما كان متراخياً إلى وصف لا يستقل بنفسه أشبه العلل،
الحكم
وهو النماء النصاب
وكان هذه الشبهة غالباً؛ لأن النصاب أصل، والنماء وصف، ومن حكمه أنه لايظهر وجوب الزكاة في أوّل الحول قطعاً بخلاف ما ذكرنا من البيوع. ولما أشبه العلل وكان ذلك أصلاً كان الوجوب ثابتاً من الأصل في التقدير
=
أي النصاب أو شبه العلل
أي وجوب الزكاة
النصاب
نعم لو كان النماء علةٌ مستقلة لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فافهم والثاني ما بينه بقوله: وإلى ما هو إلخ. شبيه بالعلل يعني النماء الذي تراخى إليه الحكم شبيه بالعلل وليس بعلة مستقلة كما مرّ، فلما لم يكن علة مستقلة كان النصاب شبيهاً بالسبب لا سبباً حقيقيا؛ إذ لو كان النماء المتوسطة علة حقيقية لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقياً كما بينا في دلالة السارق، ولما كان يتوهّم أن المتوسط بين النصاب والحكم هو النماء الذي ليس بعلة حقيقية فتردّد النصاب بين أن يكون علة يشبه السبب أو سبباً يشبه العلة؛ لأن المتوسط إذا يكون علة حقيقية يكون الأول سببا محضاً كما علمت في دلالة السارق، وإذا يكون المتوسط ما ليس بعلة حقيقية ولا شبيها بالعلة كان الأول علة حقيقية، وإذا كان المتوسط ما ليس بعلة ولكنه يشبه العلة فترد الأول بين الأمرين المذكورين، فلم قلتم النصاب علة يشبه السبب، ولم تقولوا بالعكس؟ فدفعه المصنف بقوله : ولما كان متراخيا إلخ. العلل: ولو كان النماء مستقلاً بنفسه لكان النصاب سببا حقيقيا، ولما لم يكن مستقلا لم يكن النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فلا محالة أشبه العلل. وكان هذه الشبهة إلخ يعني شبهة العلة للنصاب من جهة نفسه، وشبهة السبب من جهة توقف الحكم على النماء الذي هو وصفه وتابع له فترجّح الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة نفسه على الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة وصفه؛ لترجّح الأصل على الفرع فلذا قلنا: النصاب علة يشبه السبب لا العكس حكمه: أي حكم النصاب علة يشبه السبب. قطعا وقوله : "قطعا" داخل في النفي، والحاصل أن النصاب لما صار علة شبيهة بالسبب وتأخر حكمه إلى وجود النماء لا يمكن القول بوجوب الزكاة في أول الحول بطريق القطع لفوات وصف النماء؛ إذ العلة الموصوفة بوصف لا يعمل بدون الوصف.
الذي هو
من البيوع فإن العلة للملك، وهي البيع بنفسه ووصفه في البيع الموقوف والبيع بشرط الخيار، ولكن حق المالك والتعليق بالشرط كانا مانعين لثبوت الحكم وهو الملك، فلما زال المانع ثبت الحكم من حين العقد. أصلا والنماء فرعاً ووصفاً لايستقل بنفسه كما مرّ تقريره ثابتاً من الأصل إلخ: لأن النماء وصف لايستقلّ بالنصاب، فلما ثبت استند إلى أصل النصاب وصار من أول الحول متصفاً بأنه حولي كشجرة تبقى على الأرض بمائة سنة فيكون الموصوف هذا البقاء هي بعينها من أول ما نبتت فلما أسند النماء إلى النصاب من أول الحول أسند الوجوب الذي كان موقوفاً على النماء إلى النصاب أيضاً من أول الحول.
بنفسه
Chapter of Analogy
The 'illa and its ruling
And likewise every obligation attached to a time is an 'illa in name and meaning, not in ruling, but it resembles sabab.
The nisāb is made an 'illa with the attribute of growth
And likewise the nisāb of zakāh at the beginning of the year is an 'illa in name because it is placed for it, and in meaning for being effective, i.e., the nisāb in its ruling; because wealth necessitates charity, but it is made an 'illa with the attribute of growth. When it is delayed—and it is the obligation, i.e., the nisāb—its ruling resembles sabab. Do you not see that it is only delayed to what is not produced by it, the nisāb, being an 'illa for a time like your saying: You are divorced tomorrow. This is a third example. So this obligation is an 'illa in name for being the subject of the added ruling, and in meaning for its effect on that ruling, not in ruling due to its deferral to the added time and its non-establishment at present. It resembles sabab: because of the time intervening between it and the ruling, and its reliance on the existence of the 'illa in that the ruling is not established from the time of speech but from tomorrow—an 'illa for the obligation of zakāh. This is a fourth example.
In two ways
Because it is etc.: i.e., because the nisāb of zakāh is placed for obligation legally, therefore zakāh is attributed to it. Charity: i.e., beneficence to the poor, and wealth is only considered by the nisāb, so the nisāb becomes a cause of charity which is realized in performing zakāh. With the attribute of growth: the passing of the year is established in its place, like establishing travel in place of hardship, as narrated: 'No zakāh on wealth until a year passes over it.' Its ruling: i.e., the ruling of the nisāb, which is the obligation of zakāh until the existence of growth, and it is not a real 'illa because it is a description not independent by itself. Sabab: indeed, if the ruling were not delayed to growth, the nisāb would be an 'illa without resemblance to sabab, and if growth were a real 'illa for the ruling, the nisāb would be a pure sabab. Then he clarified its resemblance to sabab: one of them is what he explained by saying: Do you not see etc. What is not produced by it means growth, to which the ruling is delayed, is not produced, i.e., it is not established by the nisāb itself; because real growth is milk, offspring, fat in animals, and increase of wealth in trade; and legal growth is the passing of the year. It is not obtained by the nisāb itself but by pasture of livestock, work of merchants, and changes in prices occurring by His doing, exalted. So when the ruling is delayed to what is not produced by it, the separation between the nisāb and the ruling is strengthened by a separate matter, and the resemblance to sabab is realized. I say: there is discussion in it; for if that were an 'illa, it would necessitate causality itself, not its resemblance. Therefore, some virtuous people carried this speech and the following speech, which is a second proof, as being one proof, by saying: The ruling of the nisāb is delayed to what is not produced by it—growth—which is not an independent 'illa for the ruling, because it is a description that does not stand by itself, so the nisāb becomes an 'illa resembling sabab.

Indeed, if growth were an independent 'illa, the nisāb would be a real sabab. Understand, and the second is what he explained by saying: And to what is etc. Similar to causes means growth, to which the ruling is delayed, is similar to causes and not an independent 'illa as passed. So when it was not an independent 'illa, the nisāb became similar to sabab, not a real sabab; for if the intermediate growth were a real 'illa, the nisāb would be a pure sabab as we explained in the indication of the thief. And when it is imagined that the intermediate between the nisāb and the ruling is growth, which is not a real 'illa, the nisāb wavers between being an 'illa resembling sabab or a sabab resembling 'illa; because when the intermediate is a real 'illa, the first is a pure sabab, as you know from the indication of the thief; and when the intermediate is not a real 'illa and not similar to 'illa, the first is a real 'illa; and when the intermediate is not a 'illa but resembles 'illa, the first wavers between the two mentioned cases. So why did you say the nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab, and why did you not say the opposite? The author repelled it by saying: And when it is delayed etc. The causes: and if growth were independent by itself, the nisāb would be a real sabab, and when it was not independent, the nisāb was not a real sabab, so necessarily it resembles causes. And this resemblance etc. means the resemblance of 'illa to the nisāb from the aspect of itself, and the resemblance of sabab from the aspect of the ruling being dependent on growth, which is its description and follower. So the resemblance obtained from the aspect of itself outweighed the resemblance obtained from the aspect of its description; due to the precedence of the root over the branch, therefore we said: the nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab, not the opposite. Its ruling: i.e., the ruling of the nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab. Definitely, and his saying: 'definitely' is included in the negation. The conclusion is that when the nisāb became an 'illa resembling sabab and its ruling was delayed to the existence of growth, it is not possible to say that zakāh is obligatory at the beginning of the year definitively due to the absence of the attribute of growth; for the 'illa described with a description does not work without the description.

from sales, for the 'illa for ownership is the sale itself and its description in the suspended sale and the sale with a condition of option, but the right of the owner and the suspension with a condition were preventers of the establishment of the ruling, which is ownership. When the preventer was removed, the ruling was established from the time of the contract. A root, and growth is a branch and a description that does not stand by itself as passed in its elaboration. So when growth was attributed to the nisāb from the beginning of the year, the obligation that was suspended on growth was also attributed to the nisāb from the beginning of the year.

Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary defines the concept of 'illa (cause) and its relationship to sabab (occasion). The author begins by stating that every obligation attached to a time is an 'illa in name and meaning but not in ruling, and it resembles sabab. The key example is the nisāb (minimum threshold) for zakāh: at the start of the year, the nisāb is an 'illa in name because it is the subject of the obligation, and in meaning because it is effective in bringing about charity, but its ruling (obligation) is delayed until the growth (namā') of wealth occurs. Because the ruling is deferred, the nisāb resembles a sabab (mere occasion) rather than a true 'illa. The text then provides multiple examples, including the analogy of divorce pronounced for tomorrow, to illustrate that a deferred 'illa functions like a sabab. The commentary elaborates by clarifying the distinction between real growth (e.g., produce, offspring) and legal growth (the passing of a year), and argues that because growth is not directly caused by the nisāb, the nisāb's causation is incomplete, making it more like a sabab. The text also addresses a potential objection: why is the nisāb considered an 'illa resembling sabab rather than a sabab resembling 'illa? The author explains that because the nisāb is the root (aṣl) and growth is a description (waṣf) dependent on it, the resemblance to 'illa is predominant. However, since the ruling is delayed to a description that is not independent, the nisāb ultimately resembles a sabab. This discussion shows the Hanafi precision in categorizing causes and their effects within qiyās.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that brings about a ruling; in this passage, it is distinguished between 'illa in name and meaning vs. 'illa in ruling.
السبب (as-sabab): An occasion or external factor that triggers a ruling but does not itself possess causal efficacy; it is distinguished from 'illa by the lack of intrinsic effect.
النصاب (an-nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakāh obligatory; in this passage, it is the subject of the 'illa.
النماء (an-namā'): Growth or increase, both real (like produce) and legal (the passing of a year); it is the description that completes the 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the second way the nisāb resembles a sabab?
A) The ruling is delayed to a time that is not defined.
B) The ruling is delayed to growth, which is not an independent 'illa.
C) The nisāb is not the subject of the obligation.
D) The nisāb produces growth directly.

Key Takeaway
The nisāb resembles a sabab in two ways: its ruling is delayed to something external (growth) and that something is a dependent description, not an independent cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Resolving the Classification: Why Nisāb Is an 'Illa Resembling Sabab
Resolving the classification of nisāb as 'illa resembling sabab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to defend the Hanafi classification that the nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab (not a sabab resembling 'illa) by applying the principle that the root (aṣl) outweighs the description (waṣf).

Core Idea
The nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab because the root (aṣl) dominates the description (waṣf), making the causal link stronger than the temporal gap.

This lesson resolves a potential objection: why do Hanafi scholars classify the nisāb as an 'illa resembling sabab rather than the reverse (a sabab resembling 'illa)? The source passage explains that the nisāb is the root (aṣl) and growth is a description (waṣf) dependent on it. Since the root takes precedence, the nisāb retains enough causal efficacy to be considered an 'illa, though the delay makes it resemble a sabab. This resolution highlights how Hanafi usul balances multiple factors in classification.

Guided Path
1
State the Objection
The text raises the question: why not say the nisāb is a sabab resembling 'illa? After all, the ruling is delayed to an external factor. Identify the exact phrasing: 'فلم قلتم النصاب علة يشبه السبب، ولم تقولوا بالعكس؟'
This is the critical question that drives the resolution.
2
Identify the Author's Response
The author responds by stating: 'ولما كان متراخيا إلى وصف لا يستقل بنفسه' (and when it is delayed to a description that does not stand by itself). This shows that because growth is a dependent description, the nisāb's own causal nature is not overridden.
The key is the dependency of growth on the nisāb.
3
Apply the Principle of Root over Description
The passage explains: 'وكان هذه الشبهة غالباً لأن النصاب أصل والنماء وصف' (this resemblance is predominant because the nisāb is a root and growth is a description). The root (aṣl) takes precedence over the branch (far') or description. So the nisāb's intrinsic causal link is stronger than the deferral effect.
This is a Hanafi principle: the original cause is prioritized over secondary attributes.
4
Conclude with the Muftā Bihī Classification
The final ruling is that the nisāb is an 'illa resembling sabab (علة تشبه السبب). This means it is still an 'illa in essence, but its ruling is deferred, giving it the appearance of a sabab. The text also clarifies the practical consequence: zakāh is not definitively obligatory at the beginning of the year due to the missing description (growth).
Understanding this classification is essential for applying qiyās correctly.

باب القياس
العلة وحكمها
وكذلك كل إيجاب مضاف إلى وقتٍ علةً اسما ومعنى لا حكماً لكنه يشبه الأسباب.
النصاب جعل علة بصفة النماء
وكذلك نصاب الزكاة في أول الحول علة اسماً؛ لأنه وضع له ومعنى لكونه مؤثراً أي النصاب في حكمه؛ لأن الغناء يوجب المواساة لكنه جعل علة بصفة النماء، فلما تراخي وهو الوجوب أي النصاب حكمه أشبه الأسباب. ألا ترى أنه إنما تراخى إلى ما ليس بحادث به، النصاب وهو علة إلى وقت مثل قوله: أنت طالق غداً، وهذا مثال ثالث له، فهذا الإيجاب علة اسما لكونه موضوعاً للحكم المضاف إليه، ومعنى لتأثيره في ذلك الحكم، لا حكما لتأخره إلى الزمان المضاف إليه وعدم ثبوته في الحال. يشبه الأسباب : لتخلّل الزمان بينه وبين الحكم، وعدم استناده إلى وجود العلة من حيث لا يثبت الحكم من وقت التكلم بل من غد علة لوجوب الزكاة، هذا مثال رابع.
بوجهين
لأنه إلخ : أي لأن نصاب الزكاة موضوع للوجوب شرعاً، ولذا يضاف الزكاة إليه. المواساة: أي الإحسان إلى الفقير، والغنى إنما يعتبر بالنصاب، فصار النصاب موجباً للمواساة التي يتحقق في أداء الزكاة. بصفة النماء: الذي أقيم حولان الحول مقامه، مثل إقامة السفر مقام المشقة كما ورد "لا زكاة في مال حتى يحول عليه الحول". حكمه أي حكم النصاب وهو وجوب الزكاة إلى وجود النماء، وهو ليس بعلة حقيقية؛ لأنه وصف غير مستقل بنفسه. الأسباب : نعم لو لم يكن الحكم متراخياً إلى النماء لكان النصاب علة من غير مشابهة بالأسباب، ولو كان النماء علة حقيقية للحكم لكان النصاب سبباً محضاً. ثم أوضح مشابهته بالأسباب أحدهما ما بينه بقوله : ألا ترى إلخ. بحادث به أعني النماء الذي تراخى إليه الحكم ليس بحادث أي ثابت بنفس النصاب؛ لأن النماء الحقيقي هو الدر والنسل والسمن في الحيوان وزيادة المال في التجارة، والحكمي هو حولان الحول، لا يحصل بنفس النصاب بل بسوم السائمة وعمل التجار وتغير الأسعار الحادث بصنعه تعالى، فلما تراخى الحكم إلى ما ليس بحادث به تأكد الانفصال بين النصاب وبين الحكم بأمر منفصل، وتحقق الشبهة بالسبب. أقول : فيه بحث؛ إذ لو كان ذلك علة لأوجب نفس السببية لا شبهها، فلذا حمل بعض الفضلاء هذا الكلام والكلام الآتي الذي هو دليل ثان على أنهما دليل واحد، بأن يقال: تراخى حكم النصاب إلى ما ليس بحادث به النماء الذي ليس بعلة مستقلة للحكم؛ لأنه وصف لا يستقل بنفسه، فيكون النصاب علة شبيها بالسبب.
وهو
وإلى ما هو شبيه بالعلل، ولما كان متراخياً إلى وصف لا يستقل بنفسه أشبه العلل،
الحكم
وهو النماء النصاب
وكان هذه الشبهة غالباً؛ لأن النصاب أصل، والنماء وصف، ومن حكمه أنه لايظهر وجوب الزكاة في أوّل الحول قطعاً بخلاف ما ذكرنا من البيوع. ولما أشبه العلل وكان ذلك أصلاً كان الوجوب ثابتاً من الأصل في التقدير
=
أي النصاب أو شبه العلل
أي وجوب الزكاة
النصاب
نعم لو كان النماء علةٌ مستقلة لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فافهم والثاني ما بينه بقوله: وإلى ما هو إلخ. شبيه بالعلل يعني النماء الذي تراخى إليه الحكم شبيه بالعلل وليس بعلة مستقلة كما مرّ، فلما لم يكن علة مستقلة كان النصاب شبيهاً بالسبب لا سبباً حقيقيا؛ إذ لو كان النماء المتوسطة علة حقيقية لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقياً كما بينا في دلالة السارق، ولما كان يتوهّم أن المتوسط بين النصاب والحكم هو النماء الذي ليس بعلة حقيقية فتردّد النصاب بين أن يكون علة يشبه السبب أو سبباً يشبه العلة؛ لأن المتوسط إذا يكون علة حقيقية يكون الأول سببا محضاً كما علمت في دلالة السارق، وإذا يكون المتوسط ما ليس بعلة حقيقية ولا شبيها بالعلة كان الأول علة حقيقية، وإذا كان المتوسط ما ليس بعلة ولكنه يشبه العلة فترد الأول بين الأمرين المذكورين، فلم قلتم النصاب علة يشبه السبب، ولم تقولوا بالعكس؟ فدفعه المصنف بقوله : ولما كان متراخيا إلخ. العلل: ولو كان النماء مستقلاً بنفسه لكان النصاب سببا حقيقيا، ولما لم يكن مستقلا لم يكن النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فلا محالة أشبه العلل. وكان هذه الشبهة إلخ يعني شبهة العلة للنصاب من جهة نفسه، وشبهة السبب من جهة توقف الحكم على النماء الذي هو وصفه وتابع له فترجّح الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة نفسه على الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة وصفه؛ لترجّح الأصل على الفرع فلذا قلنا: النصاب علة يشبه السبب لا العكس حكمه: أي حكم النصاب علة يشبه السبب. قطعا وقوله : "قطعا" داخل في النفي، والحاصل أن النصاب لما صار علة شبيهة بالسبب وتأخر حكمه إلى وجود النماء لا يمكن القول بوجوب الزكاة في أول الحول بطريق القطع لفوات وصف النماء؛ إذ العلة الموصوفة بوصف لا يعمل بدون الوصف.
الذي هو
من البيوع فإن العلة للملك، وهي البيع بنفسه ووصفه في البيع الموقوف والبيع بشرط الخيار، ولكن حق المالك والتعليق بالشرط كانا مانعين لثبوت الحكم وهو الملك، فلما زال المانع ثبت الحكم من حين العقد. أصلا والنماء فرعاً ووصفاً لايستقل بنفسه كما مرّ تقريره ثابتاً من الأصل إلخ: لأن النماء وصف لايستقلّ بالنصاب، فلما ثبت استند إلى أصل النصاب وصار من أول الحول متصفاً بأنه حولي كشجرة تبقى على الأرض بمائة سنة فيكون الموصوف هذا البقاء هي بعينها من أول ما نبتت فلما أسند النماء إلى النصاب من أول الحول أسند الوجوب الذي كان موقوفاً على النماء إلى النصاب أيضاً من أول الحول.

Chapter of Analogy
The 'illa and its ruling
And likewise every obligation attached to a time is an 'illa in name and meaning, not in ruling, but it resembles sabab.
The nisāb is made an 'illa with the attribute of growth
And likewise the nisāb of zakāh at the beginning of the year is an 'illa in name because it is placed for it, and in meaning for being effective, i.e., the nisāb in its ruling; because wealth necessitates charity, but it is made an 'illa with the attribute of growth. When it is delayed—and it is the obligation, i.e., the nisāb—its ruling resembles sabab. Do you not see that it is only delayed to what is not produced by it, the nisāb, being an 'illa for a time like your saying: You are divorced tomorrow. This is a third example. So this obligation is an 'illa in name for being the subject of the added ruling, and in meaning for its effect on that ruling, not in ruling due to its deferral to the added time and its non-establishment at present. It resembles sabab: because of the time intervening between it and the ruling, and its reliance on the existence of the 'illa in that the ruling is not established from the time of speech but from tomorrow—an 'illa for the obligation of zakāh. This is a fourth example.

Because it is etc.: i.e., because the nisāb of zakāh is placed for obligation legally, therefore zakāh is attributed to it. Charity: i.e., beneficence to the poor, and wealth is only considered by the nisāb, so the nisāb becomes a cause of charity which is realized in performing zakāh. With the attribute of growth: the passing of the year is established in its place, like establishing travel in place of hardship, as narrated: 'No zakāh on wealth until a year passes over it.' Its ruling: i.e., the ruling of the nisāb, which is the obligation of zakāh until the existence of growth, and it is not a real 'illa because it is a description not independent by itself. Sabab: indeed, if the ruling were not delayed to growth, the nisāb would be an 'illa without resemblance to sabab, and if growth were a real 'illa for the ruling, the nisāb would be a pure sabab. Then he clarified its resemblance to sabab: one of them is what he explained by saying: Do you not see etc. What is not produced by it means growth, to which the ruling is delayed, is not produced, i.e., it is not established by the nisāb itself; because real growth is milk, offspring, fat in animals, and increase of wealth in trade; and legal growth is the passing of the year. Established from the root etc.: because growth is a description that does not stand by the nisāb. So when it was established, it relied on the root of the nisāb and became from the beginning of the year described as annual, like a tree that remains on the ground for a hundred years; the described thing, this remaining, is the very same from the beginning of its growth. So when growth was attributed to the nisāb from the beginning of the year, the obligation that was suspended on growth was also attributed to the nisāb from the beginning of the year.
by itself
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary defines the concept of 'illa (cause) and its relationship to sabab (occasion). The author begins by stating that every obligation attached to a time is an 'illa in name and meaning but not in ruling, and it resembles sabab. The key example is the nisāb (minimum threshold) for zakāh: at the start of the year, the nisāb is an 'illa in name because it is the subject of the obligation, and in meaning because it is effective in bringing about charity, but its ruling (obligation) is delayed until the growth (namā') of wealth occurs. Because the ruling is deferred, the nisāb resembles a sabab (mere occasion) rather than a true 'illa. The text then provides multiple examples, including the analogy of divorce pronounced for tomorrow, to illustrate that a deferred 'illa functions like a sabab. The commentary elaborates by clarifying the distinction between real growth (e.g., produce, offspring) and legal growth (the passing of a year), and argues that because growth is not directly caused by the nisāb, the nisāb's causation is incomplete, making it more like a sabab. The text also addresses a potential objection: why is the nisāb considered an 'illa resembling sabab rather than a sabab resembling 'illa? The author explains that because the nisāb is the root (aṣl) and growth is a description (waṣf) dependent on it, the resemblance to 'illa is predominant. However, since the ruling is delayed to a description that is not independent, the nisāb ultimately resembles a sabab. This discussion shows the Hanafi precision in categorizing causes and their effects within qiyās.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that brings about a ruling; in this passage, it is distinguished between 'illa in name and meaning vs. 'illa in ruling.
السبب (as-sabab): An occasion or external factor that triggers a ruling but does not itself possess causal efficacy; it is distinguished from 'illa by the lack of intrinsic effect.
النصاب (an-nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakāh obligatory; in this passage, it is the subject of the 'illa.
النماء (an-namā'): Growth or increase, both real (like produce) and legal (the passing of a year); it is the description that completes the 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school classify the nisāb as an 'illa resembling sabab rather than a sabab resembling 'illa?
A) Because the nisāb independently produces the ruling.
B) Because the nisāb is the root and growth is a description, and the root outweighs the description.
C) Because the ruling is not delayed at all.
D) Because growth is an independent 'illa.

Key Takeaway
The nisāb is classified as an 'illa resembling sabab because it is the root (aṣl) and the deferring factor (growth) is a dependent description, making the causal link stronger than the temporal gap.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
Types of 'Illah: Zakat and Marad al-Mawt Examples
Defines categories of 'illah in qiyas with two examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the nisab and death illness as causes ('illah) that resemble causes (sabab) and apply the Hanafi usul principle to determine the permissibility of advancing zakat before the year.

Core Idea
A cause delayed to a description resembles a sabab, but its strength depends on whether the description arises from it.

In Hanafi usul, the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas is not always straightforward. Some causes are delayed in their effect until a description is present. This lesson explores two key examples: the nisab for zakat and death illness (marad al-mawt). Both are 'illah that resemble causes (sabab), but with a crucial difference. Understanding this classification helps resolve practical issues like advancing zakat payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples
Recognize the nisab (minimum wealth threshold) with its description of growth (nama) and death illness (marad al-mawt) with its description of connection to death (ittisal bi al-mawt).
Both examples are used to illustrate 'illah that are not fully independent.
2
Analyse why they resemble sabab
For both, the ruling (zakat obligation or death restrictions) is delayed to a description that does not stand alone. This makes them 'illah that resemble sabab, not true 'illah.
The description is dependent on the origin.
3
Compare the strength of resemblance
Death illness is more like a true cause because the description of connection to death arises from the illness itself, whereas the growth (nama) is external to the nisab. Thus, marad al-mawt is more resembling a true 'illah than the nisab.
Hanafi: the cause's strength depends on whether the description is intrinsic or extrinsic.
4
Derive the ruling on ta'jil al-zakat
Because the nisab resembles a sabab and the description of growth is attributed back to the beginning of the year (like a tree that remains for years), advancing zakat before the year is valid when the year later completes.
This is the Hanafi position; contrast with Malik.
5
Identify the ikhtilaf with Malik
Malik considers the nisab an incomplete cause (like a cause with two descriptions), so he disallows advancing zakat. The Hanafi response insists the description of growth is attached from the start.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi may pay early, Maliki must wait.

النصاب
نعم لو كان النماء علةٌ مستقلة لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فافهم والثاني ما بينه بقوله: وإلى ما هو إلخ. شبيه بالعلل يعني النماء الذي تراخى إليه الحكم شبيه بالعلل وليس بعلة مستقلة كما مرّ، فلما لم يكن علة مستقلة كان النصاب شبيهاً بالسبب لا سبباً حقيقيا؛ إذ لو كان النماء المتوسطة علة حقيقية لكان النصاب سبباً حقيقياً كما بينا في دلالة السارق، ولما كان يتوهّم أن المتوسط بين النصاب والحكم هو النماء الذي ليس بعلة حقيقية فتردّد النصاب بين أن يكون علة يشبه السبب أو سبباً يشبه العلة؛ لأن المتوسط إذا يكون علة حقيقية يكون الأول سببا محضاً كما علمت في دلالة السارق، وإذا يكون المتوسط ما ليس بعلة حقيقية ولا شبيها بالعلة كان الأول علة حقيقية، وإذا كان المتوسط ما ليس بعلة ولكنه يشبه العلة فترد الأول بين الأمرين المذكورين، فلم قلتم النصاب علة يشبه السبب، ولم تقولوا بالعكس؟ فدفعه المصنف بقوله : ولما كان متراخيا إلخ. العلل: ولو كان النماء مستقلاً بنفسه لكان النصاب سببا حقيقيا، ولما لم يكن مستقلا لم يكن النصاب سبباً حقيقيا، فلا محالة أشبه العلل. وكان هذه الشبهة إلخ يعني شبهة العلة للنصاب من جهة نفسه، وشبهة السبب من جهة توقف الحكم على النماء الذي هو وصفه وتابع له فترجّح الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة نفسه على الشبهة الذي حصل من جهة وصفه؛ لترجّح الأصل على الفرع فلذا قلنا: النصاب علة يشبه السبب لا العكس حكمه: أي حكم النصاب علة يشبه السبب. قطعا وقوله : "قطعا" داخل في النفي، والحاصل أن النصاب لما صار علة شبيهة بالسبب وتأخر حكمه إلى وجود النماء لا يمكن القول بوجوب الزكاة في أول الحول بطريق القطع لفوات وصف النماء؛ إذ العلة الموصوفة بوصف لا يعمل بدون الوصف.
الذي هو
من البيوع فإن العلة للملك، وهي البيع بنفسه ووصفه في البيع الموقوف والبيع بشرط الخيار، ولكن حق المالك والتعليق بالشرط كانا مانعين لثبوت الحكم وهو الملك، فلما زال المانع ثبت الحكم من حين العقد. أصلا والنماء فرعاً ووصفاً لايستقل بنفسه كما مرّ تقريره ثابتاً من الأصل إلخ: لأن النماء وصف لايستقلّ بالنصاب، فلما ثبت استند إلى أصل النصاب وصار من أول الحول متصفاً بأنه حولي كشجرة تبقى على الأرض بمائة سنة فيكون الموصوف هذا البقاء هي بعينها من أول ما نبتت فلما أسند النماء إلى النصاب من أول الحول أسند الوجوب الذي كان موقوفاً على النماء إلى النصاب أيضاً من أول الحول.

Chapter of Analogy. The cause and its ruling. And to what resembles causes, and since it is delayed to a description that does not stand alone, it resembles causes. The ruling: and it is the growth, the nisab. And this resemblance was predominant because the nisab is an origin and the growth is a description, and from its ruling is that the obligation of zakat does not appear at the beginning of the year definitively, unlike what we mentioned regarding sales. And since it resembled causes and that was an origin, the obligation was established from the origin in estimation. = i.e., the nisab or resembling causes. i.e., the obligation of zakat. The nisab. Yes, if the growth were an independent cause, the nisab would be a real cause (sabab). Understand. And the second is what he clarified by his statement: 'and to what is resembling causes' meaning the growth that the ruling is delayed to resembles causes and is not an independent cause as passed. So since it was not an independent cause, the nisab became similar to a cause (sabab) not a real cause; because if the intermediary growth were a real cause, the nisab would be a real cause as we explained in the indication of the thief. And since it might be imagined that the intermediary between the nisab and the ruling is the growth that is not a real cause, so the nisab is uncertain between being a cause that resembles a sabab or a sabab that resembles a cause; because if the intermediary is a real cause, the first is a pure sabab as you learned in the indication of the thief; and if the intermediary is not a real cause nor resembling a cause, the first is a real cause; and if the intermediary is not a cause but resembles a cause, the first is uncertain between the two mentioned matters. So why did you say the nisab is a cause resembling a sabab and not the opposite? He repelled this by his statement: 'and since it is delayed...' etc. The causes: and if the growth were independent by itself, the nisab would be a real sabab; and since it was not independent, the nisab was not a real sabab, so inevitably it resembles causes. And this resemblance etc. means the resemblance of the cause to the nisab from its own aspect, and the resemblance of the sabab from the aspect of the ruling's dependence on the growth which is its description and subordinate to it. So the resemblance obtained from its own aspect outweighed the resemblance obtained from the aspect of its description due to the precedence of the origin over the branch. Therefore we said: the nisab is a cause resembling a sabab, not the opposite. Its ruling: meaning the ruling of the nisab as a cause resembling a sabab. Definitively. And his statement 'definitively' is included in the negation. The summary is that when the nisab became a cause resembling a sabab and its ruling was delayed to the existence of growth, it is not possible to say that zakat is obligatory at the beginning of the year in a definitive way due to the absence of the description of growth; because a cause described with a description does not operate without the description. Which is from sales: for the cause of ownership is the sale itself and its description in the suspended sale and the sale with the option of stipulation, but the right of the owner and the suspension by condition were preventers of the establishment of the ruling (ownership). So when the preventer was removed, the ruling was established from the time of the contract. The origin and the growth are a branch and a description that does not stand alone as passed its explanation. 'Established from the origin' etc.: because the growth is a description that does not stand alone with the nisab, so when it was established, it attributed to the origin of the nisab and from the beginning of the year became described as annual, like a tree that remains on the earth for a hundred years, so the described (the tree) is this remaining itself from when it first grew. So when the growth was attributed to the nisab from the beginning of the year, the obligation that was dependent on the growth was also attributed to the nisab from the beginning of the year. By itself. It becomes after the year, and likewise the illness of death is a cause for the change of rulings until the advancement is valid, but it is zakat (i.e., the accelerated zakat). The rulings in name and meaning except that its ruling is established by it with the description of connection to death, so it resembles causes from this aspect, and it is a cause in reality, and this is more resembling causes than the nisab. · The advancement: i.e., advancing zakat before the completion of the year due to the existence of the origin of the cause after the year and the absence of the description of the cause in the present. So when the year completes and its nisab is complete, the paid amount is valid as zakat because the description is attributed to the beginning of the year, contrary to Malik because the nisab before the completion of the year does not have the ruling of a cause according to him, and its being growing by the year is like the last description of a cause with two descriptions, so it is not permissible to advance zakat before the year according to him, just as it is not permissible to advance expiation before the oath. Al-Shafi'i said to him: the nisab before the year is a complete cause for the obligation of zakat with no resemblance of causes in it. And if the description of being annual were from the cause, advancement before it would not be valid, just as advancement before the nisab is not valid. Rather, the year is merely a time for demand from the owner as a convenience for him. So according to him, if he pays before the completion of the year, the paid amount counts as zakat without being conditional upon the arrival of the term, like a debtor who pays the debt before the term. And if it counts as zakat, he cannot take it back from the poor person before the year. A cause for the change of rulings related to his wealth, such as the attachment of the heir's right and the restriction of the sick patient from donating more than a third. In name: because it is placed in the Sharia for the change from freedom to restriction. And in meaning: because it is effective in restricting transactions beyond a third, as mentioned in the hadith of Sa'd. And since it was not a cause for a divine ruling, he indicated: except that its ruling etc. means the ruling of death illness, which is the restriction on transactions, is established by the illness with the description of its connection to death, like the nisab whose ruling was dependent on the description of growth. So when its ruling was delayed to the description of connection, it resembles causes, and in reality it is a cause. The reason for our statement 'its ruling was delayed to the description of connection' is that if a sick patient gives away all his wealth and hands it over to the recipient, it becomes his ownership immediately, because the cause that prevents transactions – which is death illness – did not exist with its description (connection to death). So if the patient dies afterwards, the cause is completed with its description and what exceeds one-third is taken back, and this description is attributed to the first appearance of the illness. And if the description is attributed to the beginning of the illness, its ruling (the restriction) is also attributed, so it becomes as if he transacted after the restriction. And if he recovers from the illness, his transaction is effective because the cause was not completed with its description. 'More resembling causes' etc. means the illness is more resembling causes than the nisab, because the description of connection that the ruling is delayed to arises from the illness; because the pains that lead to death arise from the illness, unlike the growth, which does not arise from the nisab as you have known. So since the description of connection is not an external thing due to its arising from the illness, the illness's ruling does not depend on another matter, unlike the nisab. Therefore, its causality for the ruling is stronger than that of the nisab. And this is a fifth example for him, and some counted this example and the following example (buying a relative) as examples of the cause that is in the category of causes (i.e., a cause resembling causes). And Fakhr al-Islam made the ambiguous cause...
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the classification of the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author distinguishes between a true 'illah (which operates independently) and a 'illah that resembles a cause (sabab) because its effect is delayed to a description. The main example is the nisab (minimum wealth threshold) for zakat. The nisab is considered a 'illah for zakat, but its effect (obligation) is not immediate; it depends on the description of growth (nama) over the year. Thus, the nisab is a 'illah that resembles a sabab. The author explains why it is not a real sabab: if nama were an independent 'illah, nisab would be a real sabab, but since nama is not independent, nisab becomes a 'illah resembling a sabab. The discussion includes a comparison with sales (where ownership is immediate) and an analogy with the thief's hand (where the intermediate step is a real 'illah). The author then addresses a potential objection about why nisab is considered a 'illah resembling a sabab rather than a sabab resembling a 'illah, responding that the preponderance of the nisab's own resemblance over its description's resemblance leads to the former classification. A second example is marad al-mawt (death illness). This is a 'illah for restricting the patient's transactions, but its effect (hijr) depends on the description of connection to death (ittisal bi al-mawt). Thus, it too resembles a sabab, but it is more like a true 'illah than the nisab because the description of connection arises from the illness itself. The passage also records a dispute with Imam Malik regarding advancing zakat before the year: Malik disallows it because nisab is not a complete 'illah for him; al-Shafi'i allows it because he considers nisab a complete 'illah. The Hanafi position agrees with allowing advancement due to the attribution of the description to the beginning of the year.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illah): A cause that necessitates a ruling, either immediately or through a description.
السبب (as-sabab): A cause that is external and real, not dependent on a description.
النماء (an-nama): The description of growth that triggers zakat obligation after a year.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Death illness; a cause for legal restrictions on transactions beyond one-third of wealth.
التعجيل (at-ta'jil): Advancing zakat payment before the end of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author classify the nisab as a 'illah that resembles a sabab rather than a sabab resembling a 'illah?
A) Because the nisab is the origin and the growth is a description, and the origin outweighs the branch.
B) Because the growth is an independent cause.
C) Because the nisab is a real sabab in all cases.
D) Because the description of growth is external to the nisab.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a cause whose effect is delayed to a dependent description is classified as a 'illah resembling a sabab, and the strength of that resemblance depends on whether the description arises from the cause itself or is external.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The 'Illa in Name and Meaning Without Immediate Legal Effect: Marad al-Mawt and Zakat Examples
Defines a type of 'illa that is effective in name and meaning but not in ruling, using marad al-mawt and the zakat advance payment debate as examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of an 'illa that is asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman, explain the Hanafi position on advance payment of zakat, and apply this concept to analyze marad al-mawt rulings.

Core Idea
An 'illa may be recognized legally yet require a second description to produce its ruling – it then functions like a sabab.

In Hanafi usul, not every recognized cause ( 'illa) immediately generates its legal effect. Some causes are effective only in name and meaning but not in ruling; their ruling depends on an additional description. This passage from the Muntakhab explores such a cause through marad al-mawt (mortal illness) and compares it to the nisab for zakat. Understanding this nuance is essential to grasp how Hanafi jurists treat causes that are partially effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three dimensions of 'illa
In Hanafi usul, an 'illa can be considered in name (ism), meaning (ma'na), and ruling (hukm). A cause effective in all three is a complete 'illa; one effective only in name and meaning but not ruling is this lesson's focus.
The passage calls this 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman.
2
Examine the marad al-mawt example
The illness itself is recognized as a cause (asma'an wa ma'nan) for restricting transactions, but the restriction only applies when the illness leads to death (ittiṣāl bi al-mawt). Until death, the cause lacks the description needed for its ruling.
If the patient recovers, the cause never reaches completion; transactions remain fully valid.
3
Compare with the zakat advance payment dispute
The nisab is the original cause for zakat, but the passing of a full lunar year (hawl) is a second description. Hanafis allow advance payment because the nisab is partially effective, attributing the completion back to the beginning. Malik and al-Shafi'i disagree, each with a different view on the completeness of the cause.
The passage contrasts the Hanafi view with Malik (cause incomplete) and al-Shafi'i (cause complete, year is only a term).
4
Synthesize the Hanafi concept
Such an 'illa resembles a sabab because its ruling is deferred to a later description. However, it remains a true cause ( 'illa) in reality, as the description arises from that cause (e.g., the pains of death come from the illness, unlike the year which is extraneous to the nisab).
This is why the passage says marad al-mawt resembles causes more than nisab.

Chapter of Qiyas. The cause and its ruling. After the year completes, similarly illness of death is a cause for change until advance payment is valid, but it is zakat i.e. the advanced zakat, the rulings in name and meaning except that its ruling is established by the description of connection to death, so it resembles causes from this aspect, and it is a cause in reality and this resembles causes more than the nisab. Advance payment: meaning advancing zakat before the completion of the year due to the existence of the original cause after the year, due to the absence of the description of the cause at present. So when the year completes and its nisab is complete, the paid amount is valid for zakat because the description is attributed to the beginning of the year, contrary to Malik. Because the nisab before completion of the year does not have the ruling of a cause in his view, and its being growth (nama') by the year is like the last description of a cause with two descriptions. So advance payment of zakat before the year is not permissible according to him, just as advance payment of expiation before oath-breaking is not permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: the nisab before the year is a complete cause for the obligation of zakat, without any resemblance to causes. And if the description of being yearly was part of the cause, then advance payment before it would not be valid, just as advance payment before nisab is not valid. Rather, the year is merely a term for demanding payment from the owner as a facilitation. In his view, if one pays before the completion of the year, the payment is considered zakat without being suspended on the term, like a debtor who pays a debt before the term. And if the payment is considered zakat, he cannot reclaim it from the poor before the year. It is a cause for changing the rulings related to his wealth, such as the attachment of the heir's right and the restriction of the patient from donating more than one-third. In name: because it is legislated for changing from release to restriction. And in meaning: because it is effective in restricting transactions beyond one-third, as reported in the hadith of Sa'd. And since it is not a cause hukman, he indicated: except that its ruling... meaning the ruling of marad al-mawt, which is restriction on transactions, is only established by illness with the description of its connection to death, like the nisab whose ruling was suspended on the description of growth. When its ruling was deferred to the description of connection, it resembles causes, but in reality it is a cause. The meaning of 'its ruling deferred to the description of connection' is that if a patient gives away all his wealth and hands it over to the donee, it becomes his property immediately, because the cause that prevents transactions—which is marad al-mawt—has not been found with its description, which is connection with death. So if the patient dies thereafter, the cause is completed with its description and what exceeds one-third is reclaimed, and this description is attributed to the beginning of the illness. If the description is attributed to the beginning of the illness, its ruling is attributed, which is restriction, so it becomes as if the transaction occurred after restriction. And if he recovers from the illness, his transaction is effective, because the cause was not completed with its description. 'Resembles causes' etc. means illness resembles causes more than nisab, because the description of connection to which the ruling is deferred arises from the illness, as the pains that lead to death arise from illness, unlike growth, which does not arise from nisab as you know. Since the description of connection is not extraneous because it arises from it, the ruling of illness is not dependent on another matter unlike nisab, so its causality for the ruling is stronger than nisab. This is a fifth example, and some count this example and the following example: buying a relative as an example of the cause that is in the realm of causes, i.e., a cause resembling a cause. And Fakhr al-Islam made the resembling cause=
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage defines a category of 'illa (cause) in Hanafi usul: an 'illa that is 'asman wa ma'nan' (in name and meaning) but not 'hukman' (in ruling). The example given is marad al-mawt (mortal illness). The illness itself is recognized as a cause ( 'illa) for preventing certain transactions, but its legal effect (hukm) only materializes when the additional description of being connected to death (ittiṣāl bi al-mawt) occurs. Thus it resembles a sabab (a cause in the sense of a condition or instrument) rather than a full, immediate 'illa. The passage uses the analogy of zakat: the nisab (minimum wealth) is the original cause for zakat, but the description of the year (hawl) must also be present for the obligation to be due. Hanafi scholars allow advancing zakat before the year because the nisab is partially effective, unlike Malik who requires both descriptions. Al-Shafi'i differs, viewing the nisab alone as a complete cause and the year as merely a term. The passage then elaborates on marad al-mawt: if a sick person gives away all his wealth, it is effective immediately because the 'illa lacks the description of death; but if he dies, the description is retroactively attached, restricting the gift. This shows the cause is not fully effective until the description attaches, making it similar to a sabab. Fakhr al-Islam classified this as a 'mutashābiha' (resembling) cause.

Key Terms
العلة (al-‘illa): A cause that brings about a legal ruling; in this passage, an 'illa may be incomplete (in need of a description) to produce its ruling.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A mortal illness that, when connected to death, imposes restrictions on financial transactions.
التعجيل (al-ta‘jīl): Advance payment of an obligation before its time, e.g., paying zakat before the end of the lunar year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is advance payment of zakat before the end of the lunar year valid?
A) Because the year is not a part of the cause but a term for convenience.
B) Because the nisab is the complete cause and the year is irrelevant.
C) Because the nisab is the original cause and the description of growth (nama') during the year is treated as the last part of a cause with two descriptions, so the ruling is attributed back to the beginning upon completion.
D) Because the hadith allows it absolutely.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an 'illa can be effective in name and meaning without immediate legal effect; its ruling is deferred to an additional description, making it resemble a sabab.

The Rule of Two Effective Descriptions in 'Illa Classification
Explains the rule of two effective descriptions in 'illa classification, with the example of purchasing a relative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the later of two effective descriptions is the cause hukman to identify the effective cause in a legal scenario.

Core Idea
When a ruling depends on two effective descriptions, the later one is the cause in legal effect.

In this passage, the Hanafi usul text explores a subtle classification of the 'illa (cause) by examining the example of purchasing a relative. It introduces the rule that when two effective descriptions are present, the one occurring later is considered the effective cause ( 'illa hukman). Understanding this rule is key to correctly identifying the causative factor in complex legal situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two descriptions in the example
In the example of purchasing a relative, two descriptions are said to be effective: kinship (qarābah) and ownership (milk). Both are given as causes for emancipation.
The passage explicitly mentions 'two effective descriptions' (wasfayn mu'aththirayn) as kinship and ownership.
2
Determine which description occurs last
Consider the sequence: a person has a relative (kinship exists first), then purchases them (ownership occurs later). Thus ownership is the later description in existence.
The rule applies regardless of which description is first; the later one is the cause hukman.
3
Apply the rule: the later description is the 'illa hukman
According to the passage, when a ruling depends on two effective descriptions, the later one in existence is the cause hukman (the effective cause for the ruling). Therefore, ownership is the 'illa hukman for emancipation.
The passage states: 'If a ruling depends on two effective descriptions, the later one in existence is the cause hukman.'
4
Classify the example according to the threefold division of 'illa
The passage clarifies that the purchase example is 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan wa hukman (in name, meaning, and ruling), not merely a cause resembling a cause. The purchase is a cause of the cause (through ownership), but it still qualifies as a full cause in all three senses.
This classification distinguishes it from other examples where the 'illa is only in name and meaning.

بالسبب قسماً آخر سوى الأقسام السبعة، فبين تلك العلة وبين العلة اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً عموم من وجه؛ لصدقهما في الأمثلة السابقة، وصدق الأول فقط في شراء القريب، وصدق الثاني فقط في البيع الموقوف، فعلى هذا شراء القريب ليس من أمثلة العلة اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً، بل هو علة اسماً ومعنى وحكماً. الملك: لأن الشرى يوجب الملك والملك في القريب يوجب العتق؛ لقوله عليه: "من ملك ذا عتق عليه"، [الترمذي رقم: ١٣٦٥]، فيكون العتق مضافاً إلى أوّله بواسطته، فمن حيث إنه علة العلة فكان علة، ومن حيث توسطه بينهما الواسطة يشبه السبب كالرمي: فإنه علة للقتل ولكن له شبه بالسبب، من حيث إن القتل بالرمي إنما يتوقف على نفوذ السهم ومضيّه في الهواء حتى لا يجب القصاص بمجرد الرمي، ولما كانت هذه الوسائط من موجبات الرمي كان الرمي علة لا سببا كالشراء للعتق اعلم أن المصنّف له لم يصرح في هذا المثال أنه علة اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً كما صرّح في غيره وإن أدرجه تحت أمثلة هذا القسم، ويفهم من هذا أن هذا المثال ليس علة اسماً ومعنى لا حكماً، وأن المصنف اختار مذهب فخر الإسلام له وجعل العلة المتشابهة بالسبب قسماً آخر، وأورده بعد العلة اسماً ومعنى لا حكما، وأما مثال العلة معنى وحكماً لا اسماً فما بينه المصنف الله بقوله: وإذا تعلق إلخ بوصفين مؤثرين كالقرابة والملك للعتق واحترز بقوله: "مؤثرين" عما إذا كان أحدهما مؤثراً في الحكم دون الآخر، فإنه حينئذ العلة هو المؤثر والآخر شرط.
لأنه مؤثر فيه: يعني الوصف الأخير من هذين الوصفين المؤثرين علة حكما؛ لوجود الحكم عنده، والوصف الأول وإن كان موجوداً ولكن الحكم لا يضاف إليه بل يضاف إلى الوصف الأخير؛ لرجحان الوصف الأخير على الأول بسبب وجود الحكم عند وجوده فإن الحكم إذا وجد بوجود الوصف الأخير ولم يوجد بالأول لكان الوصف الأخير راجحا عليه، فإذا كان راجحا يضاف الحكم إليه، فكأن الوصف الأول معدوم، وهو علة أيضاً، فإن المؤثر في الحكم هو الوصف الأخير، وأما الوصف الأول فهو يكون علة معنى لا اسماً ولا حكماً،

وذلك كالقرابة والملك، فإن المجموع منهما علة للعتق ولكن المؤثر هو الوصف الأخير منهما أيهما كان، فإن كان الملك أخيراً بأن اشترى عبداً قريباً ومحرماً منه فالملك حينئذ علة للعتق حكماً؛ لوجود العتق عنده ومعنى؛

And similarly, purchasing a relative is a cause for emancipation, but through an intermediate that is among the requirements of purchase, which is ownership. So it was a cause resembling a cause, like throwing (an arrow). And if a ruling depends on two effective descriptions, the later one in existence is the cause hukman, because the ruling is attributed to it due to its preponderance over the first by existence in its presence and meaning, because it is effective in it. ... So on this, purchasing a relative is not from the examples of 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman, but rather it is 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan wa hukman. Ownership: because purchase necessitates ownership, and ownership of a relative necessitates emancipation due to his statement: 'Whoever owns a relative, he is set free.' [Tirmidhi no. 1365]. So emancipation is attributed to its first cause through the intermediate. So in terms of being the cause of the cause, it is a cause. And in terms of the intermediate between them, it resembles a cause like throwing: for it is a cause of killing but has resemblance to a cause, in that killing by throwing depends on the arrow's penetration and travel in the air until retaliation is not obligatory by mere throwing. And since these intermediates are among the requirements of throwing, throwing is a cause not a cause (i.e., not a sabab) like purchase for emancipation. Know that the author did not explicitly state in this example that it is 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman as he stated in others, and he included it under the examples of this section. From this it is understood that this example is not 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman, but rather 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan wa hukman. ... And as for the example of 'illa ma'nan wa hukman la sman, the author clarified by his saying: 'And if a ruling depends on two effective descriptions...' such as kinship and ownership for emancipation. And he guarded by saying 'effective' in case one of them is effective in the ruling and the other not. Then in that case the effective one is the cause and the other is a condition. 'Because it is effective in it' means the later of the two effective descriptions is the cause hukman due to the existence of the ruling with it, and the first description even though existent, the ruling is not attributed to it but to the later description, due to the preponderance of the later description over the first because of the existence of the ruling with it. If the ruling is found with the existence of the later description and not with the first, then the later description is preponderant over it. So if it is preponderant, the ruling is attributed to it, making the first description as if non-existent. And it is also a cause, but the effective in the ruling is the later description. As for the first description, it is a cause in meaning not in name or ruling. Meaning: and that is like kinship and ownership, for the combination of the two is a cause for emancipation, but the effective is the later of the two, whichever it is. If ownership is later, such as buying a relative who is mahram, then ownership is the cause for emancipation hukman, because emancipation occurs with it and meaning; =
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage discusses another type of 'illa in Hanafi usul: the example of purchasing a relative (shirā' al-qarīb) as a cause for emancipation ( 'itq). The purchase itself is not the direct cause; it causes ownership (milk), and ownership of a relative is what directly triggers emancipation, based on the hadith 'Whoever owns a relative, he is set free.' Thus the purchase is a cause of the cause, making it resemble a sabab (like throwing an arrow that causes death after the arrow travels). The passage then introduces a rule: when a ruling depends on two effective descriptions (wasfayn mu'aththirayn), the later one in existence is considered the 'illa hukman (the effective cause for the ruling). The earlier description is a cause in meaning (ma'nan) but not in name or ruling. For example, kinship (qarābah) and ownership (milk) together cause emancipation, but the effective one is whichever occurs last. If a person buys a relative, ownership is the later description, so it is the 'illa hukman. The author (al-Marghinani? Fakhr al-Islam?) is shown to have adopted Fakhr al-Islam's view, making the 'illa that resembles a sabab a separate category. The passage clarifies that the purchase example is not of the 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman type, but rather asma'an wa ma'nan wa hukman (in name, meaning, and ruling). This is a nuanced classification: the earlier description (kinship) is a cause in meaning but not the direct effective cause, while the later (ownership) is the effective one in name and ruling.

Key Terms
شراء القريب (shirā' al-qarīb): The act of purchasing a relative within the prohibited degrees (mahram).
وصف مؤثر (wasf mu'aththir): A description that has an effective influence on the ruling; in this context, both kinship and ownership are effective, but the later one is the direct cause.
علة حكماً ('illa hukman): The cause to which the ruling is attributed in the sense of being the effective reason, as opposed to a cause in name or meaning only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the purchase of a relative is considered a cause ('illa) for emancipation. What is its specific classification?
A) 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan la hukman
B) 'illa asma'an wa ma'nan wa hukman
C) 'illa ma'nan wa hukman la sman
D) Sabab (cause in the strict sense)

Key Takeaway
The later of two effective descriptions is the cause hukman; this rule is illustrated by the example of purchasing a relative, where ownership is the later description and the direct cause of emancipation.

Tripartite Classification of 'Illa: Name, Meaning, and Ruling
Classifying 'illa into categories by name, meaning, and ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an 'illa according to its name, meaning, and ruling, and apply the Hanafi tripartite distinction to examples such as purchase of a relative and travel for license.

Core Idea
A cause may be effective in name, meaning, and ruling, or only in some; the law attaches rulings based on the interplay of these three aspects.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the 'illa (effective cause) is not a monolithic concept. Classical scholars analyze it from three perspectives: what it is called (ism), what it actually does (ma'na), and what the law attaches to it (hukm). This lesson unpacks these categories using the commentary's examples, including the purchase of a relative, the co-existence of two effective descriptions, and the distinction between 'illa and sabab. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for mastering qiyas and distinguishing strong from weak causes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tripartite classification
Identify the three aspects of 'illa: ism (name), ma'na (meaning/effectiveness), and hukm (ruling/legal attachment). Recognize that a cause may be present in one, two, or all three aspects.
The author uses examples to show which combinations exist: e.g., purchase of a relative is a cause in all three.
2
Analyze the example of purchase of a relative
Trace how the purchase leads to emancipation through an intermediary (ownership). The purchase is a cause in name and meaning because ownership is effective, and it is a cause in ruling because emancipation is attributed to it.
The intermediary makes it resemble a sabab (reason), but it remains an 'illa.
3
Examine two effective descriptions
When two descriptions (e.g., kinship and ownership) are both effective, the later one in existence becomes the cause in ruling, while the earlier one may be a cause in meaning only.
The ruling is attributed to the last description due to preponderance by existence.
4
Apply the concept of shubha al-illa to riba
Understand that riba al-nasi'ah is prohibited by one descriptor (genus or quantity) alone because it has a semblance (shubha) of the true cause (both descriptors). This shows how a weaker cause can establish a weaker ruling.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the weak is established by the weak.
5
Distinguish 'illa from sabab via iqamah al-shay' maqam ghayrihi
Travel is a cause for license in name and ruling, but the effective meaning is hardship. The law places travel in the position of hardship for ease of application. This is an example where 'illa exists in name and ruling but not meaning.
This illustrates the separation between the nominal cause and the true effective cause.
